Qualifications of a Judge and Ijtihad as a Condition of Priority
Commentary on the conditions for appointing a judge and mufti, emphasizing necessity of ijtihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qualifications for a judge and explain why ijtihad is a condition of priority, not an absolute requirement.

Core Idea
The most deserving judge must possess trustworthiness, knowledge, and ijtihad, but ijtihad is a condition of priority, not absolute necessity.

Choosing a judge is one of the most critical decisions a ruler makes. The Hanafi school, as elaborated in the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, lays out clear qualifications that ensure justice. At the heart of this discussion is the role of ijtihad: is it an absolute requirement or a preference? The answer shapes how we understand judicial appointments in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Dissect the matn's list of qualifications
Identify each term in the matn: chastity (ʿiffah), intellect (ʿaql), righteousness (ṣalāḥ), understanding (fahm), knowledge of Sunnah and traditions, and aspects of fiqh and ijtihad. Understand their legal significance as conditions for the judge's appointment.
The list shows that the judge must be both morally upright and possess deep legal knowledge.
2
Trace the dalil for appointing the most deserving
Locate the hadith: 'Whoever appoints a person while there is among his subjects one more deserving has betrayed Allah, His Messenger, and the Muslims.' Analyze how this proof establishes the obligation to appoint the best candidate.
The phrase 'one more deserving' (man huwa awlā) is key to understanding the prioritization.
3
Distinguish between conditions of validity and conditions of priority
The passage explicitly says 'Ijtihad is a condition of priority' (wa al-ijtihād sharṭ al-awlawiyyah). Compare this to an absolute condition (sharṭ al-ṣiḥḥah). Understand the practical difference: a judge may be validly appointed without ijtihad if the most deserving candidate lacks it, but the ruler is blameworthy if he overlooks a more qualified person.
This distinction is central to Hanafi methodology and differs from other schools.
4
Apply to the mufti and note flexibility
The commentary extends similar qualifications to the mufti but notes that a mufti can be a slave, woman, blind, or mute and that his gestures are valid. This shows that the mufti's role has different requirements than a witness, being akin to a narrator.
This flexibility reflects the Hanafi focus on functional competence over formal status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القضاء
يكون موثوقاً به في عفافه وعقله وصلاحه وفهمه وعلمه بالسنة والآثار ووجوه الفقه والاجتهاد
:
عليه الغفلة والسهو لأن اشتراط العدالة يغني عنهما. وفي شرح الروض: وينبغي للإمام أن يسأل أهل العلم المشهورين في عصره عمن يصلح للفتوى ليمنع من لا يصلح ويتوعده بالعقوبة بالعود وليكن المفتي متنزهاً عن خوارم المروءة، فقيه النفس، سليم الذهن. حسن التصرف والاستنباط، ولو كان المفتي عبداً أو امرأة أو أعمى أو أخرس بالإشارة وليس هو كالشاهد في رد فتواه لقرابة وجر نفع ودفع ضر وعداوة فهو كالراوي لا كالشاهد وتقبل فتوى من لا يكفر ولا يفسق ببدعة كشهادته ا هـ . وفي تلقيح المحبوبي أن الإشارة من المفتي الناطق يعمل بها فلا يختص بالأخرس. وفي القنية رامز العين الأئمة المكي: أشار المفتي برأسه مكان قوله نعم فللمستفتي أن يعمل به ورمز للنوازل عن أبي القاسم مثله، ورمز لظهير الدين المرغيناني لا لأن إشارة الناطق لا تعتبر اهـ. وسيأتي أنه ينبغي أن يكون المفتي كالقاضي في أوصاف الكمال. وفي الظهيرية ولا بأس للقاضي أن يفتي من لم يخاصم إليه ولا يفتي أحد الخصمين فيما خوصم إليه ا هـ قوله : (ولا ينبغي أن يكون القاضي فظا غليظاً جباراً عنيداً) لأن المقصود منه وهو إيصال الحقوق إلى أهلها لا يحصل به وفي المصباح : رجل فظ شدید غليظ القلب يقال منه فظ يفظ من باب تعب فظاظة إذا غلظ حتى يهاب في غير موضعه، وغلظ الرجل اشتد فهو غليظ وفيه غلظة أي غير لين ولا سلس، وأغلظ له في القول إغلاظاً عنفه ا هـ . والجبار في الخلق الحامل غيره على الشيء قهراً وغلبة وفي أسمائه تعالى الذي جبر خلقه على ما أراد من أمره ونهيه والعنيد من عاند فلان عناداً من باب قاتل إذا ركب الخلاف والعصيان وعانده معاندة عارضه وفعل مثل فعله قال الأزهري : المعاند المعارض بالخلاف لا بالوفاق وقد يكون مباراة بغير خلاف ا.هـ. وفسره في المغرب بمن يظهر له الحق فيأباه . وذكر مسكين أن الفظ هو الجافي سيئ الخلق والغليظ قاسي القلب، والجبار من جبره على الأمر بمعنى أجبره أي لا يجبر غيره على ما لا يريد والعنيد المعاند المجانب للحق المعادي لأهله.
والآثار
ووجوه
.
قوله: (وينبغي أن يكون موثوقاً به في عفافه وعقله وصلاحه وفهمه وعلمه بالسنة الفقه) ويكون شديداً من غير عنف، ليناً من غير ضعف، لأن القضاء من أهم أمور المسلمين فكل من كان أعرف وأقدر وأوجه وأهيب واصبر على ما يصيبه من الناس كان أولى. وينبغي للسلطان أن يتفحص في ذلك ويولي من هو أولى لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام من قلد إنساناً عملاً وفي رعيته من هو أولى فقد خان الله ورسوله وجماعة المسلمين» والموثوق به من وثقت به أثق بكسرهما ثقة ووثوقاً ائتمنته وهو وهي وهم ثقة لأنه مصدر، وقد يجمع في الذكور والإناث فيقال ثقات والعفاف بالفتح من عف عن الشيء يعف من باب ضرب عفة بالكسر امتنع عنه فهو عفيف؛ كذا في المصباح. وفسره الكرماني شارح البخاري بالكف
عن المحارم وخوارم المروءة والعقل على قول الأكثر كما في التحرير قوة بها إدراك الكليات للنفس ا هـ . . والمراد بالوثوق به في عقله أن يكون كامله فلا يولي الأحمق وهو ناقص العقل. في المستظرف : الحمق الخفة غريزة لا تنفع فيها الحيلة وهي داء دواؤه الموت وفي الحديث الأحمق أبغض الخلق إلى الله تعالى» إذ حرمه أعز الأشياء عليه وهو العقل. ويستدل على صفته من حيث الصورة بطول اللحية لأن مخرجها من الدماغ فمن أفرط طول لحيته قل دماغه، ومن قل دماغه قل عقله، ومن قل عقله فهو أخف. وأما صفته من حيث الأفعال فترك نظره في العواقب، وثقته بمن لا يعرفه والعجب وكثرة الكلام وسرعة الجواب وكثرة الالتفات والخلو من العلم والعجلة والخفة والسفه والظلم والغفلة والسهو والخيلاء، إن استغنى بطر، وإن افتقر قنط، وإن قال فحش وإن سئل بخل، وإن سأل ألح، وإن قال لم يحسن، وإن قيل له لم يفقه وإن ضحك قهقه، وإن بكى صرخ. وإذا اعتبرنا هذه الخصال وجدناها في كثير من الناس فلا يكاد يعرف العاقل من الأحمق قال عيسى عليه السلام: عالجت الأكمه والأبرص فأبرأتهما وعالجت الأحمق فلم يبرأ ا وأما الصلاح فهو لغة خلاف الفساد كما في المصباح، وذكر الكرماني أنه لفظ جامع لكل خير ولذا وصف الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام نبينا و به ليلة الإسراء فقال كل من لقيه في السموات مرحباً . بالنبي الصالح، ولو كان هناك وصف أجمع منه للخير لوصفوه به اهـ. وفي أوقاف الخصاف : الصالح من كان مستوراً ليس بمهتوك ولا صاحب ريبة، وكان مستقيم الطريقة، سليم الناحية، كامن الأذى، قليل السوء، ليس بمعاقر للنبيذ ولا ينادم عليه الرجال، وليس بقذاف للمحصنات ولا معروفاً بالكذب، فهذا عندنا من أهل الصلاح ا هـ . والفهم لغة كما في المصباح العلم والعنف عدم الرفق والضعف العجز عن احتمال الشيء. وفي فتح القدير قبيل الحبس : ويستحب أن يكون في القاضي عبسة بلا غضب وأن يلتزم التواضع من غير وهن ولا ضعف والمراد بعلم السنة ما ثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قولاً وفعلاً وتقريراً عند أمر يعاينه والمراد بوجوه الفقه طرقه وقدمنا تعريفه أول الكتاب. وذكر مسكين هنا أن الفقه عند عامة العلماء اسم لعلم خاص في الدين لا لكل علم وهو العلم بالمعاني التي تعلقت بها الأحكام من كتاب وسنة وإجماع ومقتضياتها وإشاراتها .
قوله: (والاجتهاد شرط الأولوية وهو لغة بذل الطاقة في تحصيل ذي كلفة، واصطلاحاً ذلك من الفقه في تحصيل حكم شرعي ظني كما في التحرير. واختلفوا في المجتهد فقيل أن يعلم الكتاب بمعانيه والسنة بطرقها والمراد بعلمهما علم ما يتعلق به الأحكام منهما من العام والخاص والمشترك والمؤوّل والنص والظاهر والناسخ والمنسوخ ومعرفة الاجماع والقياس، ولا يشترط حفظه لجميع القرآن ولا لبعضه عن ظهر القلب بل
Book of Judging. He should be trustworthy in his chastity, intellect, righteousness, understanding, knowledge of the Sunnah and traditions, and aspects of fiqh and ijtihad. Negligence and forgetfulness are waived because the condition of uprightness suffices for them. In Sharh al-Rawd: The imam should ask the well-known scholars of his time about who is fit for fatwa to prevent the unfit and threaten them with punishment upon return. The mufti should be free from violations of manliness, jurist in spirit, sound-minded, good in action and deduction. Even if the mufti is a slave, woman, blind, or mute by pointing, he is not like the witness in rejection of his fatwa due to kinship, benefit, harm, or enmity; he is like a narrator, not like a witness. The fatwa of one who does not disbelieve or become sinful by innovation is accepted like his testimony. In Talqih al-Mahbubi: The gesture of a speaking mufti is acted upon, so it is not specific to the mute. In al-Qunyah: Ramiz al-Ayn al-A'imma al-Makki: If the mufti gestured with his head instead of saying yes, the seeker may act upon it. Similarly, he gestured for nawazil from Abu al-Qasim, and gestured for Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani: No, because the gesture of a speaking person is not considered. It will come that the mufti should be like the judge in attributes of perfection. In al-Zahiriyyah: It is no problem for a judge to give fatwa to one who has not litigated with him, but he should not give fatwa to one of the two litigants in what is litigated before him. His statement: (The judge should not be harsh, rough, tyrannical, stubborn) because the intended purpose, which is delivering rights to their owners, is not achieved by that. In al-Misbah: A harsh man, severe, rough-hearted. Al-Jabbar in creation is one who compels others by force and domination. In His names, the Exalted, it is He who compelled His creation to what He willed of His command and prohibition. Al-Anid is one who stubbornly opposes, goes against, and disobeys. Al-Azhari said: The stubborn one opposes in disagreement, not agreement. In al-Mughrib: One to whom the truth appears but he rejects it. Maskin mentioned: Al-Fazz is the coarse ill-tempered, al-Ghaliz is the hard-hearted, al-Jabbar is one who compels others to what they do not want, al-Anid is the obstinate one who avoids truth and is hostile to its people. His statement: (He should be trustworthy in his chastity, intellect, righteousness, understanding, knowledge of the Sunnah and fiqh) and be firm without violence, gentle without weakness, because judging is among the most important affairs of Muslims. Whoever is more knowledgeable, capable, dignified, awe-inspiring, and patient with what befalls him from people is more deserving. The ruler should investigate that and appoint whoever is more deserving, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever appoints a person to a post while there is among his subjects one more deserving has betrayed Allah, His Messenger, and the Muslims.' The trustworthy: one whom you trust... Chastity: refraining from things. Al-Kirmani interpreted it as refraining from prohibitions and violations of manliness. Intellect: according to most, as in al-Tahrir, a power by which the soul perceives universals. The meaning of trusting in his intellect is that it is complete; he should not appoint the foolish one, who has deficient intellect. In al-Mustazraf: Foolishness is lightness of disposition, a disease whose cure is death. In the hadith: 'The fool is the most hated of creation to Allah' as He deprived him of the most precious thing to Him, which is intellect. His attribute is inferred from form by the length of the beard, because its origin is from the brain; if his beard is excessively long, his brain is little; if his brain is little, his intellect is little; if his intellect is little, he is lighter. As for his attribute in terms of actions: neglecting consideration of consequences, trusting one he does not know, self-admiration, excessive speech, quickness of answer, frequent turning, lack of knowledge, haste, frivolity, foolishness, injustice, negligence, forgetfulness, and vanity. If he becomes rich, he is arrogant; if poor, he despairs; if he speaks, he uses obscenity; if asked, he is miserly; if he asks, he is insistent; if he says something, he does not do it well; if something is said to him, he does not understand; if he laughs, he guffaws; if he cries, he screams. If we consider these traits, we find them in many people, so hardly can the intelligent be known from the foolish. Jesus, peace be upon him, said: 'I treated the blind and the leper and cured them, but I treated the fool and could not cure him.' Righteousness: linguistically the opposite of corruption. Al-Kirmani said it is a comprehensive word for all good. In Awqaf al-Khassaf: The righteous one is he who is concealed, not exposed, nor suspect; he is of straight path, sound side, hidden harm, little evil, not a drinker of nabidh, not a companion of men, not a slanderer, not known for lying. This is, in our view, the people of righteousness. Understanding: linguistically knowledge. Harshness: lack of gentleness. Weakness: inability to bear something. In Fath al-Qadir: It is recommended that the judge have frowning without anger and maintain humility without weakness. The meaning of knowledge of the Sunnah is what is established from the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, in word, deed, or approval regarding a matter he witnessed. The meaning of aspects of fiqh is its paths; we have already given its definition at the beginning of the book. Maskin mentioned that fiqh, according to the general scholars, is a name for a specific knowledge in religion, not every knowledge; it is knowledge of the meanings related to rulings from the Book, Sunnah, consensus, and their implications and indications. His statement: (Ijtihad is a condition of priority. It is linguistically the exertion of effort in obtaining something burdensome. Technically, it is the exertion of effort by the jurist in obtaining a probable legal ruling, as in al-Tahrir. They differed regarding the mujtahid: it is said he must know the Book with its meanings and the Sunnah with its chains. The meaning of knowing both is knowing what pertains to rulings from them of general and specific, shared and interpretable, text and apparent, abrogating and abrogated, and knowledge of consensus and analogy. He is not required to memorize all of the Quran or part of it by heart, rather...
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa’iq regarding the qualifications of a judge (qadi) and, by extension, a mufti. The author begins by quoting the matn: 'He should be trustworthy in his chastity, intellect, righteousness, understanding, knowledge of the Sunnah and traditions, and aspects of fiqh and ijtihad.' The commentary then explains each term. It notes that the conditions of justice (ʿadālah) suffice to cover abstinence from negligence and forgetfulness. A section from Sharh al-Rawd provides details on how a ruler should select a mufti: the mufti must be free from violations of manliness (murūʾah), be a jurist in spirit, sound-minded, and skilled in deduction. Importantly, the mufti can be a slave, woman, blind, or mute, and his gestures (ishārah) are valid. His fatwa is not rejected for kinship, benefit, harm, or enmity; he is like a narrator (rāwi), not a witness. The text then addresses the judge: he should not be harsh (fazz), rough (ghalīẓ), tyrannical (jabbār), or stubborn (ʿanīd). These traits prevent the delivery of rights. Each term is defined linguistically. The commentary returns to the matn: 'He should be trustworthy in his chastity, intellect, righteousness, understanding, knowledge of the Sunnah and fiqh.' It emphasizes that the judge should be firm but not violent, gentle but not weak. The ruler must appoint the most deserving person, based on the hadith: 'Whoever appoints a person while there is among the subjects one more deserving has betrayed Allah, His Messenger, and the Muslims.' The commentary then elaborates on intellect (ʿaql): it must be complete; the judge must not be a fool (ahmaq). Foolishness is a disease of character. Signs of foolishness include excessive trust, hasty answers, lack of knowledge, etc. Righteousness (ṣalāḥ) is defined as refraining from prohibitions and being a person of integrity. Understanding (fahm) is knowledge, and harshness (ʿunf) is lack of gentleness. The passage concludes with a statement on ijtihad as a condition of priority (sharṭ al-awlawiyyah). Ijtihad is defined technically as the exertion of effort to reach a probable legal ruling. The mujtahid must know the Book and Sunnah with their relevant aspects (general, specific, abrogating, etc.), and must know consensus and analogy. He need not memorize the entire Quran; rather, he must know the verses related to rulings. This passage provides a comprehensive view of the Hanafi requirements for judicial and iftā’ authority.

Key Terms
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Linguistically: exertion of effort in a burdensome task. Technically: the exertion of effort by a jurist to derive a probable legal ruling (ḥukm sharʿī ẓannī), as defined in al-Tahrir.
العدالة (al-ʿadālah): Uprightness; the condition that suffices to cover negligence and forgetfulness. The judge must be ʿādil (upright).
المروءة (al-murūʾah): Manliness; the quality of being free from all actions that lower one's dignity. The mufti must be free from violations of murūʾah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the status of ijtihad for a judge?
A) It is an absolute requirement without which the appointment is invalid.
B) It is a condition of priority (sharṭ al-awlawiyyah); the most deserving judge should have it.
C) It is recommended but not necessary.
D) It is only required for the mufti, not the judge.

Key Takeaway
Ijtihad is a condition of priority for a judge, meaning the most deserving candidate should have it, but it is not an absolute requirement for the validity of the appointment.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling on Appointing a Judge and the Condition of Intellect
Defines the ruling on appointing a judge and the condition of intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on appointing a judge who fears injustice and identify the characteristics of a fool (ahmaq) that disqualify him from judgeship.

Core Idea
A judge must be fully intelligent; appointing a fool is disliked and invalid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies one of the fundamental conditions of a judge: complete intellect. It begins with the ruling on appointing a judge who fears injustice, then defines foolishness and its signs to ensure only qualified persons are appointed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Locate the opening statement: 'kurihat al-taqild li-man khafa al-hayf'. This declares that appointing a judge who fears injustice is disliked (makruh tanzih).
If he is secure from injustice, there is no dislike.
2
Understand the Condition of Trust in Intellect
The text states that trust in intellect requires the judge to be intellectually complete. A fool (ahmaq) is deficient and must not be appointed.
The term 'وثوق به في عقله' means confidence in his intellect.
3
Define the Fool (Ahmaq)
Foolishness is defined as a natural lightness (khiffa) that cannot be cured by trickery. It is a disease whose cure is death. A hadith calls the fool the most detested of creation.
The fool is deprived of the most precious thing: intellect.
4
Recognize the Signs of a Fool
The text lists physical signs (excessively long beard) and behavioral signs (abandoning consequences, trusting strangers, arrogance, excessive speech, quick answers, etc.).
These signs help identify a fool in practice.
5
Practical Implication
If a judge candidate exhibits these foolish traits, his appointment is invalid (or at least disliked). The condition of intellect ensures sound judgment.
The prophet Jesus said treating a fool is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرط الأولوية والمفتي ينبغي أن يكون هكذا وكره التقليد لمن خاف الحيف وإن أمنه لا ولا عن المحارم وخوارم المروءة والعقل على قول الأكثر كما في التحرير قوة بها إدراك الكليات للنفس ا هـ . . والمراد بالوثوق به في عقله أن يكون كامله فلا يولي الأحمق وهو ناقص العقل. في المستظرف : الحمق الخفة غريزة لا تنفع فيها الحيلة وهي داء دواؤه الموت وفي الحديث الأحمق أبغض الخلق إلى الله تعالى» إذ حرمه أعز الأشياء عليه وهو العقل. ويستدل على صفته من حيث الصورة بطول اللحية لأن مخرجها من الدماغ فمن أفرط طول لحيته قل دماغه، ومن قل دماغه قل عقله، ومن قل عقله فهو أخف. وأما صفته من حيث الأفعال فترك نظره في العواقب، وثقته بمن لا يعرفه والعجب وكثرة الكلام وسرعة الجواب وكثرة الالتفات والخلو من العلم والعجلة والخفة والسفه والظلم والغفلة والسهو والخيلاء، إن استغنى بطر، وإن افتقر قنط، وإن قال فحش وإن سئل بخل، وإن سأل ألح، وإن قال لم يحسن، وإن قيل له لم يفقه وإن ضحك قهقه، وإن بكى صرخ. وإذا اعتبرنا هذه الخصال وجدناها في كثير من الناس فلا يكاد يعرف العاقل من الأحمق قال عيسى عليه السلام: عالجت الأكمه والأبرص فأبرأتهما وعالجت الأحمق فلم يبرأ ا وأما الصلاح فهو لغة خلاف الفساد كما في المصباح، وذكر الكرماني أنه لفظ جامع لكل خير ولذا وصف الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام نبينا و به ليلة الإسراء فقال كل من لقيه في السموات مرحباً . بالنبي الصالح، ولو كان هناك وصف أجمع منه للخير لوصفوه به اهـ. وفي أوقاف الخصاف : الصالح من كان مستوراً ليس بمهتوك ولا صاحب ريبة، وكان مستقيم الطريقة، سليم الناحية، كامن الأذى، قليل السوء، ليس بمعاقر للنبيذ ولا ينادم عليه الرجال، وليس بقذاف للمحصنات ولا معروفاً بالكذب، فهذا عندنا من أهل الصلاح ا هـ . والفهم لغة كما في المصباح العلم والعنف عدم الرفق والضعف العجز عن احتمال الشيء. وفي فتح القدير قبيل الحبس : ويستحب أن يكون في القاضي عبسة بلا غضب وأن يلتزم التواضع من غير وهن ولا ضعف والمراد بعلم السنة ما ثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قولاً وفعلاً وتقريراً عند أمر يعاينه والمراد بوجوه الفقه طرقه وقدمنا تعريفه أول الكتاب.
Condition of priority and the mufti should be like this, and it is disliked to appoint one who fears injustice, and if he is secure from it, there is no dislike. Regarding the meaning of trust in his intellect: that he be complete, so the fool is not appointed, for he is deficient in intellect. In al-Mustazraf: Foolishness is lightness, a disposition that cannot be remedied by trickery; it is a disease whose cure is death. In the hadith: 'The fool is the most detested of creation to Allah Almighty', because He has deprived him of the most precious thing to Him, which is intellect. Evidence of his condition from form: long beard, because its origin is from the brain; whoever's beard is excessively long, his brain is small; whoever's brain is small, his intellect is small; whoever's intellect is small, he is lighter. As for his condition from actions: abandoning consideration of consequences, trusting one he does not know, arrogance, excessive speech, quickness of response, frequent turning away, emptiness from knowledge, haste, lightness, foolishness, injustice, heedlessness, forgetfulness, and vanity. If he becomes wealthy, he is extravagant; if poor, he despairs; if he speaks, he utters obscenity; if asked, he is stingy; if he asks, he persists; if he says, he does not say well; if told, he does not understand; if he laughs, he guffaws; if he cries, he screams. If we consider these traits, we find them in many people, so the intelligent is hardly known from the fool. Jesus, peace be upon him, said: 'I treated the blind and the leper and cured them, but I treated the fool and could not cure him.' As for righteousness (salah), linguistically it is the opposite of corruption, as in al-Misbah. Al-Kirmani mentioned that it is a comprehensive term for all good, hence the prophets, peace and blessings upon our Prophet, described him on the night of Isra saying everyone he met in the heavens welcomed him as 'the righteous prophet', and if there were a description more comprehensive than that for good, they would have described him with it. In Awqaf al-Khassaf: The righteous person is one who is concealing (his faults), not flagrantly sinful, not suspicious, upright in conduct, sound in character, hidden in harm, little in evil, not a habitual drinker of nabidh, not a drinking companion of men, not a defamer of chaste women, and not known for lying; this is according to us from the people of righteousness. Comprehension (fahm) linguistically, as in al-Misbah, is knowledge, and harshness (anf) is lack of gentleness, and weakness (duf) is inability to bear something. In Fath al-Qadir, near the discussion on detention: It is recommended that the judge have a stern expression without anger, and that he adhere to humility without weakness or feebleness. The meaning of knowledge of the Sunnah is what is established from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in word, deed, and tacit approval regarding an observed matter. The meaning of the aspects of fiqh is its methods, and we have presented its definition at the beginning of the book.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the conditions of a judge. It begins by stating the ruling that it is disliked to appoint a judge who fears injustice, but if he is secure from it, there is no dislike. The commentator then explains the required qualities: trust in intellect, meaning complete intellect, so a fool (ahmaq) should not be appointed. He defines foolishness as a natural lightness incurable by trickery, citing a hadith that the fool is the most detested to Allah. The signs of a fool from appearance (long beard indicating small brain) and actions (list of negative traits) are given. Next, he defines righteousness (salah) linguistically and technically, quoting al-Khassaf that a righteous person is one who conceals his sins, is not flagrant, not suspicious, upright, not a drunkard, etc. Then he defines comprehension (fahm) as knowledge. Finally, he mentions that it is recommended for a judge to have a stern expression without anger and to be humble but not weak. The passage ends by defining knowledge of the Sunnah and the aspects of fiqh.

Key Terms
الأحمق (al-ahmaq): The fool: one deficient in intellect, characterized by lightness and incurable foolishness.
الوثوق به في عقله (al-wuthuq bihi fi aqlihi): Trust in his intellect: meaning the judge must be intellectually complete.
الحيف (al-hayf): Injustice or bias; a judge's fear of committing it leads to dislike of his appointment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a behavioral sign of a fool (ahmaq)?
A) Trusting strangers
B) Excessive speech
C) Patience in adversity
D) Quickness of response

Key Takeaway
Appointing a judge who fears injustice is disliked; a judge must be fully intelligent, and a fool is disqualified.

The Conditions of Righteousness and Understanding for a Judge
Defines two qualities: salah and fahm, and gives practical description and recommendations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define righteousness (salah) and understanding (fahm) as required qualities for a judge according to the Hanafi school, and identify the recommended traits of a judge's demeanor.

Core Idea
A judge must be righteous (salah) and possess understanding (fahm); righteousness means concealing faults and avoiding major sins, and understanding is the ability to comprehend legal issues.

After establishing the condition of intellect, the text defines two more essential qualities for a judge: righteousness (salah) and understanding (fahm). It provides detailed descriptions and includes practical recommendations for the judge's conduct, such as stern expression without anger and humility without weakness.

Guided Path
1
Define Righteousness (Salah) Linguistically
The text says 'salah' is the opposite of corruption (fasad), and is a comprehensive term for all good.
Al-Kirmani mentions that the prophets described our Prophet as 'al-nabi al-salih' to encompass all goodness.
2
Identify the Characteristics of a Righteous Person
From Awqaf al-Khassaf: a righteous person is one who is concealing (not flagrant), not suspicious, upright, sound, hidden in harm, little in evil, not a habitual drinker, not a defamer, not known for lying.
These criteria are for judgeship.
3
Define Understanding (Fahm)
Fahm is knowledge ('ilm) linguistically; it is required for a judge to comprehend legal issues.
The text also mentions harshness (anf) as lack of gentleness and weakness as inability.
4
Note the Recommended Demeanor
From Fath al-Qadir: it is recommended for a judge to have a stern expression without anger, and to adhere to humility without weakness.
This balances authority and approachability.
5
Understand the Overall Requirement
Knowledge of the Sunnah (words, deeds, approvals of the Prophet) and knowledge of the methods of fiqh are also required.
These are summarized at the end.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the conditions of a judge. It begins by stating the ruling that it is disliked to appoint a judge who fears injustice, but if he is secure from it, there is no dislike. الصلاح (al-salah): Righteousness: a comprehensive term for all good, specifically one who conceals faults, is not flagrant, upright, etc.

Qada — Judiciary

Ijtihad as a Condition of Priority for a Judge
Defines ijtihad, conditions of mujtahid, and the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on judge's qualifications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that ijtihad is a condition of priority for a judge, explain why a muqallid can validly serve as judge, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ijtihad is a condition of priority, not validity: a muqallid judge suffices because the goal of qada is delivering rights by acting on a fatwa.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a critical question in Islamic judicial theory: must a judge be a fully qualified mujtahid? The Hanafi school, drawing on the purpose of the judiciary (delivering rights), distinguishes between priority and validity. While a mujtahid is preferred, a muqallid (one who follows a mujtahid's rulings) can be appointed because he can judge by relying on another's fatwa. The commentary defines ijtihad and lists the conditions of a mujtahid, then contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires personal knowledge and capability.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that ijtihad is a condition of priority (shart al-awlawiyya), not a condition of validity. A muqallid can be a judge.
The matn explicitly says 'shart al-awlawiyya' which is key.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a judge must be a mujtahid because the command for qada requires capability, which depends on knowledge.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i's proof: the command to judge implies ability, and ability requires knowing the ruling directly, not through taqlid.
The source mentions 'لا قدرة بدون العلم' (no capability without knowledge).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: capability can be achieved by following a fatwa; the purpose of qada (delivering rights) is met even if the judge does not derive rulings himself.
This relies on the purpose (maqsad) of the judiciary.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi allows muqallid judges; Shafi'i requires mujtahids. This affects who can be appointed as a judge in the community.
The Hanafi position is more flexible, especially important when mujtahids are scarce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والاجتهاد شرط (الأولوية وهو لغة بذل الطاقة في تحصيل ذي كلفة، واصطلاحاً ذلك من الفقه في تحصيل حكم شرعي ظني كما في التحرير. واختلفوا في المجتهد فقيل أن يعلم الكتاب بمعانيه والسنة بطرقها والمراد بعلمهما علم ما يتعلق به الأحكام منهما من العام والخاص والمشترك والمؤوّل والنص والظاهر والناسخ والمنسوخ ومعرفة الاجماع والقياس، ولا يشترط حفظه لجميع القرآن ولا لبعضه عن ظهر القلب بل يكفي أن يعرف مظان أحكامها في أبوابها فيراجعها وقت الحاجة، ولا يشترط التبحر في هذه العلوم، ولا بد له من معرفة لسان العرب لغة واعراباً وأما الاعتقاد فيكفيه اعتقاد جازم، ولا يشترط معرفتها على طريق المتكلمين وأدلتهم لأنها هذه الجملة فهو أهل للاجتهاد فيجب عليه أن يعمل بإجتهاده ولا يقلد أحداً. وقوله «شرط الأولوية» يفيد أن تولية الجاهل صحيحة عندنا لأن المقصود من القضاء وهو إيصال الحق إلى مستحقه يحصل بالعمل بفتوى غيره. وفي البزازية من كتاب الإيمان قبيل الثالث والعشرين : المفتي يفتي بالديانة والقاضي يقضي بالظاهر إلى أن قال : دل أن الجاهل لا يمكنه القضاء بالفتوى أيضاً فلا بد في كون القاضي الحاكم من الدماء والفروج عالماً المراد منه المقلد بقرينة جعل الاجتهاد شرط الأولوية ا وهكذا في إيضاح الاصلاح وجوز في العناية أن يراد بالجاهل المقلد لكونه ذكر في مقابلة المجتهد وأن يراد من لا يحفظ شيئاً من أقوال الفقهاء وهو المناسب لسياق الكلام لقوله في دليل الشافعي: ولا قدرة بدون العلم ولم يقل بدون الاجتهاد ا.هـ. وأما معناه لغة واصطلاحاً فقدمناهما. وأما حكمه فهو غلبة الظن بالحكم مع احتمال الخطأ، ورأيت في حجج الدلائل أن الظن الغالب غير غلبة الظن لتغير الثاني دون الأول، وقد يقال المقلد أيضاً يعمل بفتوى غيره ولو أخذها من الكتب. وحاصل شرائط المجتهد على ما في التلويح والتحرير الإسلام، والبلوغ، والعقل، هـ. : قوله : (وذكر يعقوب باشا) أي في حاشية على صدر الشريعة وعبارته : وعند الشافعي لا يصح تقليد الفاسق والجاهل ودليله على عدم صحة تقليد الجاهل أن الأمر بالقضاء يستدعي القدرة عليه ولا قدرة بدون العلم ودليلنا على صحته أنه يمكنه أن يقضي بفتوى غيره ومقصود القاضي يحصل به وهو إيصال الحق إلى مستحقه ؛ كذا في الهداية ويعلم من هذا الخ. وفي الفواكه البدرية لابن الغرس ما ملخصه : ليس مرادهم بالجاهل العامي المحض بل لا بد من تأهل العلم والفهم وأقله أن
His statement: (And ijtihad is a condition of priority). Ijtihad linguistically is expending effort to obtain something burdensome, and technically it is that from fiqh to obtain a speculative legal ruling, as in al-Tahrir. They differed about the mujtahid: it is said that he must know the Book with its meanings and the Sunnah with its paths, and the meaning of knowing both is knowledge of what pertains to rulings from them: the general, specific, common, interpreted, explicit, apparent, abrogating, and abrogated, and knowledge of consensus and analogy. It is not a condition that he memorize all of the Quran or even part of it by heart, but rather it suffices that he know the loci of their rulings in their chapters so he can refer to them when needed. Immersion in these sciences is not required, but he must know the Arabic language lexically and grammatically. As for belief, a firm belief suffices, and it is not required to know it according to the method of the scholastic theologians and their proofs, because that is their craft. The sayings of the Companions are included in the Sunnah, so he must know them because he might analogize in the presence of a Companion's saying. He must know the custom of the people, which is the meaning of their statement: 'He must be a person of innate ability (qariha).' In al-Qamus: Al-qariha is the first water extracted from a well, and the first of everything, and 'your nature' (minka tab'uka); al-iqtirah is improvising speech and deriving something without hearing, choosing, initiating a thing, and being arbitrary. In Manaqib al-Imam Muhammad by al-Kardari: Muhammad used to go to the dyers and ask about their transactions and what they conducted among themselves, and al-Kisa'i used to visit Muhammad and said to him one day: 'How much you say! And upon this are the meanings of people's speech. What are you? This statement is only known by the experts of this craft.' Whoever masters this summary is qualified for ijtihad, and it is obligatory on him to act by his ijtihad and not to imitate anyone. His statement 'condition of priority' indicates that appointing an ignorant person (jahil) is valid according to us because the purpose of qada, which is delivering the right to its owner, is achieved by acting on the fatwa of someone else. In al-Bazzaziyya from the book of Iman, near the twenty-third: The mufti gives fatwa by religious duty and the judge judges by outward appearance, until he said: This indicates that the ignorant person cannot judge by fatwa either, so the judge ruler concerning blood and private parts must be learned in religion like red sulfur, and where is red sulfur and where is religion and knowledge!? Ya'qub Pasha mentioned, and it is understood from the evidence that by 'ignorant person' is meant one who is unable to take the issues from fiqh books and to record the statements of jurists, as is not hidden, although by it is meant the muqallid, by the context that makes ijtihad a condition of priority. Thus in Idah al-Islah, and it is permitted in al-Inayah that by 'ignorant person' is meant the muqallid because he is mentioned in contrast to the mujtahid, and that it means one who does not preserve any of the statements of jurists, which is appropriate to the context of speech, due to his statement in the proof of al-Shafi'i: 'There is no capability without knowledge,' and he did not say without ijtihad. As for its meaning linguistically and technically, we have presented them. As for its legal effect, it is preponderance of speculation (ghalabat al-zann) regarding the ruling with the possibility of error. I saw in Hujaj al-Dala'il that predominant speculation (al-zann al-ghalib) is different from ghalabat al-zann because the second changes without the first. It may be said the muqallid also acts on the fatwa of others even if he takes it from books. The summary of the conditions of the mujtahid according to al-Talwih and al-Tahrir: Islam, puberty, and intellect. His statement: (And Ya'qub Pasha mentioned) i.e. in his gloss on Sadr al-Shari'a, and his statement: According to al-Shafi'i, it is not valid to follow (taqlid) a sinner or an ignorant person, and his proof for the invalidity of following an ignorant person is that the command for qada requires capability for it, and there is no capability without knowledge. Our proof for its validity is that he can judge by the fatwa of someone else, and the purpose of the judge is achieved by it, which is delivering the right to its owner; thus in al-Hidayah, and it is known from this etc. In al-Fawakih al-Badriyya by Ibn al-Ghars, its summary: They do not mean by 'ignorant person' the pure layperson, but rather he must be qualified with knowledge and understanding, and the least of that is...
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the condition of ijtihad for a judge. It begins by defining ijtihad: linguistically, expending effort; technically, deriving a speculative legal ruling from fiqh. The commentator then lists the conditions of a mujtahid: knowledge of the Quran and Sunnah in terms of general, specific, abrogating, etc., knowledge of consensus and analogy, Arabic language, knowledge of Companion sayings, and knowledge of custom (urf). It is not required to memorize the entire Quran, nor to be an expert in scholastic theology. The passage cites the story of Imam Muhammad consulting dyers to learn about transactions, indicating the importance of knowing people's customs. The key point is that ijtihad is a condition of priority (shart al-awlawiyya), not of validity. Thus it is valid to appoint a judge who is not a mujtahid but follows (yuqallid) a mujtahid, because the purpose of qada (delivering rights) can be achieved through another's fatwa. The passage then discusses the dispute with al-Shafi'i, who holds that a judge must have knowledge to be capable, so a muqallid or ignorant person cannot be a judge. The Hanafi response: capability can be obtained by following a fatwa, so a muqallid can judge. The passage clarifies that by 'ignorant' (jahil) is meant one who cannot extract rulings from books or preserve jurists' statements, not the absolute layperson. The judge must have some qualification (tahassul) in knowledge and understanding, but not necessarily ijtihad. Finally, the conditions of a mujtahid are summarized as Islam, puberty, and intellect.

Key Terms
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Expending effort in fiqh to derive a speculative legal ruling.
الجاهل (al-jahil): One who cannot extract rulings from fiqh books or cannot preserve jurists' statements; here used for a muqallid.
الشريحة (al-qariha): Innate ability or natural talent; a mujtahid must be a person of qariha, meaning he understands people's customs and can derive rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why can a judge who is a muqallid (follower) be appointed?
A) Because he is more knowledgeable than a mujtahid
B) Because the purpose of qada is achieved by following a fatwa
C) Because ijtihad is impossible to attain
D) Because the Shafi'i school also allows it

Key Takeaway
Ijtihad is a condition of priority (shart al-awlawiyya), not validity, allowing a muqallid judge to serve by acting on another's fatwa.

The Judge's Qualifications: Ijtihad is a Condition of Priority, Not Validity
Explains that a judge may be a muqallid; ijtihad is only a condition of priority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the judge's qualifications and explain why ijtihad is a condition of priority, not validity.

Core Idea
A judge in the Hanafi school may be a muqallid; ijtihad is preferred but not required for valid judgment.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the qualifications of a judge in the Hanafi school. A common misconception is that a judge must be a mujtahid across all Islamic schools. However, the Hanafi school holds that ijtihad is only a condition of priority (shart al-awlawiyya), meaning it is better but not essential for the validity of the judge's appointment. Let's explore the reasoning behind this position and the counterargument from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Determine the exact ruling being discussed: the validity of appointing a non-mujtahid (muqallid) as a judge.
2
State the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi school rules that the appointment is valid. Ijtihad is a condition of priority, not validity.
3
Locate the Dalil
The proof is istihsan: the purpose of qada (delivering rights) can be achieved by the judge acting on the fatwa of a mujtahid.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school requires the judge to be a mujtahid, arguing that the command to judge requires ability (knowledge), which implies ijtihad.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response refines the Shafi'i proof: ability can be achieved through reliance on a fatwa; the text says 'without knowledge,' not 'without ijtihad.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القضاء يكتفي أن يعرف مظان أحكامها في أبوابها فيراجعها وقت الحاجة، ولا يشترط التبحر في هذه العلوم، ولا بد له من معرفة لسان العرب لغة واعراباً وأما الاعتقاد فيكفيه اعتقاد جازم، ولا يشترط معرفتها على طريق المتكلمين وأدلتهم لأنها صناعة لهم. ويدخل في السنة أقوال الصحابة فلا بد من معرفتها لأنه قد يقيس مع وجود قول الصحابي : ولا بد له من معرفة عرف الناس وهو معنى قولهم لا بد أن يكون صاحب قريحة. وفي القاموس : والقريحة أول ماء يستنبط من القرح كالبئر وأول كل شيء ومنك طبعك والاقتراح ارتجال الكلام واستنباط الشيء من غير سماع والاجتباء والاختيار وابتداع الشيء والتحكم ا هـ. وفي مناقب الإمام محمد للكردري : كان محمد يذهب إلى الصباغين ويسأل عن معاملاتهم وما يديرونها فيما بينهما، وكان الكسائي يختلف إلى محمد فقال له يوماً ما أكثر ما تقولون وعلى هذا معاني كلم الناس ما أنتم وهذا القول لا يعرفه إلا الحذاق من أهل هذه الصناعة، فمن أتقن هذه الجملة فهو أهل للاجتهاد فيجب عليه أن يعمل بإجتهاده ولا يقلد أحداً. وقوله «شرط الأولوية» يفيد أن تولية الجاهل صحيحة عندنا لأن المقصود من القضاء وهو إيصال الحق إلى مستحقه يحصل بالعمل بفتوى غيره. وفي البزازية من كتاب الإيمان قبيل الثالث والعشرين : المفتي يفتي بالديانة والقاضي يقضي بالظاهر إلى أن قال : دل أن الجاهل لا يمكنه القضاء بالفتوى أيضاً فلا بد في كون القاضي الحاكم من الدماء والفروج عالماً ديناً كالكبريت الأحمر وأين الكبريت الأحمر وأين الدين والعلم!؟ ا هـ . وذكر يعقوب باشا ويعلم من الدليل أن المراد من الجاهل من لا يقدر على أخذ المسائل من كتب الفقه وضبط أقوال الفقهاء كما لا يخفى مع أن المراد منه المقلد بقرينة جعل الاجتهاد شرط الأولوية ا وهكذا في إيضاح الاصلاح وجوز في العناية أن يراد بالجاهل المقلد لكونه ذكر في مقابلة المجتهد وأن يراد يراد من لا يحفظ شيئاً من أقوال الفقهاء وهو المناسب لسياق الكلام لقوله في دليل الشافعي: ولا قدرة بدون العلم ولم يقل بدون الاجتهاد ا.هـ.
It is sufficient for him to know the places of its rulings in their chapters so that he can refer to them when needed, and deep immersion in these sciences is not required. He must have knowledge of the Arabic language, both lexicon and grammar. As for belief, a firm belief suffices, and it is not required to know it according to the way of the theologians and their proofs, because that is a craft of theirs. Included in the Sunnah are the sayings of the Companions, so he must know them, because he might make analogical reasoning when a Companion's saying exists. He must know the custom of the people, and this is the meaning of their statement: he must be a person of qariha. In al-Qamus: al-qariha is the first water extracted from a well, and the beginning of everything, and from it is your nature, and al-irtijal is improvisation, and istinbat is deriving something without hearing, and al-ijtiba' is selection, and ibtida' is innovation, and al-tahakkum is arbitrary judgment, etc. In Manaqib al-Imam Muhammad by al-Kardari: Muhammad used to go to the dyers and ask about their transactions and how they conducted them among themselves, and al-Kisa'i used to visit Muhammad and said to him one day: 'How much you speak! And on this, the meanings of people's words, what are you? This statement is only known by the skilled people of this craft.' So whoever masters these matters is qualified for ijtihad, and he must act according to his ijtihad and not imitate anyone. And his saying 'a condition of priority' indicates that appointing an ignorant person is valid in our view, because the purpose of judgment, which is to deliver rights to their claimants, is achieved by acting on the fatwa of someone else. In al-Bazzaziyya from the Book of Iman, just before the twenty-third: 'The mufti gives fatwa according to conscience, and the judge judges according to outward appearance...' until he said: 'This indicates that the ignorant person cannot judge by fatwa either, so it is necessary that the judge in matters of blood and private parts be knowledgeable in religion, like red sulfur. But where is red sulfur and where is religion and knowledge!?' Then it was mentioned by Ya'qub Pasha: It is understood from the proof that what is meant by 'jahil' is one who is unable to derive rulings from books of fiqh and to memorize the statements of jurists, as is clear, and that what is meant is the muqallid, as indicated by making ijtihad a condition of priority. And this is also in Idah al-Islah, and it is allowed in al-Inayah that 'jahil' could refer to the muqallid because it is mentioned in contrast to the mujtahid, and it could refer to one who does not remember any of the statements of the jurists, which is appropriate for the context of the speech, because in the proof of al-Shafi'i: 'There is no ability without knowledge,' and he did not say without ijtihad.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the qualifications of a judge (qadi). The author explains that a judge need not be a mujtahid in the absolute sense; rather, it suffices that he knows where to find rulings (mazann al-ahkam) in the books of fiqh, understands Arabic, and has a firm belief (i'tiqad). The Hanafi school differs from the Shafi'i school here: ijtihad is considered a condition of priority (shart al-awlawiyya), not a condition of validity. Thus, appointing a judge who is not a mujtahid (a muqallid) is valid. The author supports this with a rational argument: the purpose of qada is to deliver rights to their claimants, and this can be achieved by the judge acting on the fatwa of a mujtahid. The marginal note by Ya'qub Pasha clarifies that by 'jahil' (ignorant) the text does not mean a total layperson, but rather a muqallid who can access and understand the books. The Shafi'i objection that a judge must have knowledge (ability to ijtihad) is rebutted by noting that the text of the proof says 'no ability without knowledge,' not 'no ability without ijtihad.'

Key Terms
شرط الأولوية (shart al-awlawiyya): A condition of priority or preference, meaning that ijtihad is better but not essential for validity.
جاهل (jahil): In this context, a muqallid who cannot derive rulings independently but can access books and follow a mujtahid.
مظان الأحكام (mazann al-ahkam): The places or chapters in fiqh books where specific rulings are found.
قريحة (qariha): Natural intelligence and ability to derive rulings; innate sharpness of mind.
مقلد (muqallid): One who follows the ruling of a mujtahid without independent derivation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is valid; ijtihad is a condition of priority, not validity.
D) It is only valid in cases of necessity.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a judge need not be a mujtahid; ijtihad is a condition of priority, not validity, so the appointment of a muqallid judge is valid.

Conditions of a Mujtahid and Definition of Ijtihad
Definition and conditions of ijtihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the 14 conditions of a mujtahid and define ijtihad as ghalabat al-zann with its distinction from al-zann al-ghalib.

Core Idea
Ijtihad is reaching a preponderant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) on a legal ruling, requiring 14 conditions but not kalam or all fiqh details.

Ijtihad is the engine of Islamic jurisprudence—the process through which a qualified scholar derives rulings from the sources. In this passage, the Hanafi school defines ijtihad as probable opinion and sets fourteen conditions for the mujtahid. Understanding these conditions is essential for distinguishing valid scholarly authority from mere opinion.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish meanings of ijtihad
Separate the lexical meaning from the technical meaning. The passage notes both have been presented earlier, so focus on the technical ruling: ghalabat al-zann.
Remember: technical ijtihad produces probable opinion, not certainty.
2
Understand the hukm of ijtihad
The hukm (ruling) is ghalabat al-zann—a preponderant opinion that allows for error. Note the subtle difference from al-zann al-ghalib: the latter is static, while ghalabat al-zann may shift.
This distinction is from Hujaj al-Dala'il.
3
Enumerate the 14 conditions
List the conditions as given: Islam, puberty, intellect, faqih al-nafs, knowledge of Arabic (morphology, syntax, rhetoric, usul), knowledge of Quranic rulings, knowledge of hadith (text, chain, abrogation), knowledge of qiyas (subsumed under usul), knowledge of ijma and its contexts, knowledge of customs. Note that kalam, detailed fiqh, masculinity, freedom, and 'adalah are not required.
Total is fourteen; count them carefully.
4
Identify what is not required
Explicitly note: theology (kalam) after sound creed, details of fiqh (tafari'), masculinity, freedom, and uprightness ('adalah) are not conditions. A fasiq can perform ijtihad for himself.
This distinguishes Hanafi from some other schools.
5
Recognize the rukn of ijtihad
The rukn (pillar) consists of the mujtahid (the person) and the mujtahad fihi (the subject matter — a probable shar'i ruling with evidence).
This frames ijtihad as an act with two essential components.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما معناه لغة واصطلاحاً فقدمناهما. وأما حكمه فهو غلبة الظن بالحكم مع احتمال الخطأ، ورأيت في حجج الدلائل أن الظن الغالب غير غلبة الظن لتغير الثاني دون الأول، وقد يقال المقلد أيضاً يعمل بفتوى غيره ولو أخذها من الكتب. وحاصل شرائط المجتهد على ما في التلويح والتحرير الإسلام، والبلوغ، والعقل، وكونه فقيه النفس بمعنى شديد الفهم بالطبع، وعلمه باللغة والعربية أي الصرف والنحو والمعاني والبيان والأصول، وكونه حاوياً بالعلم كتاب الله تعالى مما يتعلق بالأحكام، وكونه عالماً بالحديث متناً وسنداً وناسخاً ومنسوخاً، ولا يشترط فيه بعد صحة العقيدة علم الكلام ولا تفاريع الفقه ولا الذكورة والحرية ولا العدالة فللفاسق الاجتهاد ليعمل بنفسه وأما غيره فلا يعمل به. ويشترط كونه عالماً بوجوه القياس وفي الحقيقة اشتراط علمه بالأصول يغني عنه، ولا بد من معرفة الإجماع ومواقعه ومن معرفة عادات الناس، فالحاصل أن الشرائط أربعة عشر شرطاً. وأما ركنه فالمجتهد وهو ما قدمناه والمجتهد فيه وهو حكم شرعي ظني عليه دليل.
As for its meaning lexically and technically, we have already presented them. As for its ruling (hukm), it is the preponderance of opinion (ghalabat al-zann) regarding the ruling with the possibility of error. I saw in Hujaj al-Dala'il that 'al-zann al-ghalib' is different from 'ghalabat al-zann' because the second changes while the first does not. It may be said that the muqallid also acts on the fatwa of someone else even if he takes it from books. The summary of the conditions of a mujtahid according to al-Talwih and al-Tahrir: Islam, puberty, intellect, being a faqih al-nafs meaning having a strong natural understanding, knowledge of the language and Arabic (i.e., morphology, syntax, rhetoric, and usul), having comprehensive knowledge of the Book of Allah regarding rulings, being knowledgeable in hadith in terms of text, chain, abrogating, and abrogated. Knowledge of theology (kalam) is not required after sound creed, nor details of fiqh, nor masculinity and freedom, nor uprightness (adalah); thus a fasiq can perform ijtihad for himself but others cannot act on it. He must be knowledgeable in the ways of qiyas; in fact, the condition of knowledge of usul suffices. He must know ijmā' and its occurrences, and he must know the customs of people. Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage defines ijtihad and enumerates the conditions set for a mujtahid. The author clarifies that ijtihad is the process of reaching a preponderant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) about a legal ruling, with the awareness that error is possible. He notes a distinction between 'al-zann al-ghalib' and 'ghalabat al-zann' from Hujaj al-Dala'il: the former refers to a high probability that remains stable, while the latter may change. The conditions for a mujtahid, drawn from al-Talwih and al-Tahrir, are listed: Islam, puberty, intellect, natural comprehension (faqih al-nafs), knowledge of Arabic language and grammar, knowledge of Quranic verses related to rulings, knowledge of hadith texts and chains, and abrogation. Notably, theology (kalam) after sound belief is not required, nor is knowledge of all branches of fiqh, nor masculinity, freedom, or even uprightness (adalah), meaning a fasiq (sinner) can perform ijtihad for himself, but others cannot rely on it. The condition of knowing qiyas is subsumed under usul. Also required is knowledge of ijmā' and its contexts, and of people's customs. The total is fourteen conditions. The ru kn of ijtihad is the mujtahid and the subject matter (mujtahad fihi) which is a probable shar'i ruling supported by evidence.

Key Terms
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Preponderance of opinion that a ruling is correct, with allowance for error.
فقيه النفس (faqih al-nafs): A natural ability to understand and derive rulings quickly.
شرائط المجتهد (shara'it al-mujtahid): The 14 conditions that qualify a person for ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ijtihad is a probable opinion (ghalabat al-zann) and requires 14 conditions, but not kalam or detailed fiqh.

The Mufti Must Be a Mujtahid; Non-Mujtahids Are Only Transmitters
States that a mufti must be a mujtahid; defines non-mujtahid's role as transmitter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement that a mufti must be a mujtahid, and describe the obligations of a non-mujtahid when asked a question, including the proper method of transmission.

Core Idea
A mufti must be a mujtahid; a non-mujtahid can only transmit a mujtahid's ruling, not issue fatwa.

This lesson explores a foundational principle for issuing fatwa in the Hanafi tradition: the mufti must be a mujtahid. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, expanding on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, clarifies that what we often call 'fatwa' in our time is actually a transmission of earlier rulings. Non-mujtahids are transmitters, and they must follow strict guidelines to ensure the reliability of what they convey. We will walk through the ruling, its proof, and the practical consequences for those who perform this role today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its authority
Locate the statement that the mufti must be a mujtahid. Note that the text cites Fath al-Qadir and the consensus of the usuliyun as the basis. This establishes the authority for the ruling.
The ruling is derived by analogy with the judge (qadi), as both positions require ijtihad.
2
Distinguish between mufti and narrator
Understand that a non-mujtahid who knows the rulings is not a mufti; he is a narrator (hikaya). His duty is to transmit the exact words of the mujtahid, not to assert them as his own.
3
Examine the conditions for reliable transmission
The text outlines two acceptable ways to transmit: a direct chain of transmission, or reliance on a famous book (like those of Muhammad al-Shaybani) that has circulated widely. Rare books (nawadir) are not sufficient unless cited in standard works.
This parallels the classification of hadith: mutawatir and mashhur are reliable; shadhdh (rare) is not.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf on narrating multiple opinions
The author mentions a disagreement: some say a non-mujtahid must narrate all differing opinions for the mustafti to choose; the author opines that narrating one opinion suffices, since the muqallid may follow any mujtahid.
The author's view is based on practicality – requiring all opinions would be burdensome.
5
Apply the ruling to modern practice
Consider how a mufti today, if not a mujtahid, should phrase his response: he should say 'Abu Hanifa said...' rather than 'The answer is...'. This maintains the distinction between transmission and independent fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والمفتي ينبغي أن يكون هكذا أي موثوقاً به في دينة وعفافه إلى آخره. وأن يكون مجتهداً قال في فتح القدير واعلم أن ما ذكر في القاضي ذكر في المفتي فلا يفتي إلا المجتهد، وقد استقر رأي الأصوليين على أن المفتي هو المجتهد فأما غير المجتهد ممن يحفظ أقوال المجتهد فليس مفتياً، والواجب عليه إذا سئل أن يذكر قول المجتهد كأبي حنيفة على جهة الحكاية فعرف أن ما يكون في زماننا من فتوى الموجودين ليس بفتوى بل هو نقل كلام المفتي ليأخذ به المستفتي وطريق نقله لذلك عن المجتهد أحد أمرين : إما أن يكون له سند فيه أو يأخذه . من کتاب معروف تداولته الأيدي نحو كتب محمد بن الحسن ونحوها من التصانيف المشهورة للمجتهدين لأنه بمنزلة الخبر المتواتر أو المشهور؛ هكذا ذكر الرازي. فعلى هذا لو وجد بعض نسخ النوادر في زماننا لا يحل عز وما فيها إلى محمد ولا إلى أبي يوسف لأنها لم تشتهر في عصرنا في ديارنا ولم تتداول، نعم إذا وجد النقل عن النوادر مثلاً في كتاب مشهور معروف کالهداية والمبسوط كان ذلك تعويلاً على ذلك الكتاب فلو كان حافظاً للأقاويل المختلفة للمجتهدين ولا يعرف الحجة ولا قدرة له على الاجتهاد للترجيح لا يقطع بقول منها يفتي به بل يحكيها للمستفتي فيختار المستفتي ما يقع في قلبه أنه الأصوب؛ ذكر في بعض الجوامع وعندي لا يجب عليه حكاية كلها بل يكفيه أن يحكي قولاً منها فإن المقلد له أن يقلد أي مجتهد شاء، فإذا ذكر أحدها فقلده حصل المقصود نعم لا يقطع عليه فيقول جواب مسألتك كذا بل يقول قال أبو حنيفة حكم هذا كذا، نعم لو حكى الكل فلأخذ بما يقع في قلبه أن أصوب أولى وإلا فالعامي لا عبرة بما يقع في قلبه من صواب الحكم يحسن بعض الحوادث والمسائل الدقيقة وأن يعرف طريق تحصيل الأحكام الشرعية من كتب المذهب وصدور المشايخ وكيفية الإيراد والإصدار في الوقائع مع الدعاوى والحجج ويدل على ذلك قولهم : العالم إذا تعين للقضاء وجب عليه قبوله وإذا تركه أثم وما لم يتعين فالترك أفضل، وإذا كان الجاهل أهلاً للقضاء فمتى يتعين. قال في النهر وأقول : وجود الجاهل لا يمنع من تعينه وذلك أنه إذا لم
His saying: (And the mufti should be like this, i.e., trustworthy in his religion and chastity, etc. And he should be a mujtahid.) He said in Fath al-Qadir: 'Know that what has been mentioned regarding the judge applies to the mufti as well; only a mujtahid may give fatwa. The usuliyun have settled that the mufti is the mujtahid. As for a non-mujtahid who memorizes the statements of a mujtahid, he is not a mufti. His duty when asked is to mention the statement of the mujtahid, like Abu Hanifa, by way of narration. Therefore, what occurs in our time from the fatwa of those present is not a fatwa but rather a transmission of the mufti's words for the mustafti to act upon. His method of transmission from the mujtahid is one of two: either he has a chain of transmission to him, or he takes it from a well-known book that has circulated widely, like the books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and similar famous compilations of the mujtahids, because that is like mutawatir or mashhur reports. Thus, if in our time some copies of al-Nawadir are found, it is not permissible to attribute what is in them to Muhammad or to Abu Yusuf because they are not famous in our time and region and have not circulated. However, if a transmission from al-Nawadir is found in a well-known book like al-Hidayah or al-Mabsut, then that reliance is on that book. If someone memorizes different statements of the mujtahids but does not know the evidence and has no ability for ijtihad to weigh between them, he should not assert a particular opinion to be given as fatwa, but rather should narrate them to the mustafti, who then chooses what he feels in his heart to be more correct. It is mentioned in some compilations, but in my view, he is not required to narrate all of them; it suffices to narrate one opinion, because the muqallid may follow whichever mujtahid he wishes. When he mentions one and the mustafti follows it, the purpose is achieved. However, he should not affirmatively say 'the answer to your question is such,' but rather say 'Abu Hanifa said the ruling on this is such.' If he narrates all, then it is better for the mustafti to take what he feels in his heart to be most correct, but otherwise the layperson's heart-feeling is not reliable. He should be good at handling some incidents and subtle issues, and know the way to derive legal rulings from the books of the madhhab and the statements of the shuyukh, and the method of giving and taking in cases with claims and evidence. This is indicated by their saying: When a scholar is specifically needed for qada, he must accept, otherwise leaving it is better. And if an ignorant person is qualified for qada, then when would it become obligatory? He said in al-Nahr: I say: the existence of an ignorant person does not prevent specificity; because if he does not...
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage discusses the essential qualifications of a mufti. Relying on Fath al-Qadir, it establishes that a mufti must be a mujtahid, just like a judge. Non-mujtahids who memorize the rulings of mujtahids are not true muftis; they are mere narrators of the mujtahid's words. In our time (the mu'allif's time), what is called 'fatwa' is actually a transmission of earlier rulings. The transmission must be based either on a direct chain or on famous books like those of Muhammad al-Shaybani, which are like mutawatir reports. Rare books (nawadir) that have not circulated widely cannot be relied upon unless they are cited in standard works like al-Hidayah or al-Mabsut. If a person knows several opinions of mujtahids but cannot weigh them, he should narrate them all, and the seeker (mustafti) chooses. However, the author opines that it is sufficient to narrate one opinion, as the muqallid can follow any mujtahid. He must not assert an opinion as definitive but should say 'Abu Hanifa said...' The passage concludes with a discussion on the obligation of a qualified scholar to accept the post of qada when he is specifically needed, and that even a 'jahil' (non-mujtahid) may be qualified if the necessary knowledge is present, but that is incomplete.

Key Terms
مفتي (mufti): One who issues fatwa; must be a mujtahid. Non-mujtahids are only transmitters.
حكاية (hikaya): Narration or transmission of a mujtahid's statement without asserting it as one's own fatwa.
نوادر (nawadir): Rare transmissions or books that are not widely circulated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the status of a non-mujtahid who gives fatwa in the Hanafi tradition?
A) He is still a mufti but less knowledgeable.
B) He is not a mufti; he is only a narrator of the mujtahid's words.
C) He can give fatwa but only in his own madhhab.
D) He can give fatwa if he has a chain of transmission.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi tradition, only a mujtahid can be a mufti; non-mujtahids are transmitters and must not assert rulings as their own.

Fourteen Conditions for a Hanafi Qadi
Listing the fourteen conditions for a qadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the fourteen conditions for a Hanafi qadi and distinguish between shurut (conditions) and rukn (pillar) in qada.

Core Idea
A qadi's ruling is valid only if he meets fourteen specific conditions, but he need not be just, free, or male.

In the Hanafi school, the appointment of a judge (qadi) is subject to strict prerequisites. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates fourteen conditions that must be present for the judge's rulings to be valid. It also clarifies what is not required, such as justice ('adalah) or masculinity, and identifies the essential pillar (rukn) of qada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the total number of conditions
The passage concludes with 'fahsil anna al-shara'it arba'ata 'ashar shartan' – the conditions are fourteen. Count them as you read.
Some conditions are grouped, e.g., knowledge of language includes morphology, syntax, etc.
2
List each condition mentioned in the text
The conditions include: faqih al-nafs, knowledge of Arabic (sarf, nahw, ma'ani, bayan), knowledge of Quranic rulings, knowledge of hadith (matn, sanad, nasikh, mansukh), knowledge of qiyas (or usul), knowledge of ijma', and knowledge of people's customs. Also note what is explicitly not required.
The passage states that knowledge of usul subsumes qiyas.
3
Analyze what is NOT required
The text explicitly says that after sound creed, knowledge of kalam, furu', masculinity, freedom, and justice are not required. This is distinctive to the Hanafi school.
A fasiq can practice ijtihad for himself but others cannot act on it.
4
Distinguish shurut from rukn
Shurut are external prerequisites for validity; the rukn (pillar) is the mujtahid and the hukm shari' (the ruling). If the rukn is missing, qada is invalid; if a shart is missing, the ruling is also invalid.
The passage ends by stating the rukn: 'Wa amma ruknuhu fa al-mujtahid wa al-mujtahad fihi'.
5
Compare with other schools
Note that other schools require justice ('adalah) and often gender, but the Hanafi school does not. This affects who can become a qadi.
This difference stems from the Hanafi view of ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكونه فقيه النفس بمعنى شديد الفهم بالطبع، وعلمه باللغة والعربية أي الصرف والنحو والمعاني والبيان والأصول، وكونه حاوياً بالعلم كتاب الله تعالى مما يتعلق بالأحكام، وكونه عالماً بالحديث متناً وسنداً وناسخاً ومنسوخاً، ولا يشترط فيه بعد صحة العقيدة علم الكلام ولا تفاريع الفقه ولا الذكورة والحرية ولا العدالة فللفاسق الاجتهاد ليعمل بنفسه وأما غيره فلا يعمل به. ويشترط كونه عالماً بوجوه القياس وفي الحقيقة اشتراط علمه بالأصول يغني عنه، ولا بد من معرفة الإجماع ومواقعه ومن معرفة عادات الناس، فالحاصل أن الشرائط أربعة عشر شرطاً. وأما ركنه فالمجتهد وهو ما قدمناه والمجتهد فيه وهو حكم شرعي ظني عليه دليل.
And that he is faqih al-nafs, meaning very sharp in understanding by nature, and his knowledge of language and Arabic, i.e., morphology, syntax, semantics, rhetoric, and principles (usul), and that he encompasses knowledge of the Book of Allah, the Exalted, regarding legal rulings, and that he is knowledgeable of hadith, text and chain, abrogating and abrogated. There is no condition after sound creed for knowledge of kalam, nor the branches of fiqh, nor masculinity, nor freedom, nor justice. So the sinful person may exercise ijtihad to act upon it himself, but others do not act upon it. And it is required that he knows the aspects of analogy, and in reality, the condition of knowing usul suffices for it. And knowledge of consensus and its occurrences is indispensable, and knowledge of people's customs. So the result is that the conditions are fourteen conditions. As for its pillar, it is the mujtahid, which we have already mentioned, and the subject of ijtihad, which is a speculative legal ruling supported by evidence.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage enumerates the fourteen conditions for a qadi (judge) according to the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that the judge must be faqih al-nafs, meaning naturally sharp in understanding. He must know the Arabic language including morphology, syntax, rhetoric, and the principles of jurisprudence (usul). He must be well-versed in the Quranic verses pertaining to rulings, and in hadith including text, chain, abrogating and abrogated. Interestingly, it clarifies that after sound creed, knowledge of scholastic theology (kalam), detailed fiqh furu', masculinity, freedom, and even justice ('adalah) are not required; even a sinful person (fasiq) can engage in ijtihad for himself, though others cannot act on his ijtihad. It also requires knowledge of analogical reasoning (qiyas), but says that requiring knowledge of usul covers that. Knowledge of consensus and its points, and knowledge of people's customs are also necessary. The total is fourteen conditions. The rukn (pillar) of qada is the mujtahid himself and the ruling (the object of ijtihad) which is a speculative legal ruling based on evidence.

Key Terms
فقيه النفس (faqih al-nafs): Natural sharpness of understanding in fiqh, a natural aptitude for legal reasoning.
شروط (shurut): Conditions that must be present in the judge for his qada to be valid.
ركن (rukn): The essential component of qada: the mujtahid and the ruling itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is explicitly stated as NOT required for a qadi in the Hanafi school according to this passage?
A) Knowledge of Arabic
B) Justice ('adalah)
C) Knowledge of qiyas
D) Knowledge of hadith

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi qadi must meet fourteen conditions, but the pillar of qada is the mujtahid and the ruling itself, not external qualities like justice or gender.

Qualifications of a Mufti and Rules of Fatwa
Explaining that the mufti must be a mujtahid and non-mujtahid only transmits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that a mufti must be a mujtahid and explain the duty of a non-mujtahid in issuing fatwa.

Core Idea
Only a mujtahid can issue fatwa; non-mujtahids must narrate the mujtahid's words as transmission.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies who qualifies as a mufti in the Hanafi school. It establishes that a true mufti must be a mujtahid, capable of independent reasoning. A non-mujtahid, even if he knows the rulings, is merely a transmitter and must present the mujtahid's sayings without independent fatwa. The ruling is supported by the consensus of usul scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on who can be a mufti
The passage states that only a mujtahid can be a mufti. Recognize that this is the central claim.
This is based on the consensus of usul scholars.
2
Recognize the dalil
The proof cited is the consensus (ijma) of usul scholars, as mentioned by al-Razi. Understand that consensus is a primary source of authority in Hanafi usul.
The passage says 'استقر رأي الأصوليين على أن المفتي هو المجتهد'.
3
Understand the duty of a non-mujtahid
If a person is not a mujtahid, his duty when asked is to narrate the saying of the mujtahid, not to issue his own fatwa. This is a wajib obligation.
He must say 'Abu Hanifa said...' not 'The answer is...'
4
Note the method of transmission
The transmission must be through a reliable chain (sanad) or from well-known, widely circulated books like those of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Rare manuscripts are not acceptable.
This ensures the transmission is trustworthy.
5
Consider the case of multiple opinions
If the transmitter knows multiple conflicting opinions but cannot prefer one, he should narrate them to the questioner, who chooses. It suffices to narrate one, but not to be definitive.
The layperson's heart is not a reliable criterion for correctness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والمفتي ينبغي أن يكون هكذا أي موثوقاً به في دينة وعفافه إلى آخره. وأن يكون مجتهداً قال في فتح القدير واعلم أن ما ذكر في القاضي ذكر في المفتي فلا يفتي إلا المجتهد، وقد استقر رأي الأصوليين على أن المفتي هو المجتهد فأما غير المجتهد ممن يحفظ أقوال المجتهد فليس مفتياً، والواجب عليه إذا سئل أن يذكر قول المجتهد كأبي حنيفة على جهة الحكاية فعرف أن ما يكون في زماننا من فتوى الموجودين ليس بفتوى بل هو نقل كلام المفتي ليأخذ به المستفتي وطريق نقله لذلك عن المجتهد أحد أمرين : إما أن يكون له سند فيه أو يأخذه . من کتاب معروف تداولته الأيدي نحو كتب محمد بن الحسن ونحوها من التصانيف المشهورة للمجتهدين لأنه بمنزلة الخبر المتواتر أو المشهور ؛ هكذا ذكر الرازي. فعلى هذا لو وجد بعض نسخ النوادر في زماننا لا يحل عز وما فيها إلى محمد ولا إلى أبي يوسف لأنها لم تشتهر في عصرنا في ديارنا ولم تتداول، نعم إذا وجد النقل عن النوادر مثلاً في كتاب مشهور معروف کالهداية والمبسوط كان ذلك تعويلاً على ذلك الكتاب فلو كان حافظاً للأقاويل المختلفة للمجتهدين ولا يعرف الحجة ولا قدرة له على الاجتهاد للترجيح لا يقطع بقول منها يفتي به بل يحكيها للمستفتي فيختار المستفتي ما يقع في قلبه أنه الأصوب؛ ذكر في بعض الجوامع وعندي لا يجب عليه حكاية كلها بل يكفيه أن يحكي قولاً منها فإن المقلد له أن يقلد أي مجتهد شاء، فإذا ذكر أحدها فقلده حصل المقصود نعم لا يقطع عليه فيقول جواب مسألتك كذا بل يقول قال أبو حنيفة حكم هذا كذا، نعم لو حكى الكل فلأخذ بما يقع في قلبه أن أصوب أولى وإلا فالعامي لا عبرة بما يقع في قلبه من صواب الحكم
His statement: (The mufti should be like this, i.e., trustworthy in his religion and integrity, etc. And he must be a mujtahid.) He said in Fath al-Qadir: Know that what is mentioned for the judge is mentioned for the mufti, so no one gives fatwa except the mujtahid. And the opinion of the usul scholars has settled that the mufti is the mujtahid. As for the non-mujtahid among those who memorize the sayings of the mujtahid, he is not a mufti, and his duty when asked is to mention the saying of the mujtahid, like Abu Hanifa, by way of narration. So it is known that the fatwa of those present in our time is not a fatwa, but a transmission of the mufti's words for the mustafti to act upon. His method of transmitting that from the mujtahid is one of two things: either he has a chain (sanad) in it, or he takes it from a well-known book that has circulated among people, like the books of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and the like of the famous compilations of the mujtahids, because it is in the position of mutawatir or mashhur report. Thus said al-Razi. Therefore, if some copies of al-Nawadir are found in our time, it is not permissible to attribute what is in them to Muhammad or to Abu Yusuf, because they are not famous in our time in our regions and have not circulated. Yes, if the transmission from al-Nawadir is found, for example, in a well-known famous book like al-Hidayah and al-Mabsut, that reliance is on that book. So if he is a memorizer of the different sayings of the mujtahids but does not know the evidence and has no ability for ijtihad to prefer, he does not definitively say a saying from them by which he gives fatwa, but he narrates them to the mustafti, and the mustafti chooses what falls in his heart as the most correct. It is mentioned in some compilations: In my opinion, it is not necessary for him to narrate all of them; rather, it suffices for him to narrate one saying from them, because the muqallid is allowed to imitate any mujtahid he wishes. So if he mentions one of them and he imitates it, the purpose is achieved. Yes, he should not be definitive, saying 'The answer to your issue is such-and-such,' but rather he says, 'Abu Hanifa said the ruling for this is such-and-such.' Yes, if he narrates all, then it is better for him to take what falls in his heart as most correct; otherwise, the layman's fall of the heart regarding correctness of the ruling is not considered.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage discusses the qualifications of a mufti and the proper method for issuing fatwa. It begins by stating that, just like a qadi, a mufti must be trustworthy in his religion and integrity, and most importantly, he must be a mujtahid. The author of al-Fath al-Qadir notes that the conditions for a qadi also apply to a mufti, and only a mujtahid can issue fatwa. The consensus of usul scholars is that the mufti is the mujtahid. Someone who merely memorizes the sayings of mujtahids without the ability to exercise ijtihad is not a mufti; his duty when asked is to relate the saying of the mujtahid, such as Abu Hanifa, as a narration (hikayah). Therefore, the fatwas given in our time (by non-mujtahids) are not fatwas but mere transmission of the mujtahid's words for the questioner to act upon. The transmitter must have either a direct chain (sanad) to the mujtahid or rely on widely circulated books like those of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and other famous compilations, which are considered like mutawatir or mashhur reports. Hence, if one finds a rare manuscript (nawadir) in our time, it is not permissible to attribute its contents to Muhammad or Abu Yusuf because it is not well-known in our region and era. However, if the rare narration is quoted in a well-known book like al-Hidayah or al-Mabsut, then one can rely on that book. If a person knows multiple conflicting opinions of mujtahids but lacks the ability to weigh evidence and cannot prefer one over another, he should not definitively issue a fatwa based on one opinion but should relate all opinions to the questioner, who then chooses the one that seems most correct to his heart. The commentator notes that it is not necessary to narrate all opinions; it suffices to mention one, because the layperson (muqallid) may follow any mujtahid he wishes. However, the narrator must not say 'the answer to your question is such-and-such' but rather 'Abu Hanifa said the ruling for this is such-and-such.' If he does narrate all, then the layperson should choose the one that seems most correct, but if the layperson does not have the ability to judge correctness, his heart's inclination is not reliable.

Key Terms
مفتي (mufti): A jurist who issues fatwa; in this passage, only a mujtahid qualifies.
حكاية (hikayah): Narration or transmission of the mujtahid's words verbatim, not independent fatwa.
مقلد (muqallid): A layperson who follows a mujtahid; he may choose any mujtahid to follow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what must a non-mujtahid do when asked a legal question?
A) Give his own opinion
B) Cite the Quran and Sunnah directly
C) Narrate the sayings of the mujtahid
D) Refer the questioner to a mujtahid

Key Takeaway
The mufti must be a mujtahid; a non-mujtahid can only transmit the sayings of the mujtahid, not issue independent fatwa.
