The Mustafti: Obligations and Etiquette
Rules for the one seeking fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations and recommended etiquettes of a mustafti (one seeking a fatwa) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Seeking a fatwa requires verifying the mufti's qualifications and repeating the question if the basis is unknown.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the rules for the one who seeks a fatwa (mustafti). It addresses how to choose a mufti, what to do when answers are unclear, and the proper conduct when submitting a question. These rules ensure that the mustafti acts responsibly and respects the fatwa process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mustafti's primary obligation
The text states it is obligatory (wajib) to seek fatwa only from a mufti whose knowledge and uprightness are known. The mustafti must verify this, either by the report of a trustworthy, knowledgeable person or by common knowledge.
The verification is a responsibility of the asker.
2
Determine which mufti to follow when multiple are available
If two qualified muftis differ on a ruling and there is no explicit text, the mustafti must follow the more learned of the two. If he believes one is more learned or more pious, he should prefer the more learned over the more pious.
This principle guides the layperson in case of ikhtilaf.
3
Handle recurrence of a past question
If a non-recurring issue was answered previously, and the same issue arises again, the mustafti must re-ask the question unless he knows the answer was based on a clear text or consensus.
This ensures the fatwa's validity over time.
4
Follow the etiquette of interacting with the mufti
It is recommended but not obligatory to ask another mufti if the asker's heart is not at ease. The mustafti should not ask when the mufti is standing or preoccupied, should not say 'thus I said', and should not demand evidence on the spot. He should write clearly, dot ambiguous words, and ponder the note carefully.
Good adab facilitates accurate fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

استحب سؤال غيره ولا يجب. ويكفي المستفتي بعث رقعة أو رسول ثقة، ومن الأدب أن لا يسأل والمفتي قائم أو مشغول بما يمنع تمام الفكر وأن لا يقول بجوابه هكذا قلت أنا ولا يطالبه بدليل فإن أراده فوقت آخر وليبين للفتوى ليمنع من لا يصلح، وليكن المفتي متنزهاً عن خوارم المروءة فقيه النفس سليم الذهن حسن التصرف ولو عبداً أو امرأة أو أخرس تفهم إشارته، وليس هو كالشاهد في رد فتواه لقرابة وجر نفع وتقبل فتوى لا يكفر، ولا يفسق ببدعة كشهادته ويفتي ولو كان قاضياً وفي اشتراط معرفة الحساب لتصحيح مسائله وجهان ويشترط أن يحفظ مذهب إمامه ويعرف قواعده وأساليبه. وليس المبتدأ والخبر نعت لمجتهد . قوله : ( ويكره أن يقتصر على ما فيه (قولان أي على قوله في الجواب فيه قولان . للأصولي الماهر وكذا البحاث في الخلاف من أئمة الفقه وفحول المناظرين أن يفتي في الفروع الشرعية، ولا يجب افتاء فيما لا يقع. ويحرم التساهل في الفتوى واتباع الحيل إن فسدت الأغراض وسؤال من عرف لذلك، ولا يفتي في حال تغير أخلاقه خروجه عن الاعتدال ولو لفرح، ومدافعة أخبثين، فإن أفتى معتقداً أن ذلك لم يمنعه عن درك الصواب صحت فتواه وإن خاطر والأولى أن يتبرع بالفتوى فإن أخذ رزقاً من بيت المال جاز إلا إن تعينت عليه وله كفاية. ولا يأخذ أجرة من مستفت فإن جعل له أهل البلد رزقاً جاز وإن استؤجر جاز والأولى كونها بأجرة مثل كتبه مع كراهة وله قبول هدية لا رشوة على الوجهين كالقولين لكن لا عبرة بالمتأخر إلا إذا وقعا من شخص، فإن اختلفوا في الأرجح ولم يكن أهلاً للترجيح اعتمد ما صححه الأكثر والأعلم وإلا توقف. والعمل بالجديد من قولي الشافعي إلا في نحو ثلاثين مسألة. وإن كان في الرقعة مسائل رتب الأجوبة على ترتيبها، ويكره أن يقتصر على «فيه قولان إذ لا يفيد ولا يطلق حيث التفصيل فهو خطأ، ويجيب على ما في الرقعة لا على ما يعلمه فإن أرادء قال إن أراد كذا فجوابه كذا، ويجيب الأول في الناحية اليسرى وإن شاء غيرها لا قبل البسملة، وليكتب الحمد الله وليختم بقوله والله أعلم . ولا يقبح أن يقول في الجواب عندنا وإن تعلقت بالسلطان دعا له فقال وعلى السلطان سدده الله أو شد إزاره، ويكره أطال الله بقاءه. ويختصر جوابه ويوضح عبارته. وإن سئل عن تكلم بكفر متأول قال : يسئل إن أراد كذا فلا شيء عليه، وإن أراد كذا فيستتاب فإن تاب قبلت توبته وإلا قتل. وإن سئل عمن قتل أو جرح احتاط وذكر شروط القصاص ويبين قدر التعزير ويكتب على الملصق من الورقة وإن ضاقت كتب في الظهر والحاشية أولى لا ورقة أخرى. ويشافهه بما عليه بل إن اقتضاهما السؤال لم يقتصر على أحدهما، ولا يلقنه على خصمه فإن وجب الافتاء قدم السابق بفتوى ثم أقرع، نعم يجب تقديم نساء ومسافرين تهيؤوا أو تضرروا بالتخلف إلا إن ظهر تضرر غيرهم بكثرتهم. وإن سئل عن الإخوة فصل في جوابه ابن الأبوين أو لأب أو لأم، وإن كان في الفريضة عول قال الثمن عائلاً وإن كان في الورثة من يسقط بحال دون حال بينه. ويكتب تحت الفتوى الصحيحة إن عرف أنها لأهل الجواب صحيح ونحوه وله أن يجيب إن رأى ذلك ويختصر وإن جهل حاله يبحث عن حاله، فإن لم يظهر له فله أمره بإبدالها، فإن تعسر أجاب بلسانه .
Chapter on the one seeking fatwa: He must seek from one whose knowledge and integrity are known, even by report of a trustworthy knowledgeable person or by common knowledge; otherwise he investigates. If his inner integrity is hidden, apparent integrity suffices. He acts upon the fatwa of a scholar even if a more learned one exists ignorantly; if they differ and there is no text, he gives precedence to the more learned. Likewise if he believes one is more learned or more pious, he gives precedence to the more learned over the more pious. If he was answered in a non-recurring case and then it occurs again, he must repeat the question unless he knows the answer is based on a text or consensus. If his soul is not at ease with the mufti's answer, it is recommended to ask another, not obligatory. It suffices for the mustafti to send a note or a trustworthy messenger. It is etiquette that he does not ask while the mufti is standing or preoccupied, and does not say about his answer 'Thus I said', nor demand evidence; if he wants it, then at another time. He should clarify the question, dot ambiguous words in the note, ponder it especially its end, be deliberate, and speed with accuracy does not harm. He may consult those present who are qualified, and may correct an obvious error. He should fill margins so nothing can be inserted, make his writing clear between two lines. There is no harm in writing the evidence but not the question. He should not write on the back of a sheet, but may strike out if safe from fitna even if the owner is displeased; and he forbids the mustafti from that. The note is not his property. The leader should search for qualified scholars to prevent the unqualified. The mufti should be free from vulgarity, have a fiqh-oriented mind, sound intellect, good conduct, even if a slave, woman, or mute whose signs are understood. He is not like a witness in that his fatwa is rejected due to kinship or benefit; the fatwa of someone who does not become an unbeliever or sinner by bid'ah is accepted, like testimony. He may give fatwa even if he is a judge. Regarding the condition of knowing calculation for correcting his cases, there are two views. It is conditional that he memorizes his imam's madhhab and knows its principles and methods. The subject and predicate are not descriptive of a mujtahid. He said: (It is disliked to restrict to 'there are two sayings'), meaning he says in the answer 'in it there are two sayings'. For the skilled usul scholar and also the researcher in disagreement among the imams of fiqh and great dialecticians, he may give fatwa on legal branches. Giving fatwa on what does not occur is not obligatory. Carelessness in fatwa and following legal ruses if they corrupt purposes is forbidden, as is asking someone known for that. He does not give fatwa when his character changes, when he is not in equilibrium, even due to joy, or while repelling two najas. If he gives fatwa believing that does not prevent him from reaching correctness, his fatwa is valid though he takes a risk. It is better that he gives fatwa voluntarily. If he takes a stipend from the treasury, it is permissible unless it is obligatory upon him and he has sufficiency. He does not take a fee from the mustafti. If the townspeople set a stipend for him, it is permissible. If he is hired, it is permissible, but it is better to have it as compensation for his books with dislike. He may accept a gift but not a bribe for the fatwa he desires. The leader should assign for a teacher and a mufti his sufficiency. Every town's people have their own expression, so it is not permissible to give fatwa to a people regarding wording without knowing their terminology. He should not act or give fatwa by one of two sayings or two ways without reliance. Regarding the two sayings: he acts by the later if he knows it, otherwise by the one preferred by al-Shafi'i (?), otherwise he must investigate. If he is qualified, he engages in it, learning from the principles and sources; otherwise he learns from transmitters of the madhhab. If there is no tarjih, he pauses. The ruling of the two ways is like the two sayings, but the later is not considered unless both come from one person. If they differ on the more preponderant and he is not qualified for tarjih, he relies on what the majority and the most learned have corrected, otherwise he pauses. Action is on the new of al-Shafi'i's two sayings except in about thirty issues. If there are multiple questions in the note, he orders answers accordingly. It is disliked to restrict to 'there are two sayings' as it is not beneficial and he does not say it where detail is needed, it is wrong. He answers based on what is in the note, not on what he knows. If he intends, he says: if he means such and such, then the answer is such. He writes the answer first on the left side, and if he wishes otherwise, not before the basmala. He writes 'al-hamdu lillah' and ends with 'wa Allahu a'lam'. It is not ugly to say in the answer 'with us' and if it relates to the sultan, he prays for him saying 'and upon the sultan, may Allah guide him or strengthen his reign' and it is disliked to say 'may Allah prolong his life'. He shortens his answer and clarifies his expression. If asked about someone who said words of disbelief with interpretation, he says: he is asked; if he meant such and such, then nothing upon him; if he meant such and such, he is asked to repent; if he repents, his repentance is accepted; otherwise killed. If asked about someone who killed or wounded, he is careful and mentions the conditions of qisas and explains the amount of ta'zir. He writes on the attached part of the paper, and if it is narrow, he writes on the back or margin preferably, not on another sheet. He informs him orally what is upon him; if the question requires both, he does not restrict to one. He does not coach him against his opponent. If giving fatwa becomes obligatory, he gives precedence to the earlier one with a fatwa, then draws lots. Yes, he must give precedence to women and travelers who have prepared or are harmed by delay, unless harm to others appears due to their large number. If asked about siblings, he details in his answer half-brothers by father or mother. If in the estate there is 'awl, he says 'the one-eighth is awl', and if among the heirs there is someone who is excluded in some states, he clarifies. He writes under the correct fatwa, if he knows it is for the people of the answer, 'correct' and similar. He may answer if he sees that, and shorten. If he is unaware of the questioner's condition, he investigates. If it does not become clear to him, he may order him to replace it; if that is difficult, he answers orally.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This is a comprehensive chapter on the mustafti (one seeking a fatwa) and the mufti. The first part details the obligations and etiquettes of the questioner: he must ensure the mufti is knowledgeable and upright, even if he only knows of his apparent integrity. If two muftis differ, the more knowledgeable is followed. If the same issue arises again after a previous fatwa, the question must be repeated unless the answer was based on clear text or consensus. It is recommended but not obligatory to ask another if unsatisfied. The mustafti may send a written note or a messenger; there are rules for writing the note clearly. The second part focuses on the mufti: he must be of upright character and competent, even if a slave, woman, or mute (with understood signs). His fatwa is not rejected due to kinship or benefit. He must know the madhhab's principles. It is disliked to say 'there are two sayings' without clarification. He should not take a fee but may accept a stipend or gift (not bribe). When there are multiple valid positions, he must know the preferred view (the later one if known, or the one favored by al-Shafi'i if no Hanafi tarjih is available—this is striking and may indicate a cross-madhhab borrowing in textual transmission). The mufti must order his answers, avoid abbreviations like 'there are two sayings', and write clearly. Special cases: asked about someone who spoke kufr with interpretation, he must differentiate; asked about qisas or ta'zir, he details conditions. He gives precedence to earlier claimants, but women and travelers may be prioritized. For inheritance, he specifies brother types and handles 'awl. Finally, he may verify the questioner's condition and require a rewrite if necessary.

Key Terms
مستفتي (mustafti): One who seeks a fatwa from a qualified scholar.
عدالة (adalah): Integrity, uprightness; required in a mufti and also considered in the mustafti's verification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it recommended but not obligatory for the mustafti to seek another mufti's opinion?
A) When the first mufti is less learned.
B) When his soul is not at ease with the first answer.
C) When the first mufti is a woman.
D) When the issue is about divorce.

Key Takeaway
The mustafti must verify the mufti's qualifications and may need to re-ask when the basis of a fatwa is unknown.

Qada — Judiciary

The Mufti: Qualifications, Etiquette, and Response
Regulations for mufti conduct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the qualifications required of a mufti and apply the rules of fatwa-writing etiquette according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A mufti must be scholarly, upright, and mindful of adab; his fatwa must be clear, based on his madhhab, and free from bias.

The latter part of this chapter from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq focuses on the mufti himself—his qualifications, ethical conduct, and the proper method of delivering a fatwa. From the imam's duty to appoint qualified muftis to the minutiae of writing a response, this passage equips the student with the full Hanafi framework for ifta.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufti's essential qualifications
The mufti must be free from vulgarity, have a fiqh-oriented mind, sound intellect, and good conduct. Even slaves, women, and mutes (with understood signs) can serve as muftis if qualified. He must memorize his imam's madhhab and know its principles and methods.
These conditions ensure the mufti is competent.
2
Understand the mufti's financial and ethical boundaries
It is better to give fatwa voluntarily. He may take a stipend from the treasury but not a fee from the mustafti. Gifts are allowed, but bribes are forbidden. The imam should provide a sufficient income for teachers and muftis.
Financial independence protects the mufti's integrity.
3
Master the proper form of the fatwa response
The mufti must order answers, write clearly, avoid ambiguous phrases like 'there are two sayings' without explanation, and begin with 'al-hamdu lillah' and end with 'wa Allahu a'lam'. He should not write on the back of the sheet, but may use margins. For complex cases (e.g., kufr with interpretation, qisas), he must be meticulous.
Clarity and completeness are paramount.
4
Handle situations with multiple conflicting views
When there are two sayings (qawlayn) or two ways (wajhayn), the mufti should act on the later one if known, or the one preferred by the majority. If not qualified for tarjih, he must pause or consult the preferred view of the madhhab.
This ensures the fatwa reflects the strongest position.
5
Address special cases: kufr, qisas, inheritance
If asked about someone who spoke kufr with interpretation, the mufti must differentiate based on intent. For qisas, he details conditions. For inheritance, he specifies sibling types and handles 'awl. He must also prioritize urgent cases (women, travelers) when needed.
These examples show the mufti's need for comprehensive knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المستفتي : يجب أن يستفتي من عرف علمه وعدالته ولو بإخبار ثقة عارف أو باستفاضة وإلا بحث عن ذلك فلو خفيت عدالته الباطنة اكتفى بالعدالة الظاهرة. ويعمل بفتوى عالم مع وجود أعلم جهله فإن اختلفا ولا نص قدم الأعلم، وكذا إذا اعتقد أحدهما أعلم أو أورع ويقدم الأعلم على الأورع ولو أجيب في واقعة لا تتكرر ثم حدثت لزم إعادة السؤال إن لم يعلم استناد الجواب إلى نص أو إجماع، وإن لم تطمئن نفسه إلى جواب المفتي استحب سؤال غيره ولا يجب. ويكفي المستفتي بعث رقعة أو رسول ثقة، ومن الأدب أن لا يسأل والمفتي قائم أو مشغول بما يمنع تمام الفكر وأن لا يقول بجوابه هكذا قلت أنا ولا يطالبه بدليل فإن أراده فوقت آخر وليبين موضع السؤال وينقط المشتبه في الرقعة ويتأملها لا سيما آخرها، ويتثبت ولا يقدح الإسراع مع التحقيق وأن يشاور فيما يحسن اظهاره من حضر متأهلاً وإن يصلح لحناً فاحشاً، وليشغل بياضاً بخط كيلا يلحق بشيء ويبين خطه بقلم بين قلمين، ولا بأس بكتبه الدليل لا السؤال، ولا يكتب خلف يصلح، وله أن من يضرب عليه إن أمن فتنة وإن سخط المالك وينهي المستفتي عن ذلك، وليس له الرقعة، وينبغي للإمام أن يبحث عن أهل العلم عمن يصلح للفتوى ليمنع من لا يصلح، وليكن المفتي متنزهاً عن خوارم المروءة فقيه النفس سليم الذهن حسن التصرف ولو عبداً أو امرأة أو أخرس تفهم إشارته، وليس هو كالشاهد في رد فتواه لقرابة وجر نفع وتقبل فتوى لا يكفر، ولا يفسق ببدعة كشهادته ويفتي ولو كان قاضياً وفي اشتراط معرفة الحساب لتصحيح مسائله وجهان ويشترط أن يحفظ مذهب إمامه ويعرف قواعده وأساليبه. وليس المبتدأ والخبر نعت لمجتهد . قوله : ( ويكره أن يقتصر على ما فيه (قولان أي على قوله في الجواب فيه قولان . للأصولي الماهر وكذا البحاث في الخلاف من أئمة الفقه وفحول المناظرين أن يفتي في الفروع الشرعية، ولا يجب افتاء فيما لا يقع. ويحرم التساهل في الفتوى واتباع الحيل إن فسدت الأغراض وسؤال من عرف لذلك، ولا يفتي في حال تغير أخلاقه خروجه عن الاعتدال ولو لفرح، ومدافعة أخبثين، فإن أفتى معتقداً أن ذلك لم يمنعه عن درك الصواب صحت فتواه وإن خاطر والأولى أن يتبرع بالفتوى فإن أخذ رزقاً من بيت المال جاز إلا إن تعينت عليه وله كفاية. ولا يأخذ أجرة من مستفت فإن جعل له أهل البلد رزقاً جاز وإن استؤجر جاز والأولى كونها بأجرة مثل كتبه مع كراهة وله قبول هدية لا رشوة على فتوى لما يريد، وعلى الإمام أن يفرض لمدرس ومفت كفايته . ولكل أهل بلد اصطلاح في اللفظ فلا يجوز أن يفتي أهل بلد بما يتعلق باللفظ من يعرف اصطلاحهم وليس له العمل والفتوى بأحد القولين أو الوجهين من غير تعويل عليه في القولين أن يعمل بالمتأخر إن علمه وإلا فبالذي رجحه الشافعي وإلا لزمه البحث عنه، فإن كان أهلاً اشتغل به متعرفاً لذلك من القواعد والمأخذ وإلا تلقاه من نقلة المذهب فإن عدم الترجيح توقف وحكم الوجهين كالقولين لكن لا عبرة بالمتأخر إلا إذا وقعا من شخص، فإن اختلفوا في الأرجح ولم يكن أهلاً للترجيح اعتمد ما صححه الأكثر والأعلم وإلا توقف. والعمل بالجديد من قولي الشافعي إلا في نحو ثلاثين مسألة. وإن كان في الرقعة مسائل رتب الأجوبة على ترتيبها، ويكره أن يقتصر على «فيه قولان إذ لا يفيد ولا يطلق حيث التفصيل فهو خطأ، ويجيب على ما في الرقعة لا على ما يعلمه فإن أرادء قال إن أراد كذا فجوابه كذا، ويجيب الأول في الناحية اليسرى وإن شاء غيرها لا قبل البسملة، وليكتب الحمد الله وليختم بقوله والله أعلم . ولا يقبح أن يقول في الجواب عندنا وإن تعلقت بالسلطان دعا له فقال وعلى السلطان سدده الله أو شد إزاره، ويكره أطال الله بقاءه. ويختصر جوابه ويوضح عبارته. وإن سئل عن تكلم بكفر متأول قال : يسئل إن أراد كذا فلا شيء عليه، وإن أراد كذا فيستتاب فإن تاب قبلت توبته وإلا قتل. وإن سئل عمن قتل أو جرح احتاط وذكر شروط القصاص ويبين قدر التعزير ويكتب على الملصق من الورقة وإن ضاقت كتب في الظهر والحاشية أولى لا ورقة أخرى. ويشافهه بما عليه بل إن اقتضاهما السؤال لم يقتصر على أحدهما، ولا يلقنه على خصمه فإن وجب الافتاء قدم السابق بفتوى ثم أقرع، نعم يجب تقديم نساء ومسافرين تهيؤوا أو تضرروا بالتخلف إلا إن ظهر تضرر غيرهم بكثرتهم. وإن سئل عن الإخوة فصل في جوابه ابن الأبوين أو لأب أو لأم، وإن كان في الفريضة عول قال الثمن عائلاً وإن كان في الورثة من يسقط بحال دون حال بينه. ويكتب تحت الفتوى الصحيحة إن عرف أنها لأهل الجواب صحيح ونحوه وله أن يجيب إن رأى ذلك ويختصر وإن جهل حاله يبحث عن حاله، فإن لم يظهر له فله أمره بإبدالها، فإن تعسر أجاب بلسانه .
Chapter on the one seeking fatwa: He must seek from one whose knowledge and integrity are known, even by report of a trustworthy knowledgeable person or by common knowledge; otherwise he investigates. If his inner integrity is hidden, apparent integrity suffices. He acts upon the fatwa of a scholar even if a more learned one exists ignorantly; if they differ and there is no text, he gives precedence to the more learned. Likewise if he believes one is more learned or more pious, he gives precedence to the more learned over the more pious. If he was answered in a non-recurring case and then it occurs again, he must repeat the question unless he knows the answer is based on a text or consensus. If his soul is not at ease with the mufti's answer, it is recommended to ask another, not obligatory. It suffices for the mustafti to send a note or a trustworthy messenger. It is etiquette that he does not ask while the mufti is standing or preoccupied, and does not say about his answer 'Thus I said', nor demand evidence; if he wants it, then at another time. He should clarify the question, dot ambiguous words in the note, ponder it especially its end, be deliberate, and speed with accuracy does not harm. He may consult those present who are qualified, and may correct an obvious error. He should fill margins so nothing can be inserted, make his writing clear between two lines. There is no harm in writing the evidence but not the question. He should not write on the back of a sheet, but may strike out if safe from fitna even if the owner is displeased; and he forbids the mustafti from that. The note is not his property. The leader should search for qualified scholars to prevent the unqualified. The mufti should be free from vulgarity, have a fiqh-oriented mind, sound intellect, good conduct, even if a slave, woman, or mute whose signs are understood. He is not like a witness in that his fatwa is rejected due to kinship or benefit; the fatwa of someone who does not become an unbeliever or sinner by bid'ah is accepted, like testimony. He may give fatwa even if he is a judge. Regarding the condition of knowing calculation for correcting his cases, there are two views. It is conditional that he memorizes his imam's madhhab and knows its principles and methods. The subject and predicate are not descriptive of a mujtahid. He said: (It is disliked to restrict to 'there are two sayings'), meaning he says in the answer 'in it there are two sayings'. For the skilled usul scholar and also the researcher in disagreement among the imams of fiqh and great dialecticians, he may give fatwa on legal branches. Giving fatwa on what does not occur is not obligatory. Carelessness in fatwa and following legal ruses if they corrupt purposes is forbidden, as is asking someone known for that. He does not give fatwa when his character changes, when he is not in equilibrium, even due to joy, or while repelling two najas. If he gives fatwa believing that does not prevent him from reaching correctness, his fatwa is valid though he takes a risk. It is better that he gives fatwa voluntarily. If he takes a stipend from the treasury, it is permissible unless it is obligatory upon him and he has sufficiency. He does not take a fee from the mustafti. If the townspeople set a stipend for him, it is permissible. If he is hired, it is permissible, but it is better to have it as compensation for his books with dislike. He may accept a gift but not a bribe for the fatwa he desires. The leader should assign for a teacher and a mufti his sufficiency. Every town's people have their own expression, so it is not permissible to give fatwa to a people regarding wording without knowing their terminology. He should not act or give fatwa by one of two sayings or two ways without reliance. Regarding the two sayings: he acts by the later if he knows it, otherwise by the one preferred by al-Shafi'i (?), otherwise he must investigate. If he is qualified, he engages in it, learning from the principles and sources; otherwise he learns from transmitters of the madhhab. If there is no tarjih, he pauses. The ruling of the two ways is like the two sayings, but the later is not considered unless both come from one person. If they differ on the more preponderant and he is not qualified for tarjih, he relies on what the majority and the most learned have corrected, otherwise he pauses. Action is on the new of al-Shafi'i's two sayings except in about thirty issues. If there are multiple questions in the note, he orders answers accordingly. It is disliked to restrict to 'there are two sayings' as it is not beneficial and he does not say it where detail is needed, it is wrong. He answers based on what is in the note, not on what he knows. If he intends, he says: if he means such and such, then the answer is such. He writes the answer first on the left side, and if he wishes otherwise, not before the basmala. He writes 'al-hamdu lillah' and ends with 'wa Allahu a'lam'. It is not ugly to say in the answer 'with us' and if it relates to the sultan, he prays for him saying 'and upon the sultan, may Allah guide him or strengthen his reign' and it is disliked to say 'may Allah prolong his life'. He shortens his answer and clarifies his expression. If asked about someone who said words of disbelief with interpretation, he says: he is asked; if he meant such and such, then nothing upon him; if he meant such and such, he is asked to repent; if he repents, his repentance is accepted; otherwise killed. If asked about someone who killed or wounded, he is careful and mentions the conditions of qisas and explains the amount of ta'zir. He writes on the attached part of the paper, and if it is narrow, he writes on the back or margin preferably, not on another sheet. He informs him orally what is upon him; if the question requires both, he does not restrict to one. He does not coach him against his opponent. If giving fatwa becomes obligatory, he gives precedence to the earlier one with a fatwa, then draws lots. Yes, he must give precedence to women and travelers who have prepared or are harmed by delay, unless harm to others appears due to their large number. If asked about siblings, he details in his answer half-brothers by father or mother. If in the estate there is 'awl, he says 'the one-eighth is awl', and if among the heirs there is someone who is excluded in some states, he clarifies. He writes under the correct fatwa, if he knows it is for the people of the answer, 'correct' and similar. He may answer if he sees that, and shorten. If he is unaware of the questioner's condition, he investigates. If it does not become clear to him, he may order him to replace it; if that is difficult, he answers orally.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This is a comprehensive chapter on the mustafti (one seeking a fatwa) and the mufti. The first part details the obligations and etiquettes of the questioner: he must ensure the mufti is knowledgeable and upright, even if he only knows of his apparent integrity. If two muftis differ, the more knowledgeable is followed. If the same issue arises again after a previous fatwa, the question must be repeated unless the answer was based on clear text or consensus. It is recommended but not obligatory to ask another if unsatisfied. The mustafti may send a written note or a messenger; there are rules for writing the note clearly. The second part focuses on the mufti: he must be of upright character and competent, even if a slave, woman, or mute (with understood signs). His fatwa is not rejected due to kinship or benefit. He must know the madhhab's principles. It is disliked to say 'there are two sayings' without clarification. He should not take a fee but may accept a stipend or gift (not bribe). When there are multiple valid positions, he must know the preferred view (the later one if known, or the one favored by al-Shafi'i if no Hanafi tarjih is available—this is striking and may indicate a cross-madhhab borrowing in textual transmission). The mufti must order his answers, avoid abbreviations like 'there are two sayings', and write clearly. Special cases: asked about someone who spoke kufr with interpretation, he must differentiate; asked about qisas or ta'zir, he details conditions. He gives precedence to earlier claimants, but women and travelers may be prioritized. For inheritance, he specifies brother types and handles 'awl. Finally, he may verify the questioner's condition and require a rewrite if necessary.

Key Terms
مفتي (mufti): A qualified scholar who issues fatwa (legal opinion).
عدالة (adalah): Integrity, uprightness; required in a mufti and also considered in the mustafti's verification.
تخريج (takhrij): Deriving a ruling from one case to another when the imam's texts differ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on a mufti accepting a gift from someone who might later seek a fatwa?
A) Absolutely forbidden because it is a bribe.
B) Permissible as long as it is not intended as a bribe for a desired ruling.
C) Only allowed if the mufti is poor.
D) Disliked but not haram.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must be competent, ethical, and clear in his responses, and the imam must ensure only qualified scholars issue fatwas.

Qada — Judiciary

Accepting Judgeship and Retracting a Fatwa
Rulings on judgeship and fatwa retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting judgeship from unjust rulers and explain the consequences of a mufti retracting his fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti's retraction voids a past action only if it contradicted a definitive proof; the mufti is never liable for damages.

This lesson addresses two interconnected topics from the chapter on Taqlid: the permissibility of accepting a judicial appointment from any ruler, and the binding effects of a mufti's retraction of his fatwa. The text distinguishes between retraction before and after the questioner acts, and clarifies when a prior action must be voided. It also absolves the mufti of financial liability, emphasizing that ijtihad carries no guarantee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on accepting judgeship
Locate the statement 'ويجوز تقليد القضاء السلطان العادل والجائز ومن أهل البغي'. Recognize that the Hanafi school permits accepting judgeship even from unjust or rebellious authorities.
This is based on the principle that the judge's authority comes from the office, not the ruler's personal character.
2
Understand the exceptional case of no mufti available
Read the line 'وإن عدم المفتي في بلده... فلا يؤاخذ صاحب الواقعة'. Realize that if a person cannot find a mufti or a reliable source, he is not accountable for acting without a fatwa.
This is a concession due to hardship (mashaqqa).
3
Distinguish retraction before vs. after action
The text says 'أفتاه ثم رجع قبل العمل كف عنه' (retraction before acting: stop) and 'وإن رجع بعد العمل وقد خالف دليلاً قاطعاً نقضه' (retraction after action: void only if a definitive proof is contradicted). Compare the two scenarios.
Before action, retraction always stops the act. After action, voiding depends on the nature of the proof.
4
Apply the condition of definitive proof (dalil qati')
Note that 'دليلاً قاطعاً' refers to clear Quranic or mutawatir texts. If the fatwa merely contradicted a zanni proof, the action is not voided.
For a muqallid mufti, the text of his Imam is considered like a definitive proof.
5
Recognize the mufti's obligation to inform and non-liability
The text states 'وعلى المفتي إعلامه برجوعه' and 'وإن أتلف بفتواه لا يغرم'. Understand that the mufti must inform the questioner of retraction (before action, and after if voidal is necessary), but he is not financially liable for any loss caused by his fatwa.
This is because the mufti is a guide, not a guarantor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القضاء
فصل في التقليد
يسأل القضاء ويجوز تقليد القضاء السلطان العادل والجائز ومن أهل البغي فإن تقلد يسأل
رجع
:
من
وإن عدم المفتي في بلده وغيرها ولا من ينقل له حكمها فلا يؤاخذ صاحب الواقعة بشيء يصيبه إذ لا تكليف فرع أفتاه ثم رجع قبل العمل كف عنه، وكذا إذا نكح امرأة بفتواه ثم لزمه فراقها كما في القبلة وإن رجع بعد العمل وقد خالف دليلاً قاطعاً نقضه وإلا فلا. وإن كان المفتي يقلد الإمام فنص إمامه وإن كان اجتهادياً في حقه كالدليل القطعي وعلى المفتي إعلامه برجوعه قبل العمل، وكذا بعده إن وجب النقض وإن أتلف بفتواه لا يغرم ولو كان أهلاً ا هـ والله تعالى أعلم .
Book of Judging. Section on Taqlid. He asks for the judgeship? It is permissible to accept the judgeship from a just Sultan, a sinful one, and from the people of rebellion. If he accepts, he is asked? (then) from... And if there is no mufti in his town and other places, nor anyone to convey its ruling to him, then the person with the incident is not held accountable for anything that befalls him, since there is no obligation. Branch: He gave a fatwa, then retracted before action: he refrains from acting on it. Similarly, if he married a woman by his fatwa, then separation became binding on him, as in the qibla. And if he retracts after action, and he has contradicted a definitive proof, his ruling is voided; otherwise not. And if the mufti is a muqallid of the Imam, then the text of his Imam is like a definitive proof in his regard. And upon the mufti is to inform him (the questioner) of his retraction before action, and likewise after if voidal is necessary. And if he causes destruction by his fatwa, he is not liable even if he was qualified. End. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Taqlid in the Book of Judging presents several rulings concerning the acceptance of judgeship and the consequences of retracting a fatwa. The author begins by stating that it is permissible to accept the position of judge (qada) whether the appointing authority is a just ruler, a sinful ruler, or even from the rebellious. However, the phrase 'يسأل القضاء' is unclear; it may mean 'if one seeks the judgeship' (which is generally disliked) or 'if one is asked to take it'. The underlying principle is that the judge's ruling is binding based on the authority of the appointing body, even if that body is unjust, as long as the judge himself is qualified. The passage then shifts to the case where a person has a legal incident but cannot find a mufti in his town or someone to convey the ruling. In such a case, he is not held accountable for acting without a fatwa because there is no obligation (taklif) on him to find what is inaccessible. The core ruling concerns a mufti who retracts his fatwa. If he retracts before the questioner acts upon it, the questioner must stop. For example, if he issued a fatwa permitting a marriage, then retracted before the marriage took place, the marriage must not proceed. If he retracted after the marriage, and the fatwa contradicted a definitive proof (dalil qati'), the marriage is voided; otherwise it stands. The same applies if the mufti is a muqallid (follower) of an Imam—the Imam's text is considered a definitive proof for him. The mufti is obligated to inform the questioner of his retraction before action, and also afterwards if the retraction requires voiding the action. Finally, if the mufti's fatwa causes financial loss to someone, he is not personally liable (yaghrum) even if he was qualified, because his fatwa is a form of ijtihad and he is not a guarantor.

Key Terms
تقليد القضاء (taqlid al-qada): Accepting the position of judge (qadi) from a ruler or authority.
دليل قاطع (dalil qati'): A definitive proof from the Quran or mutawatir Sunnah that is clear and unambiguous.
يغرم (yaghrum): To be liable or required to pay compensation for damages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mufti gives a fatwa permitting a marriage, then retracts after the marriage takes place, and the original fatwa contradicted a definitive proof (dalil qati'), what is the ruling?
A) The marriage stands and the couple must stay together.
B) The marriage is void and separation is required.
C) The mufti must pay compensation to the couple.
D) The mufti is considered a sinner but the marriage remains valid.

Key Takeaway
A mufti's fatwa is not a guarantee; retraction voids only when a definitive proof is contradicted, and the mufti owes no compensation.

The Mufti's Conditions, Etiquettes, and the Authority to Give Fatwa in Later Hanafism
Intra-Hanafi dispute on muqallid mufti's authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and etiquettes for a Hanafi mufti, explain the hierarchy of imams for fatwa, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a muqallid must know the evidence to give fatwa.

Core Idea
A muqallid mufti in later times gives fatwa by narrating the Imam's ruling, not by ijtihad.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq primarily sets out the practical requirements for a mufti: he must be just, avoid bias, and follow a strict hierarchy of Hanafi imams. The author then tackles a critical question: how can later scholars (mashayikh), who are merely muqallids, give fatwa when a reported condition from the early companions of Abu Hanifa requires knowing the evidence? The resolution redefines the mufti as a narrator (haki), preserving the madhhab without requiring ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions and etiquettes
List the external conditions (shurut) and inner etiquettes (adab) required of the mufti as stated at the beginning of the passage.
Conditions include justice, preserving order, not inclining to the rich; etiquettes include handling question papers with respect, studying carefully, and asking for clarification.
2
Understand the Hanafi hierarchy for fatwa
Note the ranked order: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufr and Hasan ibn Ziyad. A non-mujtahid mufti must follow this order and cannot choose arbitrarily.
This hierarchy is corrected in al-Sirajiyya.
3
Recognize the dispute
The author raises the problem: later mashayikh often gave fatwa contrary to Abu Hanifa, but they were muqallids. A report says 'it is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our saying until he knows from where we said'.
This report is attributed to the early companions of Abu Hanifa.
4
Analyze the early view (prohibition)
Al-Ramli (the muhaqqiq) argues that a non-mujtahid cannot give fatwa at all; what he issues is not a fatwa but a narration (hikayah). The early condition is categorical.
Al-Ramli's objection is that the author's position contradicts the transmitted condition.
5
Analyze the later view (obligation)
The author distinguishes between the time of the Salaf and later times. In later times, preservation (hifz) of the madhhab's rulings suffices, making it permissible and even wajib for a qualified muqallid to give fatwa by narrating the Imam's saying.
The author cites al-Qunyah and al-TatarKhaniyya in support, equating the muqallid to a hadith narrator.
6
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
If the early view were followed, the Hanafi madhhab would effectively cease to function. The later view allows continuity. The author prefers the later view as the operative position (mufta bihi) in our time.
The tarjih is based on necessity (darurah) and the analogy to narrators of hadith.

المسألة
السؤال ثم يجيب، وإذا لم يتضح السؤال سأل من المستفتي. بالكاغد إلى الأرض يرمي وهو لا يجوز، وكان بعضهم لا يأخذ الرقعة من يد امرأة ولا وكان له تلميذ يأخذ منهم ويجمعها ويرفعها فيكتبها تعظيماً للعلم والأحسن أخذ المفتي من كل أحد تواضعاً. ويجوز للشاب الفتوى إذا كان حافظاً للروايات واقفاً على الدرايات محافظاً على الطاعات مجانباً للشهوات والشبهات والعالم كبير إن كان صغيراً، والجاهل صغير وإن كان كبيراً. وصحح في السراجية أن المفتي يفتي بقول أبي حنيفة على الإطلاق ثم بقول أبي يوسف ثم بقول محمد ثم بقول زفر والحسن بن زياد ولا يخير إذا لم يكن مجتهداً. وإذا اختلف مفتيان يتبع قول الأفقه منهما بعد أن يكون أورعهما. وينبغي أن يكتب عقب جوابه «والله أعلم» أو نحوه. وقيل في العقائد يكتب والله الموفق ونحوه، وكره بعضهم الإفتاء والصحيح عدم الكراهة للأهل. ولا ينبغي الإفتاء إلا لمن عرف أقاويل العلماء من أين قالوا، فإن كان في خلاف لا يختار قولاً يجيب به حتى يعرف حجته، وينبغي السؤال من أفقه أهل زمانه فإن اختلفوا تحرى ا هـ . وصحح في الحاوي القدسي أن الإمام إذا كان في جانب وهما في جانب فالأصح أن الاعتبار لقوة المدرك. فإن قلت : كيف جاز للمشايخ الإفتاء بغير قول الإمام الأعظم مع أنهم مقلدون؟ قلت : قد أشكل على ذلك مدة طويلة ولم أر فيه جواباً إلا ما فهمته من كلامهم وهو أنهم نقلوا من أصحابنا أنه لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا حتى نقل في السراجية أن هذا مخالفة سبب عصام للإمام وكان يفتي بخلاف قوله كثيراً لأنه لم يعلم الدليل وكان يظهر له دليل غيره فيفتي به فأقول: إن هذا الشرط كان في زمانهم أما في زماننا فيكتفي بالحفظ كما في القنية وغيرها فيحل الإفتاء بقول الإمام بل يجب وإن لم نعلم من أين قال وعلى هذا فما صححه في الحاوي مبني على ذلك الشرط. وقد

الله تعالى : وكلامه هنا موهم
أن ذلك مروي عن المشايخ كما هو ظاهر من سياقه. قوله : (بل يجب الإفتاء وإن لم يعلم من أين (قال اعترضه المحشي الرملي قال : هذا مضاد لقوله «لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا إذ هو صريح في عدم جواز الإفتاء لغير أهل الاجتهاد فكيف يستدل به على وجوبه فنقول : ما يصدر من غير الأهل ليس بإفتاء حقيقة وإنما هو حكاية عن المجتهد أنه قائل بكذا وباعتبار هذا الملحظ تجوز حكاية قول غير الإمام فكيف يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه ونحوه إنما نحكي فتواهم لا غير فليتأمل .اهـ. قلت: ويشهد له ما في التتارخانية قال صاحب الأقضية أبو جعفر بعدما بين أهلية القضاء : لا ينبغي لأحد أن يقضي بالناس إلا من كان هكذا يريد به أن المفتي ينبغي أن يكون عدلاً عالماً بالكتاب والسنة واجتهاد الرأي قال : إلا أن يفتي بشيء قد سمعه فإنه يجوز وإن لم يكن عالماً بالكتاب والسنة لأنه حاك ما سمعه من غيره فهو بمنزلة الرواي في باب الأحاديث فيشترط فيه ما يشترط في الراوي من النقل والضبط
And among its conditions: preservation of the sequence, and justice between questioners, not inclining to the rich and the officials of the Sultan and the princes, but writing the answer of the precedent whether rich or poor. Its etiquettes: he takes the paper with reverence, and reads the matter with insight again and again until the issue becomes clear to him. Then he answers. And if the question does not become clear, he asks the questioner. And throwing the paper to the ground is not permissible. And some of them would not take the paper from a woman's hand, nor... and he had a student who took from them and collected them and raised them, and wrote them out of respect for knowledge. But the best is that the mufti takes from everyone out of humility. And it is permissible for a young man to give fatwa if he is a guardian of the narrations, knowledgeable of the rational matters, preserving of obedience, avoiding desires and doubts. The scholar is great even if young; the ignorant is small even if old. And it is corrected in al-Sirajiyya that the mufti gives fatwa by the saying of Abu Hanifa absolutely, then by the saying of Abu Yusuf, then by the saying of Muhammad, then by the saying of Zufr and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and he does not choose unless he is a mujtahid. And if two muftis differ, the saying of the more learned of the two is followed after he is more pious. And he should write after his answer 'And Allah knows best' or similar. And it is said in matters of beliefs he writes 'And Allah is the granter of success' and similar. And some disliked giving fatwa, but the correct is no dislike for the qualified. And he should not give fatwa except for one who knows the sayings of the scholars from where they said. Then if he is in a difference, he does not choose a saying to answer with until he knows its proof. And he should ask from the most learned of his time; if they differ, he adopts the most correct. End. And it is corrected in al-Hawi al-Qudsi that if the Imam is on one side and they are on another side, the most correct is that consideration is given to the strength of the evidence. Then if you say: How was it permissible for the senior scholars (mashayikh) to give fatwa by other than the saying of the greatest Imam (Abu Hanifa) while they were muqallids? I say: This has puzzled me for a long time, and I have not seen an answer except what I understood from their speech: that they narrated from our companions that it is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our saying until he knows from where we said. It is even narrated in al-Sirajiyya that this was the reason for 'Isam's opposition to the Imam, and he used to give fatwa contrary to his saying frequently because he did not know the evidence, and another evidence appeared to him, so he gave fatwa by it. So I say: This condition was in their time. As for our time, being content with preservation (hifz) suffices, as in al-Qunyah etc. So it is permissible, nay obligatory, to give fatwa by the Imam's saying even if we do not know from where he said. And based on this, what is corrected in al-Hawi is built on that condition. And now Allah's saying: his speech here is ambiguous... that it is narrated from the mashayikh as is apparent from its context. His saying: 'Rather, giving fatwa is obligatory even if he does not know from where he said' was objected to by the muhaqqiq al-Ramli. He said: This contradicts his saying 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our saying until he knows from where we said' for that is explicit in the non-permissibility of giving fatwa for other than the people of ijtihad. So how can it be used as evidence for its obligation? Then we say: What issues from other than the qualified is not truly a fatwa; rather it is a narration (hikayah) from the mujtahid that he said such-and-such. By this consideration, the narration of the saying of other than the Imam is permissible. So how can it be obligatory for us to give fatwa by the Imam's saying? And if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it, we are only narrating their fatwa, nothing else. So let this be considered carefully. End. I say: And what supports it is what is in al-TatarKhaniyya: the author of al-Aqdiya, Abu Ja'far, after explaining the qualification of the judge, said: It is not fit for anyone to judge among people except one who is like that. He meant by it that the mufti should be just, knowledgeable of the Book and Sunnah, and capable of ijtihad. He said: Except if he gives fatwa by something he has heard, then it is permissible even if he is not knowledgeable of the Book and Sunnah, because he is narrating what he heard from others. So he is like a narrator in the chapter of hadiths, so the same conditions required of a narrator are required of him in terms of transmission and precision.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This lengthy passage from the commentary on 'Fasl fi al-Taqlid' delves into the conditions (shurut) and etiquettes (adab) of the mufti, followed by a critical intra-Hanafi dispute about the necessity of knowing the evidence when giving fatwa. The author lists several conditions: the mufti must maintain order, be just between rich and poor, avoid bias toward authorities, and handle question papers with respect. He should study the question thoroughly and ask for clarification if needed. The mufti must be of upright character, knowledgeable of narrations (riwayat) and rational matters (dirayat), and avoid worldly desires and doubts. The hierarchy of Hanafi imams for fatwa is clarified: first Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufr and Hasan ibn Ziyad; a non-mujtahid mufti may not choose between them. If two muftis differ, the more learned and pious is followed. The passage then cites al-Sirajiyya for this ranking. A practical issue arises: many later mashayikh (senior scholars who were muqallids) gave fatwa based on the Quran and Sunnah directly, sometimes contrary to Abu Hanifa. The author addresses the conundrum by distinguishing between the early period when mujtahids existed and the later period when even muqallids could give fatwa by narrating the Imam's view. He quotes a report from the companions of Abu Hanifa that 'it is not permissible to give fatwa by our saying until one knows from where we said'. This condition was for the time of the Salaf; today, merely preserving (hifz) the transmitted rulings is sufficient, making it permissible and even wajib (obligatory) for a qualified muqallid to give fatwa according to the Hanafi school, even without knowing the evidence. The muhaqqiq al-Ramli objects, arguing that what non-mujtahids issue is not a true fatwa but a narration (hikayah) of the mujtahid's opinion. On this view, it is not wajib for a muqallid to give fatwa by the Imam's saying; he is merely narrating. The author defends the majority practice by citing Abu Ja'far in al-TatarKhaniyya, who equates such a mufti to a narrator of hadith: he transmits what he has heard, so he must be trustworthy and precise. This resolution allows the entire Hanafi tradition to function without requiring each mufti to be an independent mujtahid.

Key Terms
حكاية (hikayah): Narration or transmission of the mujtahid's opinion without personal ijtihad; the muqallid mufti is a 'haki'.
حفظ الروايات (hifz al-riwayat): Preservation of the transmitted rulings of the madhhab, which suffices for giving fatwa in later times.
مفتٍ (mufti): One who issues fatwa; in this passage, a qualified muqallid who preserves the madhhab's rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, what is the ruling for a qualified muqallid (non-mujtahid) in giving fatwa according to the Hanafi school in later times?
A) It is forbidden unless he knows the evidence.
B) It is permissible but not obligatory.
C) It is permissible and even obligatory (wajib) if he preserves the narrations.
D) It is only permissible if he is a mujtahid in another field.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti in later times must give fatwa by narrating the relied-upon view of the madhhab; preservation of narrations suffices in place of knowledge of evidence.

Qada — Judiciary
advanced
12 min
Fatwa Methodology: Knowledge of Evidence vs. Taqlid
Intra-Hanafi debate on fatwa qualifications and the role of evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a mufti according to the Hanafi school and explain the dispute about whether a muqallid must know the evidence behind the Imam's ruling.

Core Idea
A mufti in later times may give fatwa by transmitting the school's rulings, even without knowing the evidence; but the earlier condition required knowledge of the proof.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi debate about the qualifications for issuing fatwa. While earlier authorities insisted that a mufti must know the evidence (dalil) behind the Imam's ruling, later scholars relaxed this condition for muqallids. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents both views and concludes with the practical position that the mufti should follow the choices of the mashayikh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions on evidence requirement
The author argues that in later times, memorization suffices and it is even obligatory to give fatwa according to Abu Hanifah. Al-Ramli counters that this is mere narration (hikayah) and not true fatwa.
Al-Ramli's objection is based on the explicit condition set by Abu Hanifah himself.
2
Examine the proof (dalil) for each side
The author quotes al-Qunyah and Abu Ja'far to support that memorization is enough. Al-Ramli relies on the earlier statement that one must know the evidence.
The hadith narration analogy: a muqallid is like a hadith narrator.
3
Understand the reconciliation
The author distinguishes between the time of the Imams and later times. In earlier times, scholars were expected to know the evidence; later, they only need to transmit the rulings.
The mashayikh themselves sometimes deviated when they found stronger evidence.
4
Apply the later settled position
The consensus (as per Ibn al-Shibli and al-Haskafi) is that the mufti should follow the choices of the mashayikh, who generally upheld Abu Hanifah's rulings.
This means the mufti does not simply follow the Imam's saying in isolation but the preponderant view of the later authorities.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
If a qadi judges against Abu Hanifah's saying without the support of a mashayikh's tashih, his judgment is invalid and may be overturned.
This is the practical consequence: the mufti or qadi must adhere to the tarjih of the mashayikh.

المشايخ بخلافه لأنهم إنما أفتوا بخلافه لفقد شرطه في حقهم وهو الوقوف على دليله، وأما نحن فلنا الإفتاء وإن لم نقف على دليله، وقد وقع للمحقق ابن الهمام في مواضع الرد على المشايخ في الإفتاء بقولهما بأنه لا يعدل عن قوله إلا لضعف دليله وهو قوي في وقت العشاء لكونه الأحوط، وفي تكبير التشريق في آخر وقته إلى آخرها، وذكره في فتح القدير. ولكن هو أهل للنظر في الدليل ومن ليس بأهل للنظر فيه فعليه الإفتاء بقول الإمام. والمراد بالأهلية هنا أن يكون عارفاً مميزاً بين الأقاويل له قدرة على ترجيح بعضها على بعض، ولا يصير الرجل أهلاً للفتوى ما لم يصرحوا به أكثر من خطائه لأن الصواب متى كثر فقد غلب ولا عبرة بالمغلوب الإمام لا يحل له تقليد غيره في غير ما عمل به، وقد علمت ما قدمناه عن التحرير أنه خلاف المختار وأنت ترى أصحاب المتون المعتمدة قد يمشون على غير مذهب الإمام وإذا أفتى المشايخ بخلاف قوله لفقد الدليل في المفتي في زماننا ينقل ما اختاره المشايخ وهو الذي مشى عليه العلامة ابن الشلبي في فتاواه حيث قال : الأصل أن العمل على قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى ولذا ترجح المشايخ دليله في الأغلب على دليل خالفه أصحابه. ويجيبون عما استدل به ،مخالفه وهذا أمارة العمل بقوله وإن لم يصرحوا بالفتوى عليه إذ الترجيح كصريح التصحيح لأن المرجوح طائح بمقابلته بالراجح وحينئذ فلا يعدل المفتي ولا القاضي عن قوله إلا إذا صرح أحد من المشايخ بأن الفتوى على قول غيره فليس للقاضي أن يحكم بقول غير أبي حنيفة في مسألة لم يرجح فيها قول غيره ورجحوا فيها دليل أبي حنيفة على دليله، فإن حكم فيها فحكمه غير ماض ليس له غير الانتقاض والله تعالى أعلم. وهو الذي مشى عليه الشيخ علاء الدين الحصكفي أيضاً في صدر شرحه على التنوير حيث قال: وأما نحن فعلينا اتباع رجحوه وما صححوه كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم. فإن قلت: قد يحكون أقوالاً بلا ترجيح وقد يختلفون في التصحيح؟ قلت : يعمل بمثل ما عملوا من اعتبار تغير العرف وأحوال الناس وما هو الأرفق وما ظهر عليه التعامل وما قوي وجهه، ولا يخلو الوجود ممن يميز هذا حقيقة لا ظناً وعلى من لم يميز أن يرجع لمن يميز لبراءة ذمته .اهـ. والله تعالى أعلم قوله : (لكن هو أهل للنظر) الاستدراك بالنظر إلى قوله لا يعدل عن قوله إلا لضعف دليله يعني أن مثل المحقق له أن يقول من ما من
Book of Judicature. ... and a boy [cannot be a judge?]. The question [the mufti asks] then answers. If the question is not clear, he asks the questioner. [Throwing] the paper to the ground is not permissible. Some (scholars) would not take the paper from a woman, and he had a student who would take from them and collect them and raise them and write them, out of respect for knowledge. The best is that the mufti takes from everyone humbly. It is permissible for a young man to give fatwa if he is a memorizer of the narrations, cognizant of the rational proofs, preserving of acts of obedience, avoiding desires and doubts. The scholar is great even if young, and the ignorant is small even if old. It is established in al-Sirajiyyah that the mufti gives fatwa according to the saying of Abu Hanifah absolutely, then according to the saying of Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and he does not choose if he is not a mujtahid. If two muftis differ, the saying of the more fiqh-aware of them is followed, provided he is more pious. It is recommended that he writes after his answer 'And Allah knows best' or similar. It is said in matters of creed he writes 'And Allah is the granter of success' and similar. Some disliked giving fatwa; the correct is no dislike for the qualified. It is not proper to give fatwa except for one who knows the sayings of the scholars as to whence they said; if there is a difference, he does not choose a saying to answer with until he knows its proof. He should ask the most fiqh-aware of his time; if they differ, he exercises ijtihad. End. It is established in al-Hawi al-Qudsi that if the imam is on one side and they (the two disciples?) are on the other, the more correct is that consideration is given to the strength of the source. If you say: How is it permissible for the mashayikh to give fatwa contrary to the saying of the Greatest Imam, though they are muqallids? I say: This puzzled me for a long time, and I have not seen an answer except what I understood from their words: They narrated from our companions that it is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our saying until he knows from where we said it, even as it is narrated in al-Sirajiyyah that this (condition) was violated by a reason? of 'Isam (the scholar's name) and he used to give fatwa contrary to his (Abu Hanifah's) saying often because he did not know the evidence and another's evidence appeared to him, so he gave fatwa accordingly. So I say: This condition was in their time; as for our time, memorization suffices as in al-Qunyah and other works, so giving fatwa according to the Imam's saying is permissible, rather obligatory, even if we do not know whence he said. Upon this, what was established in al-Hawi is based on that condition. And now... and His statement here gives the impression that that is narrated from the mashayikh, as is apparent from its context. His saying: (Rather, giving fatwa is obligatory even if one does not know whence he said) was objected to by al-Muhashi al-Ramli, saying: This contradicts his saying 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our saying until he knows from where we said it', for it is explicit in forbidding fatwa for other than the people of ijtihad. So how is it used to argue for its obligation? We say: What proceeds from other than the qualified is not in reality a fatwa; rather it is a narration (hikayah) from the mujtahid that he said such and such. In consideration of this perspective, narrating the saying of other than the Imam is permissible. So how can it be obligatory upon us to give fatwa according to the Imam's saying even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it? We merely narrate their fatwa, nothing else. So let it be pondered. End. I say: Supporting this is what is in al-Tatarkhaniyyah: The author of al-Aqdiyah, Abu Ja'far, after discussing the qualifications for judgeship, said: No one should judge among people except one who is such – meaning by this that the mufti should be just, knowledgeable of the Book and Sunnah, and capable of ijtihad. He said: Except if he gives a fatwa about something he has heard, then it is permissible even if he is not knowledgeable of the Book and Sunnah, because he is narrating what he heard from others; he is like a narrator in hadith, and the same conditions of transmission and precision are required. ... Book of Judicature page 453: They established that fatwa is according to the saying of the Imam. It follows from this that it is obligatory upon us to give fatwa according to the Imam's saying even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it, because they only gave contrary to it due to lack of the condition in their case, which is knowing his evidence. As for us, we are permitted to give fatwa even if we do not know his evidence. Indeed, it occurred to al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in certain places to refute the mashayikh for giving fatwa according to the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)?, stating that one should not deviate from his (Abu Hanifah's) saying except due to weakness of his evidence, and it (the Imam's saying) is strong in the time of Isha prayer because it is more precautionary, and in the takbir of tashriq at the end of its time, etc. He mentioned this in Fath al-Qadir. But he (Ibn al-Humam) is qualified to examine evidence, and one who is not qualified should give fatwa according to the Imam's saying. The meaning of qualification here is that he be knowledgeable, able to distinguish between sayings, having the ability to prefer some over others. A person does not become qualified for fatwa unless his correct opinions exceed his mistakes, because when correctness increases, it prevails, and the occasional mistake is disregarded in face of the majority, for the affairs of the Shari'ah are based on what is predominant and most common. So in al-Walwaljiyyah concerning justice. In al-Zahiraiyyah, it is narrated from Abu Hanifah that he said: It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa according to our saying until he knows from where we said it. And if one is not a person of ijtihad, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa except by way of narration (hikayah), so he narrates what he memorizes of the sayings of the fuqaha'. End. So his saying 'he narrates what he memorizes' absolutely indicates that it is not obligatory to adhere to narrating the Imam's madhhab. Indeed, what the author (of al-Hidayah?) mentioned is based on the view that one who adopts the Imam's madhhab is not permissible to follow others in matters he has not acted upon? And you have known what we presented from al-Tahrir that it is against the chosen view. You see that the authors of reliable matns may follow other than the Imam's madhhab. And if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to his saying due to lack of evidence in their case, we follow them, as they are more knowledgeable. How can it be said that we must give fatwa according to the Imam's saying due to lack of condition, when he (the author) admitted that the condition is also lacking in the case of the mashayikh? Did they commit a wrong? The conclusion that equitable nature accepts is that the mufti in our time transmits what the mashayikh chose. This is what Allamah Ibn al-Shibli followed in his fatawa, where he said: The principle is that practice is according to the saying of Abu Hanifah (may Allah have mercy on him). Hence the mashayikh generally give preponderance to his evidence over the evidence of those who opposed him, and they respond to what his opponent argued. This is an indication of practice according to his saying even if they did not explicitly state the fatwa based on it, because giving preponderance is like explicit correction (tashih), since the outweighed is discarded in comparison with the outweighing. Therefore, neither the mufti nor the qadi should deviate from his saying unless one of the mashayikh explicitly states that the fatwa is according to someone else's saying. So it is not permissible for the qadi to judge according to a saying other than Abu Hanifah's in a matter in which no other saying has been given preponderance and in which they have given preponderance to Abu Hanifah's evidence over his opponent's evidence. If he judges based on it, his judgment is not effective; he has no option but to have it overturned. And Allah knows best. This is what Sheikh Ala al-Din al-Haskafi also followed in the beginning of his commentary on al-Tanwir, where he said: As for us, we must follow what they gave preponderance to and what they corrected (tashih), just as if they issued fatwa during their lifetime. If you say: They sometimes narrate sayings without giving preponderance and they differ in correction? I say: Act as they acted, considering change of custom, the condition of people, what is more suitable, what has become common practice, and what has a strong basis. The world will not be devoid of one who distinguishes this truly, not just speculatively. One who cannot distinguish should refer to one who can, to discharge his responsibility. End. And Allah knows best. His saying: (But he is qualified for examination) is an istidrak regarding his saying 'one should not deviate from his saying except due to weakness of his evidence' – meaning that someone like al-Muhaqqiq (Ibn al-Humam) may say... from...
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the qualifications and methodology of a mufti within the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating the conditions for giving fatwa: the mufti must be knowledgeable, God-fearing, and avoid desires. Even a young man may give fatwa if he is well-versed in the transmitted rulings (riwayat) and rational principles (dirayat). The mufti should follow a fixed hierarchy of opinions: first Abu Hanifah, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al-Shaybani, then Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad. He is not free to choose arbitrarily if he is not a mujtahid. If two muftis differ, the opinion of the more knowledgeable and pious is followed. The mufti should end his answer with 'And Allah knows best'. The text then addresses a critical issue: how can later scholars (mashayikh) give fatwa contrary to Abu Hanifah when they are mere muqallids? The author explains that earlier, a condition was that one must know the evidence behind the Imam's rulings. However, in later times, it suffices to simply memorize and transmit the Imam's rulings; in fact, it becomes obligatory to give fatwa according to Abu Hanifah's saying even without knowing the evidence. The commentator al-Muhashi al-Ramli objects to this, arguing that such a practice is not real fatwa but mere narration (hikayah) of the Imam's saying. He insists that true fatwa requires ijtihad. The author then reconciles by citing earlier authorities like Abu Ja'far in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, who state that one who is not a mujtahid may give a fatwa as a narrator (rawi) of the Imam's saying, provided he is reliable in transmission. The discussion concludes with the position of later Hanafi scholars like Ibn al-Shibli and al-Haskafi, who affirm that the mufti in our time should follow the choices of the mashayikh who gave preponderance to Abu Hanifah's evidence. They also note that if a qadi judges against the Imam's saying without a clear preponderance from the mashayikh, his judgment is invalid and must be overturned. The passage thus presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the nature of taqlid and the role of evidence in fatwa, ultimately settling on the practical necessity of following the established school position.

Key Terms
مفتي (mufti): The one who issues fatwa (legal rulings) to questioners. The passage discusses qualifications and hierarchy.
حكاية (hikayah): Narration or transmission of a scholar's saying without necessarily endorsing it. Some argue that non-mujtahids only engage in hikayah, not real fatwa.
إمام أعظم (al-Imam al-A'zam): Imam Abu Hanifah, the founder of the Hanafi school, whose opinion is given top priority in fatwa.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of giving preponderance to one opinion over another based on strength of evidence. The passage refers to the mashayikh's tarjih of Abu Hanifah's evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later settled position in the passage, what should a mufti do if he is asked a question and does not know the evidence behind the rulings?
A) He must refuse to give fatwa until he learns the evidence.
B) He should give fatwa according to his own ijtihad.
C) He should transmit the choices of the mashayikh, which generally uphold Abu Hanifah's rulings.
D) He may choose any Hanafi imam's opinion arbitrarily.

Key Takeaway
In later Hanafi practice, a mufti should follow the choices of the mashayikh, who generally gave preponderance to Abu Hanifah's rulings, even if he does not know the evidence.

Obligation of a Mufti to Follow Imam Abu Hanifa's Opinion
Examines the obligation to follow Imam Abu Hanifa and the role of tarjih by later scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that a non-expert mufti must follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, and identify the exception for qualified scholars.

Core Idea
A mufti who cannot weigh evidence must follow Imam Abu Hanifa; only experts may prefer another opinion.

In the Hanafi school, the primary duty of a mufti is to issue fatwa according to the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, later mashayikh sometimes adopted the opinions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad when they found the Imam's evidence weak. This passage clarifies that such deviation is only permissible for those who are qualified to evaluate evidence (ahliyya). For everyone else, adhering to the Imam's opinion is obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states 'صححوا أن الإفتاء بقول الإمام' – the corrected position is that fatwa is to be given by the Imam's saying.
This is the default obligation for all muftis.
2
Recognize the exception for mashayikh
The mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to the Imam's saying because they were aware of the weakness of his evidence. This exception does not apply to ordinary muftis.
The exception is conditioned on being acquainted with the evidence.
3
Discuss Ibn al-Humam's position
Ibn al-Humam argued that deviation should only occur when the Imam's evidence is weak. He considered himself qualified to make that judgment.
This shows the intra-madhhab dispute.
4
Distinguish between experts and non-experts
Only a mufti who has the ability to perform tarjih (preference) may deviate. Others must stick to the Imam's opinion.
Expertise is defined as being able to distinguish and prefer between opinions.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, today's muftis follow the tarjih of the later mashayikh, not necessarily the direct opinion of the Imam. This is the operative ruling.
The author indicates that we rely on the mashayikh's tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صححوا أن الإفتاء بقول الإمام فينتج من هذا أنه يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه لأنهم إنما أفتوا بخلافه لفقد شرطه في حقهم وهو الوقوف على دليله، وأما نحن فلنا الإفتاء وإن لم نقف على دليله، وقد وقع للمحقق ابن الهمام في مواضع الرد على المشايخ في الإفتاء بقولهما بأنه لا يعدل عن قوله إلا لضعف دليله وهو قوي في وقت العشاء لكونه الأحوط، وفي تكبير التشريق في آخر وقته إلى آخرها، وذكره في فتح القدير. ولكن هو أهل للنظر في الدليل ومن ليس بأهل للنظر فيه فعليه الإفتاء بقول الإمام. والمراد بالأهلية هنا أن يكون عارفاً مميزاً بين الأقاويل له قدرة على ترجيح بعضها على بعض، ولا يصير الرجل أهلاً للفتوى ما لم يصرحوا به أكثر من خطائه لأن الصواب متى كثر فقد غلب ولا عبرة بالمغلوب بمقابلة الغالب فإن أمور الشرع مبنية على الأعم الأغلب؛ كذا في الولوالجية
They have corrected that giving fatwa is by the saying of the Imam. It results from this that it is obligatory upon us to give fatwa by the saying of the Imam, even if the mashayikh gave fatwa contrary to it because they only gave fatwa contrary to it due to the absence of its condition in their regard, which is being acquainted with its evidence. As for us, we can give fatwa even if we are not acquainted with its evidence. It has occurred to the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in places to refute the mashayikh regarding giving fatwa by the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that one should not deviate from his saying except due to the weakness of his evidence, and it is strong at the time of Isha because it is more precautionary, and regarding the takbir of tashriq at the end of its time to the end of it, and he mentioned it in Fath al-Qadir. But he is an expert in looking at evidence. And whoever is not an expert in looking at it must give fatwa by the saying of the Imam. What is meant by 'expertise' here is that he be knowledgeable, distinguishing between the various sayings, having the ability to give preference to some over others. And a man does not become qualified for giving fatwa unless his correct rulings are more than his mistakes, because when the correct is abundant, it prevails, and no attention is paid to the rare in comparison to the prevalent, for the matters of Shariah are built on what is more common and prevalent; thus in al-Walwaljiyya.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligation of a mufti to follow the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa. The author explains that although later mashayikh sometimes gave fatwa by the saying of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, they did so because they were aware of the weakness of Abu Hanifa's evidence in certain contexts. For a mufti who is not an expert in examining evidence, he must follow the Imam's opinion. The text defines expertise (ahlīya) as the ability to distinguish and prefer between different opinions, and it states that one is only considered qualified if his correct fatwas outnumber his mistakes, as the Shariah is based on the prevalent norm. This ruling is taken from al-Walwaljiyya.

Key Terms
الفتوى (al-fatwa): A legal ruling given on a matter of fiqh
الأهلية (al-ahliyya): Qualification to give fatwa: being knowledgeable and able to distinguish and prefer opinions, with correct rulings outnumbering mistakes
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The act of preferring one legal opinion over another based on strength of evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If he finds it more in line with public interest
B) If he is qualified (ahl) to evaluate evidence
C) If the majority of mashayikh agree with it
D) Never, because the Imam's opinion is always the strongest

Key Takeaway
A non-expert mufti must follow the mufta bihi as determined by the later mashayikh.

The Qualification (Ahliyya) of a Mufti: Correct Rulings Must Outnumber Mistakes
Defines the qualification (ahliyya) required for a mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ahliyya for giving fatwa according to the Hanafi school, and state the condition that a mufti's correct rulings must outnumber his mistakes.

Core Idea
A mufti is not qualified unless his correct fatwas exceed his mistakes.

The second part of the passage defines what it means to be 'ahl' (qualified) for giving fatwa. It requires that the mufti be able to distinguish between different opinions and prefer some over others, and crucially, that his correct rulings outnumber his mistakes. This condition is based on the principle that the Shariah is built on the prevalent norm (al-ghalib).

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of ahliyya
The passage states 'والمراد بالأهلية هنا أن يكون عارفاً مميزاً بين الأقاويل له قدرة على ترجيح بعضها على بعض' – expertise means being knowledgeable, distinguishing between opinions, and capable of tarjih.
2
State the additional condition
'ولا يصير الرجل أهلاً للفتوى ما لم يصرحوا به أكثر من خطائه' – a person does not become qualified unless his correct rulings are more than his mistakes.
3
Understand the rationale
The Shariah is based on the prevalent norm (al-ghalib); the rare is not considered.
4
Note the source
The author references al-Walwaljiyya for this ruling.
5
Apply the condition
This condition is a safeguard ensuring that the mufti is reliable. A mufti whose mistakes outnumber correct rulings is not trustworthy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
