Following the Mashayikh's Tarjih is the Relied Upon Position
Establishes that the mufti should follow what the mashayikh have chosen as the preferred opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a mufti may follow the mashayikh's tarjih over Imam Abu Hanifa's literal saying and identify the conditions for deviation.

Core Idea
The mufti follows the mashayikh's tarjih, not every literal word of the Imam.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a fundamental question in Hanafi fatwa methodology: should a mufti rigidly transmit every literal narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, or may he follow the preferred opinions (tarjih) of later mashayikh? The author argues that non-mujtahid muftis must rely on the mashayikh's tarjih, as they are more aware of evidence and evolving customs. This resolves an apparent tension between Abu Hanifa's own warning and later practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Positions
First, recognize that there are two views: one insists on strictly adhering to Imam Abu Hanifa's literal saying (based on his statement that one must know the evidence). The other, held by later scholars like Ibn al-Shulbi and al-Haskafi, says the mufti should follow the tarjih of the mashayikh.
The opposing view is not a different madhhab but an internal Hanafi disagreement.
2
Examine the Proof for Each Position
The strict position relies on Abu Hanifa's reported saying: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our saying unless he knows from where we said it.' The mashayikh's position is supported by the fact that the authors of reliable matns sometimes follow other opinions, and that the mashayikh's tarjih is effectively a correction.
The author quotes Ibn al-Shulbi: tarjih is like explicit correction (taṣḥīḥ).
3
Understand the Hanafi Response
The author argues that Abu Hanifa's condition (knowledge of evidence) was also lost for the mashayikh, yet they were not wrong. Since the mashayikh are more knowledgeable and consider customs, their tarjih should be followed. Non-experts can rely on them.
This resolves the apparent contradiction: the mashayikh fulfill the spirit of the condition.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-on position (mufta bihi) is that the mufti transmits what the mashayikh have chosen and corrected. He should not deviate from Imam Abu Hanifa's saying unless a mashayikh explicitly states that the fatwa is on another opinion.
This is the consensus of later authorities like Ibn al-Shulbi and al-Haskafi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعدالة. وفي الظهيرية روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قال : لا يحل لأحد أن يفتي بقولنا ما لم يعلم من أين قلنا، وإن لم يكن أهل الاجتهاد لا يحل له أن يفتي إلا بطريق الحكاية فيحكي ما يحفظ من أقوال الفقهاء .اهـ. فقوله فيحكي ما يحفظ الخ» بإطلاقه يفيد عدم وجوب التزام حكاية مذهب الإمام، نعم ما ذكره المؤلف يظهر بناء على القول بأن من التزم مذهب الإمام لا يحل له تقليد غيره في غير ما عمل به، وقد علمت ما قدمناه عن التحرير أنه خلاف المختار وأنت ترى أصحاب المتون المعتمدة قد يمشون على غير مذهب الإمام وإذا أفتى المشايخ بخلاف قوله لفقد الدليل في حقهم فنحن نتبعهم إذ هم أعلم، وكيف يقال يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام لفقد الشرط وقد أقر أنه قد فقد الشرط أيضاً في حق المشايخ فهل تراهم ارتكبوا منكراً؟ والحاصل أن الإنصاف الذي يقبله الطبع السليم أن المفتي في زماننا ينقل ما اختاره المشايخ وهو الذي مشى عليه العلامة ابن الشلبي في فتاواه حيث قال : الأصل أن العمل على قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى ولذا ترجح المشايخ دليله في الأغلب على دليل خالفه أصحابه. ويجيبون عما استدل به مخالفه وهذا أمارة العمل بقوله وإن لم يصرحوا بالفتوى عليه إذ الترجيح كصريح التصحيح لأن المرجوح طائح بمقابلته بالراجح وحينئذ فلا يعدل المفتي ولا القاضي عن قوله إلا إذا صرح أحد من المشايخ بأن الفتوى على قول غيره فليس للقاضي أن يحكم بقول غير أبي حنيفة في مسألة لم يرجح فيها قول غيره ورجحوا فيها دليل أبي حنيفة على دليله، فإن حكم فيها فحكمه غير ماض ليس له غير الانتقاض والله تعالى أعلم. وهو الذي مشى عليه الشيخ علاء الدين الحصكفي أيضاً في صدر شرحه على التنوير حيث قال: وأما نحن فعلينا اتباع رجحوه وما صححوه كما لو أفتوا في حياتهم. فإن قلت: قد يحكون أقوالاً بلا ترجيح وقد يختلفون في التصحيح؟ قلت : يعمل بمثل ما عملوا من اعتبار تغير العرف وأحوال الناس وما هو الأرفق وما ظهر عليه التعامل وما قوي وجهه، ولا يخلو الوجود ممن يميز هذا حقيقة لا ظناً وعلى من لم يميز أن يرجع لمن يميز لبراءة ذمته .اهـ. والله تعالى أعلم. قوله : (لكن هو أهل للنظر) الاستدراك بالنظر إلى قوله لا يعدل عن قوله إلا لضعف دليله يعني أن مثل المحقق له أن يقول
And al-'Adāla. In al-Ẓahīriyya, it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: 'It is not permissible for anyone to give fatwa by our saying unless he knows from where we said it. And if he is not a person of ijtihad, it is not permissible for him to give fatwa except by way of narration, so he narrates what he memorizes from the sayings of the jurists.' End. So his saying 'he narrates what he memorizes' etc., by its generality indicates that there is no obligation to adhere to narrating the madhhab of the Imam. Indeed, what the author mentioned appears based on the saying that whoever adheres to the madhhab of the Imam, it is not permissible for him to follow someone else in matters he has not acted upon. And you already know what we presented from al-Tahrir that it is against the chosen view. And you see that the authors of the reliable matns sometimes proceed upon other than the madhhab of the Imam. And when the mashayikh give fatwa contrary to his saying due to the lack of evidence in their regard, then we follow them, for they are more knowledgeable. How can it be said that we must give fatwa by the saying of the Imam due to the loss of the condition, when it is acknowledged that the condition was also lost in the regard of the mashayikh? Do you think they committed a wrong? The conclusion, which sound nature accepts, is that the mufti in our time transmits what the mashayikh have chosen. And this is what Allama Ibn al-Shulbi proceeded upon in his fatawa, where he said: 'The principle is that practice is upon the saying of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and therefore the mashayikh generally prefer his evidence over the evidence of those who opposed him among his companions. And they respond to what his opponent adduced. And this is an indication of practice upon his saying even if they did not explicitly state the fatwa upon it, because tarjih is like explicit correction, since the preponderated falls away in comparison to the preponderant. In that case, the mufti and the judge should not deviate from his saying unless one of the mashayikh explicitly states that the fatwa is upon the saying of another. Then it is not for the judge to judge by the saying of other than Abu Hanifa in a matter in which they did not prefer the saying of another, and they preferred the evidence of Abu Hanifa over his evidence. If he judges in it, his judgment is not enforceable; he has nothing but annulment. And Allah knows best.' And this is what Sheikh Ala al-Din al-Haskafi also proceeded upon at the beginning of his commentary on al-Tanwir, where he said: 'As for us, we must follow what they (the mashayikh) have preponderated and what they have corrected, as if they gave fatwa in their lifetimes. If you say: They sometimes narrate sayings without tarjih and differ in correction. I say: Act according to what they acted upon, considering changes in custom and the conditions of people, and what is more convenient, and what has become customary, and what is strong in its aspect. And existence will not be devoid of one who distinguishes this in reality, not by conjecture. And whoever does not distinguish should refer to one who distinguishes for the acquittal of his conscience.' End. And Allah knows best. His saying: 'But he is an expert in looking at evidence' is an exception with reference to his saying 'one should not deviate from his saying except due to weakness of his evidence', meaning that someone like the muhaqqiq can say...
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on whom a mufti should follow. It begins by quoting Abu Hanifa's famous statement that one must not give fatwa by his saying without knowing its evidence; otherwise, one only narrates the opinions of jurists. The author then argues that this does not obligate always narrating the Imam's saying, and that in practice, the authors of matns sometimes follow other opinions. He concludes that the correct approach is for the mufti to transmit what the mashayikh have chosen, as stated by Ibn al-Shulbi and al-Haskafi. They emphasize that the mashayikh's tarjih is effectively a correction, and the mufti should follow it unless a specific scholar states that the fatwa is on another opinion. The passage also notes that the mashayikh consider changes in custom and what is more convenient.

Key Terms
الحكاية (al-hikaya): Narrating or transmitting the opinions of jurists without ijtihad
الرجحان (al-rujhan): Preponderance of one evidence over another leading to preference

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when should a judge (qadi) deviate from Imam Abu Hanifa's saying?
A) Whenever he finds the evidence of the Sahibayn stronger
B) Never, under any circumstances
C) Only if one of the mashayikh has explicitly stated that the fatwa is on the saying of another
D) Only when the sultan orders him

Key Takeaway
The mufti must follow the tarjih of the later mashayikh, as their preponderance of evidence effectively corrects the literal narration.

Qada — Judiciary

Ruling on Accepting Judgeship When One Fears Injustice
Discusses the ruling on accepting the position of qadi if one fears bias or injustice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on accepting judgeship (taqlid al-qada) when one fears injustice, apply the conditions that turn it from makruh tahrimi to fard 'ayn, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference on the enforceability of the sultan's judgment.

Core Idea
Accepting judgeship is makruh tahrimi if you fear injustice, but becomes fard 'ayn when you are the only qualified judge.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a critical issue for qualified jurists: the ruling on accepting the position of qadi when one fears personal bias or inability. The Hanafi school distinguishes between situations where judgeship is merely disliked (makruh tahrimi) and where it becomes an individual obligation (fard 'ayn). The text also clarifies the qualifications required for a qadi and discusses the enforceability of judgments issued by the sultan himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is taqlid (accepting judgeship). The default ruling for one who fears injustice (hayf) is makruh tahrimi, because it may lead to oppression.
Karahah tahrimi means it is forbidden to do so.
2
Understand the condition for karahah
The fear of hayf (injustice) or inability to establish justice triggers the dislike. The author notes that al-Quduri included both fear of injustice and fear of inability.
If one is safe from hayf and able, it is not disliked.
3
Recognize when it becomes fard 'ayn
When the qualified person is the only one available and the sultan cannot handle disputes himself, judgeship becomes an individual obligation. Refusal then incurs sin and compulsion is permissible.
This is derived from the maxim: communal obligations become individual when restricted.
4
Examine the qualifications for a qadi
Ibn al-Mubarak stated that a qadi must be insightful in hadith and opinion, and knowledgeable of Abu Hanifa's sayings. After the stabilization of madhhabs, taqlid suffices.
The passage discusses this as a proof for the necessity of qualification.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on sultan's judgment
Some Hanafis hold that a sultan's judgment is not enforceable, but the correct view (al-Khassaf, Qadi al-Imam) is that it is enforceable, and this is the mufta bihi.
This affects whether the sultan can relieve others of the obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من كتاب القضاء. وفي مناقب الكردري قال ابن المبارك. وقد سئل متى يحل للرجل أن يفتي ويلي القضاء قال : إذا كان بصيراً بالحديث والرأي عارفاً بقول أبي حنيفة حافظاً له. وهذا محمول على إحدى الروايتين عن أصحابنا وقبل استقرار المذاهب، أما بعد التقرر فلا حاجة إليه لأنه يمكنه التقليد ا.هـ. ومن العجب ما سمعت من بعض حنفية عصرنا حين تكلمت قديماً معه فيها أن قال لما أفتى المشايخ بشيء علمنا أنه قول الإمام فقلت إنه خطأ لأنهم يبينون قول الإمام في ظاهر الرواية ثم يقولون الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف أو محمد أو زفر، وسمعت من بعضهم أنه يقول الكل عن أبي حنيفة . قلت : نعم لكن ما خرج عن ظاهر الرواية فهو مرجوع عنه لما قرروه في الأصول من عدم إمكان صدور قولين مختلفين متساويين من مجتهد والمرجوع عنه لم يبق قولاً له كما ذكروه . قوله : (وكره التقليد لمن خاف الحيف كيلا يكون ذريعة إلى مباشرة الظلم هنا نسختان التقليد أي النصب من السلطان والتقليد أي قبول تقليد القضاء وهي الأولى . والحيف بمعنى الجور والظلم من حاف عليه يحيف إذا جار وخوف عدم إقامة العدل لعجزه كخوف الجور فلو قال المؤلف لمن خاف الحيف أو العجز لكان أولى لأن أحدهما يكفي؛ نص عليه القدوري والمراد بالكراهة كراهة التحريم لأن الغائب الوقوع في محظوره حينئذ، ومحل الكراهة ما إذا لم يتعين عليه فإن انحصر صار فرض عين عليه وعليه ضبط نفسه إلا أن كان السلطان يمكن أن يفصل الخصومات ويتفرغ لذلك ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وإذا لم يمكن السلطان فصل القضايا وفي البلد قوم صالحون له أثموا كلهم كذا في البزازية. ولم أر هل يفسق الممتنع ؟ الظاهر نعم لتركه الفرض إلا أن يقال : إن للممتنع في الغالب تأويلاً وهو مانع من الفسق ولم أر الآن هل يجبر الممتنع المنحصر فيه؟ الظاهر جواز جبره على القبول لاضطرار الناس إليه كاطعام المضطر وسائر فروض الكفاية عند التعين، وكذا جواز جبر المتأهلين وغير المتأهل كالمعدوم قوله : وإن أمنه (لا أي إن أمن الحيف لم يكره واحد من ذلك لأنه أهل للنظر في الدليل وأما مثلنا فلا يجوز له العدول عن قول الإمام أصلاً. قوله : (إلا أن كان السلطان يمكنه أن يفضل الخصومات إلخ) قال الرملي : هذا صريح في أن السلطان أن يقضي بين الخصمين وبه صرح في الفواكه البدرية حيث قال الحاكم إما الإمام أو القاضي أو المحكم، أما الإمام فقد قال علماؤنا : حكم السلطان العادل ينفذ واختلفوا في المرأة فيما سوى الحدود والقصاص اهـ. وسيأتي في الشرح قوله وتقضي المرأة في غير حد وقود» أنها تصلح للسلطنة وفي الخلاصة جنس آخر. وفي النوازل السلطان إذا حكم بين اثنين لا ينفذ. وفي أدب القاضي للخصاف : ينفذ وهو الأصح . وقال القاضي الإمام وهذا أصح وبه يفتي اهـ؛ ذكره في الفصل الرابع من كتاب القضاء. فظهر ضعف الرواية التي نقلها ابن حجر عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى قوله : (الظاهر جواز جبره يخالفه ما في الاختيار حيث قال : ومن تعين له يفترض عليه ولو امتع لا
From the Book of Qada. And in Manaqib al-Kardari, Ibn al-Mubarak said: He was asked, 'When is it permissible for a man to give fatwa and assume judgeship?' He said: 'When he is insightful in hadith and opinion, knowledgeable of Abu Hanifa's saying, and has memorized it.' This is carried upon one of the two narrations from our companions before the settling of the schools. As for after the stabilization, there is no need for it because he can do taqlid. End. And it is surprising what I heard from some Hanafis of our time when I spoke with him about it: he said, 'When the mashayikh gave fatwa on something, we know it is the saying of the Imam.' I said, 'That is a mistake because they state the saying of the Imam in zahir al-riwaya, then they say the fatwa is upon the saying of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, or Zufar.' And I heard from some of them that they say, 'All are from Abu Hanifa.' I said, 'Yes, but what has come out of zahir al-riwaya is retracted, because they established in usul that it is impossible for a mujtahid to issue two different equal sayings, and the retracted one is no longer a saying of his, as they mentioned.' His saying: 'And taqlid is disliked for one who fears injustice, so that it does not become a means to directly committing oppression. Here there are two copies: taqlid meaning appointment by the sultan, and taqlid meaning acceptance of the appointment to judgeship, and the first is intended. Al-Hayf means tyranny and oppression; from hafa 'alayhi yahifu if he oppresses. And fear of not establishing justice due to inability is like fear of oppression. If the author had said 'for one who fears injustice or inability' it would be better, because one of them is sufficient; al-Quduri stated this. And what is meant by karahah is karahah tahrimi, because the outcome is falling into its prohibition then. And the place of karahah is when it is not specifically incumbent upon him. If it becomes restricted to him, it becomes fard 'ayn upon him, and he must restrain himself unless the sultan can settle the disputes and devote himself to that; thus in Fath al-Qadir. And if the sultan cannot settle disputes and there are righteous people in the town, they all sin; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. And I have not seen whether the one who refuses becomes sinful? Apparently yes, due to abandoning the obligation, unless it is said that the refuser usually has an excuse, which prevents sinfulness. And I have not seen whether the one who is the only qualified person can be compelled? Apparently it is permissible to compel him to accept due to people's need for him, like feeding the starving and other communal obligations when specific. Similarly, it is permissible to compel those who are qualified and unqualified, like when there is none. His saying: 'And if he is safe from it' i.e., if he is safe from injustice, none of that is disliked, because he is an expert in looking at evidence. But someone like us may not deviate from the Imam's saying at all. His saying: 'Unless the sultan can settle the disputes, etc.' Al-Ramli said: This is explicit that the sultan can judge between the two litigants, and it is stated explicitly in al-Fawakih al-Badriyya. He said: The ruler is either the imam, the qadi, or the arbitrator. As for the imam, our scholars said: The judgment of the just sultan is enforceable. And they differed regarding women in other than hudud and qisas. End. And it will come in the commentary in the saying: 'And a woman judges in other than hudud and qisas' that she is fit for rulership. And in al-Khulasa there is another type. And in al-Nawazil, if the sultan judges between two, his judgment is not enforceable. And in Adab al-Qadi by al-Khassaf: it is enforceable, and this is the most correct. And the qadi al-Imam said: This is most correct, and fatwa is given accordingly. End. Mentioned in the fourth chapter of the Book of Qada. So the weakness of the narration that Ibn Hajar transmitted from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, is apparent. His saying: 'Apparently it is permissible to compel him' contradicts what is in al-Ikhtiyar, where he said: 'And whoever becomes specifically obligated, it is fard upon him, and if he refuses...' end.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage covers several aspects of judgeship. It begins with a narration from Ibn al-Mubarak on the qualifications of a qadi: being knowledgeable in hadith and fiqh, and knowing Abu Hanifa's madhhab. The author notes this was before the schools stabilized; later, taqlid is sufficient. Then there is a discussion about how some Hanafis mistakenly think that all mashayikh's fatwas are the Imam's saying, but the author clarifies that they sometimes follow other companions. Next, the main ruling: accepting judgeship (taqlid) is disliked with karahah tahrimi if one fears injustice (ḥayf), because it may lead to oppression. The dislike applies when it is not fard 'ayn. If only one qualified person exists, it becomes fard 'ayn, and if he refuses, he is sinful and can be compelled. The author cites Fath al-Qadir and al-Bazzaziyya. Further, if the sultan can personally judge, then others are not obligated. The passage also discusses the enforceability of a sultan's judgment, with a difference of opinion, and the correct view that it is enforceable according to al-Khassaf.

Key Terms
التقليد (al-taqlid): Here it means appointment to judgeship by the sultan, or acceptance of such appointment
الحيف (al-hayf): Injustice, bias, or oppression in judgment
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation that becomes incumbent upon the only qualified person when there is no one else

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does accepting the position of judge (qadi) become fard 'ayn according to the passage?
A) When the sultan directly orders him
B) When he is the only qualified person available and the sultan cannot handle disputes
C) When he is a mujtahid
D) Never; judgeship is always optional

Key Takeaway
Accepting judgeship is disliked only when one fears injustice; it becomes an individual obligation when one is the only qualified person.

The Five Rulings on Accepting Judgeship and Abu Hanifa's Precedent
Commentary on the ruling of accepting judgeship with conditions and categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five Hanafi rulings on accepting judgeship and apply the conditions that determine which ruling applies, including the issue of compulsion and the precedent of Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Accepting judgeship can be fard 'ayn, fard kifayah, makruh tahrimi, haram, or mubah depending on need and ability.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a comprehensive treatment of the ruling on accepting judgeship. The author presents five distinct rulings based on the candidate's circumstances, supported by earlier authorities and illustrated by the famous story of Imam Abu Hanifa's refusal. Understanding these categories is essential for any student of Hanafi fiqh, as judgeship carries immense responsibility and its ruling is highly nuanced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its duality
The term 'taqlid' here means either appointment by the sultan or acceptance of the judgeship. The author clarifies the first meaning. Students must distinguish the two.
Al-Taqleed in this context is the appointment, not acceptance.
2
Understand the concept of 'hayf' and its legal impact
Hayf means injustice or oppression. The ruling of karahah tahrimiyyah applies when one fears hayf or inability, as it leads to potential sin.
The author notes that fear of injustice or inability alone suffices for the disliked ruling.
3
Analyze the five categories
The passage lists: fard 'ayn if exclusive, fard kifayah if others exist, makruh tahrimi if fear of injustice/inability, haram if predominant expectation of oppression, mubah if safe and capable. For the unqualified, it is absolutely haram.
Each ruling is tied to a specific condition.
4
Examine the issue of compulsion and the sultan's role
The author discusses whether a qualified person can be forced to accept judgeship when exclusive. He cites differing views and notes the apparent permissibility of compulsion, though al-Ikhtiyar disagrees.
This reflects an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Learn from Abu Hanifa's precedent
The story of Abu Hanifa's repeated refusal and persecution illustrates the extreme caution of the righteous. The author uses it to support the view that leaving is devotion (azimah) while acceptance is concession (rukhsah).
Abu Hanifa's stance is personal but sheds light on the preferred avoidance.

من كتاب القضاء. وفي مناقب الكردري قال ابن المبارك. وقد سئل متى يحل للرجل أن يفتي ويلي القضاء قال : إذا كان بصيراً بالحديث والرأي عارفاً بقول أبي حنيفة حافظاً له. وهذا محمول على إحدى الروايتين عن أصحابنا وقبل استقرار المذاهب، أما بعد التقرر فلا حاجة إليه لأنه يمكنه التقليد ا.هـ. ومن العجب ما سمعت من بعض حنفية عصرنا حين تكلمت قديماً معه فيها أن قال لما أفتى المشايخ بشيء علمنا أنه قول الإمام فقلت إنه خطأ لأنهم يبينون قول الإمام في ظاهر الرواية ثم يقولون الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف أو محمد أو زفر، وسمعت من بعضهم أنه يقول الكل عن أبي حنيفة . قلت : نعم لكن ما خرج عن ظاهر الرواية فهو مرجوع عنه لما قرروه في الأصول من عدم إمكان صدور قولين مختلفين متساويين من مجتهد والمرجوع عنه لم يبق قولاً له كما ذكروه .
قوله : (وكره التقليد لمن خاف الحيف كيلا يكون ذريعة إلى مباشرة الظلم هنا نسختان التقليد أي النصب من السلطان والتقليد أي قبول تقليد القضاء وهي الأولى . والحيف بمعنى الجور والظلم من حاف عليه يحيف إذا جار وخوف عدم إقامة العدل لعجزه كخوف الجور فلو قال المؤلف لمن خاف الحيف أو العجز لكان أولى لأن أحدهما يكفي؛ نص عليه القدوري والمراد بالكراهة كراهة التحريم لأن الغائب الوقوع في محظوره حينئذ، ومحل الكراهة ما إذا لم يتعين عليه فإن انحصر صار فرض عين عليه وعليه ضبط نفسه إلا أن كان السلطان يمكن أن يفصل الخصومات ويتفرغ لذلك ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وإذا لم يمكن السلطان فصل القضايا وفي البلد قوم صالحون له أثموا كلهم كذا في البزازية. ولم أر هل يفسق الممتنع ؟ الظاهر نعم لتركه الفرض إلا أن يقال : إن للممتنع في الغالب تأويلاً وهو مانع من الفسق ولم أر الآن هل يجبر الممتنع المنحصر فيه؟ الظاهر جواز جبره على القبول لاضطرار الناس إليه كاطعام المضطر وسائر فروض الكفاية عند التعين، وكذا جواز جبر المتأهلين وغير المتأهل كالمعدوم قوله : وإن أمنه (لا أي إن أمن الحيف لم يكره
واحد من ذلك لأنه أهل للنظر في الدليل وأما مثلنا فلا يجوز له العدول عن قول الإمام أصلاً. قوله : (إلا أن كان السلطان يمكنه أن يفضل الخصومات إلخ) قال الرملي : هذا صريح في أن السلطان أن يقضي بين الخصمين وبه صرح في الفواكه البدرية حيث قال الحاكم إما الإمام أو القاضي أو المحكم، أما الإمام فقد قال علماؤنا : حكم السلطان العادل ينفذ واختلفوا في المرأة فيما سوى الحدود والقصاص اهـ. وسيأتي في الشرح قوله وتقضي المرأة في غير حد وقود» أنها تصلح للسلطنة وفي الخلاصة جنس آخر. وفي النوازل السلطان إذا حكم بين اثنين لا ينفذ. وفي أدب القاضي للخصاف : ينفذ وهو الأصح . وقال القاضي الإمام وهذا أصح وبه يفتي اهـ؛ ذكره في الفصل الرابع من كتاب القضاء. فظهر ضعف الرواية التي نقلها ابن حجر عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى قوله : (الظاهر جواز جبره يخالفه ما في الاختيار حيث قال : ومن تعين له يفترض عليه ولو امتع لا يجير عليه اهـ. قوله : (ولم أر حكم ما لو خاف الجور مع التعين قد ذكر حكمه قريباً عن الفتح حيث قال : التقليد لأن كبار الصحابة والتابعين تقلدوه ولم يتعرض المصنف لكون الدخول فيه عند الأمن رخصة فالأولى تركه أو عزيمة فالأولى الدخول فيه للاختلاف قال في البزازية : وعامة المشايخ على أن التقلد. رخصة والترك عزيمة، وقد دخل في القضاء قوم صالحون وتحامى منه قوم صالحون وترك الدخول أصلح ديناً ودنيا. وفي فتح القدير وإن أمن أبيح رخصة والترك هو العزيمة لأنه وإن أمن فالغالب خطأ ظن من ظن من نفسه الاعتدال فيظهر منه خلافه ا هـ . فالحاصل أنه فرض عين إن تعين وفرض كفاية للمتأهل عند وجود غيره لكن رخصة ومكروه عند خوف العجز أو الحيف وينبغي أن يكون حراماً عند غالب ظنه أنه يجور في الحكم، ومباح وكما قدمناه ففيه الأحكام الخمسة . أما غير الأهل فيحرم عليه الدخول فيه قطعاً، ولم أر حكم ما إذا خاف الجور مع التعين، ومقتضى كلامهم في النكاح أن لا يجوز له القبول تقديماً للمحرم على المبيح وإن كان فرضاً، وقد روي أن أبا حنيفة دعي للقضاء ثلاثة مرات فأبى حتى حبس وجلد كل مرة ثلاثين سوطاً حتى قال له أبو يوسف : لو تقلدت لمنفعة الناس؟ فنظر إليه شبه المغضب فقال : لو أمرت أن أقطع البحر سباحة لكنت أقدر عليه فكأني بك قاضياً ونكس رأسه ولم ينظر إليه بعد. وهذا يدل على كراهة الدخول فيه وهو قول البعض وقدمنا أنه لا يكره للقادر عليه. وظاهر كلام الإمام أنه عرف من نفسه عدم القدرة ولذا لم يقبل، وبه صرح في أنه لا يجوز القبول إلا لمن أجبر عليه ولذا ضرب الإمام أياماً وقيد بضعاً وخمسين وامتنع في الأصح من القبول ومات على الإباء؛ كذا في البزازية .
فتح القدير
وحاصل ما ذكره البزازي في مناقبه روايات: الأولى أن الإمام لما أكرهه المنصور على القضاء وأبى حبسه وضربه ثلاثة أيام ومات في الحبس مبطوناً. الثانية أنه حبس مرتين على القضاء والفتيا ثم أخرج ولزم بيته ومنع من الجلوس للنسا إلى أن مات. الثالثة أنهم لما عجزوا منه قتلوه بالسم. الرابعة أنه طيف به في الأسواق الخامسة أنه لما أحس بالسم سجد فخرجت روحه ساجداً سنة خمسين ومائة . ومن غريب ما ما وقع أنه جيء بجنازته فازدحم الناس فلم يقدروا على دفنه إلا بعد العصر واستمر الناس يصلون عليه على قبره عشرين يوماً وحذر من صلى عليه خمسون ألفاً ثم قال : والجمهور على أنه لم يقبل القضاء وأنه مات بالسم وقيل قبله يومين أو ثلاثة لأجل بر المنصور في يمينه ثم ترك. ثم اعلم أن واقعة المنصور معه الفتنة الثانية للإمام والأولى أكرهه ابن هبيرة والي الكوفة على قضائها وضربه على رأسه حتى انتفخ وجهه وحبسه فرأى النبي له فأمره بإطلاقه وتمامه فيها. ولم يذكر الشارحون المولى للقضاة وظاهر كلامهم أنه الخليفة أو السلطان وعند الإمام الثاني الأمير الذي ولاه
From the Book of Judiciary. And in Manaqib al-Kardari, Ibn al-Mubarak said: He was asked when it is permissible for a man to give fatwa and assume judgeship. He said: When he is insightful in hadith and opinion, knowledgeable of Abu Hanifa's statement, and has memorized it. This is carried on one of the two narrations from our companions and before the establishment of the schools; after establishment there is no need for it because he can follow (taqlid). End quote. And amazing is what I heard from some Hanafis of our time when I spoke with him earlier: He said that when the shaykhs gave a fatwa on something, we knew it is the Imam's statement. I said it is wrong because they explain the Imam's statement in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) then say the fatwa is on the statement of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, or Zafar. And I heard some say it is all from Abu Hanifa. I said: Yes, but what departs from the apparent narration is retracted from because of what they established in usul: it is impossible for a mujtahid to issue two different and equal statements, and the retracted one is no longer his statement as they mentioned. 
His statement: (And it is disliked (makruh) for one who fears injustice (al-hayf) to accept judgeship so that it not be a means to directly oppress. There are two versions of 'taqlid': taqlid meaning appointment by the sultan, and taqlid meaning acceptance of the judgeship, and the first is intended. Al-Hayf means oppression and injustice from 'hafa' 'alayhi yahifu' when he oppresses. And fear of not establishing justice due to inability is like fear of injustice. So if the author said 'for one who fears injustice or inability' it would be better because one of them suffices; al-Quduri stated it. And what is meant by disapproval is disapproval of prohibition (karahah tahrimiyyah) because it leads to falling into its prohibition then. The place of disapproval is when it is not incumbent upon him; if it becomes exclusive (munhasir) then it becomes a personal obligation (fard 'ayn) upon him, and he must control himself unless the sultan can resolve disputes and devote himself to that; thus in Fath al-Qadir. And if the sultan cannot resolve cases, and in the city there are righteous people for it, they all sin; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. And I have not seen whether the abstainer becomes sinful? Apparently yes for leaving the obligation, unless it is said that the abstainer usually has an interpretation that prevents sinfulness. And I have not seen now whether the abstainer who is the only one can be forced? Apparently it is permissible to force him to accept due to people's necessity, like feeding the starving and other communal obligations when they become specific. Likewise, forcing the qualified and non-qualified like the non-existent. 
His statement: (And if he feels safe) meaning if he feels safe from injustice, it is not disliked for one who is qualified to examine the evidence. But for someone like us, it is not permissible to deviate from the Imam's statement at all. His statement: (Unless the sultan can differentiate the disputes etc.) al-Ramli said: This is explicit that the sultan can judge between litigants, and it is stated in al-Fawa'ih al-Badriyyah: The ruler is either the Imam, the judge, or the arbitrator. As for the Imam, our scholars said: The judgment of a just sultan is executed, and they differed regarding a woman in matters other than hudud and qisas. End quote. And in the commentary will come his statement: 'A woman judges in other than hudud and qisas' that she is suitable for sultanate. And in al-Khulasa there is another type. In al-Nawazil: If the sultan judges between two, it is not executed. In Adab al-Qadi by al-Khassaf: It is executed and that is the most correct. Al-Qadi al-Imam said: This is more correct and by it fatwa is given; end quote; mentioned in the fourth chapter of the Book of Judiciary. So the weakness of the narration transmitted by Ibn Hajar from Abu Hanifa appears. His statement: (Apparently it is permissible to force him) contradicts what is in al-Ikhtiyar where it says: For whom it becomes specific, it is obligatory upon him, and if he refuses he is not forced. End quote. His statement: (And I have not seen the ruling on one who fears injustice with specification) Its ruling has been mentioned recently from al-Fath where he said: Acceptance (taqlid) because the great Companions and Followers accepted it, and the author did not address whether entering into it when safe is a concession (rukhsah) so the better is to leave it, or an act of devotion so the better is enter it, due to difference. Al-Bazzaziyyah said: The majority of shaykhs hold that acceptance is a concession and leaving is devotion. Righteous people have entered into judgeship and righteous people have refrained from it, and leaving is better for religion and worldly life. In Fath al-Qadir: And if safe, it is permissible as a concession and leaving is devotion because even if safe, mostly the one who thinks himself moderate is mistaken and the opposite appears. End quote. Therefore, it is fard 'ayn if specific, and fard kifayah for the qualified when others exist, but it is a concession and disliked when fear of inability or injustice, and it should be haram when he predominantly thinks he will oppress in judgment, and mubah as we presented; so it has the five rulings. As for the unqualified, entering it is absolutely haram. And I have not seen the ruling if one fears injustice with specification, and the implication of their words in marriage is that it is not permissible for him to accept, giving precedence to the prohibited over the permissible even if it is fard. It has been narrated that Abu Hanifa was called for judgeship three times and refused until he was imprisoned and flogged each time with thirty lashes, until Abu Yusuf said to him: Would you accept for the benefit of the people? He looked at him in anger and said: If I were commanded to cut the sea by swimming, I would be able to do it. It is as if I see you as a judge. He lowered his head and did not look at him after. This indicates the disapproval of entering it, which is the statement of some, and we have stated that it is not disliked for the capable. Apparently the Imam's statement shows he recognized his own inability and thus did not accept, and it is stated that acceptance is only permissible for one who is forced. Thus the Imam was beaten for days and tied for fifty-something, and in the most correct view he refrained from acceptance and died in refusal; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. 
Fath al-Qadir 
Summary of what al-Bazzazi mentioned in his Manaqib: Narrations: First: The Imam was forced by al-Mansur to judgeship and refused, so he imprisoned and beat him for three days and he died in prison from colic (mabtun). Second: He was imprisoned twice for judgeship and fatwa, then released, confined to his house, and prevented from sitting for teaching until he died. Third: When they were unable [to force him], they killed him by poison. Fourth: He was paraded in the markets. Fifth: When he sensed the poison, he prostrated and his soul left while in prostration in the year 150 AH. Among the strange occurrences: his funeral was brought, people crowded, they could not bury him except after Asr, and people continued to pray over his grave for twenty days, and it was said that fifty thousand prayed over him. Then he said: The majority hold that he did not accept judgeship and that he died by poison, and it was said that he accepted two or three days before due to al-Mansur's oath, then left. Then know that the incident of al-Mansur with him was the second trial for the Imam; the first: Ibn Hubayra, the governor of Kufa, forced him to judge and beat his head until his face swelled and imprisoned him, then he saw the Prophet who ordered him to release him; the full account is in it. And the commentators did not mention the master of judges; apparently their words indicate it is the caliph or sultan, and according to the Second Imam, it is the prince who appoints him.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This commentary from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the ruling of accepting judgeship. The passage begins with a discussion of the qualifications for a judge: the statement from Ibn al-Mubarak emphasizes that a judge must be knowledgeable in hadith and legal opinion (ra'y) and well-versed in Abu Hanifa's positions. The author clarifies that this was before the establishment of the madhhab; after the madhhab was settled, the judge need only follow (taqlid) the established rulings. A side note corrects a misconception: some later Hanafis mistook fatwas from later scholars as necessarily being the Imam's own view, but in reality, the scholars differentiate between the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) and the relied-upon fatwa which may follow Abu Yusuf or Muhammad. 

The core ruling is that accepting judgeship is disliked (makruh tahrimi) for one who fears he might be unjust or unable to fulfill the duties, because it becomes a means to oppression. However, if no one else is qualified and the need is exclusive to him, it becomes an individual obligation (fard 'ayn). The author discusses the nuances: if the sultan can handle the cases, the obligation is lifted; if there are multiple qualified people, it is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) and each sins if they all refrain. The text also addresses whether the abstainer becomes sinful (apparently yes if it is fard 'ayn, but there may be valid reasons). Force is permissible to compel the qualified person when necessary, like feeding one who is starving. 

The author then presents the five legal rulings on entering judgeship based on one's state: (1) fard 'ayn if exclusive, (2) fard kifayah if others exist, (3) makruh tahrimi if one fears injustice or inability, (4) haram if one predominantly expects to oppress, (5) mubah if one is safe from these and capable. For the unqualified, it is absolutely haram. 

The passage includes the famous story of Abu Hanifa's refusal to become a judge despite severe punishment by the caliph al-Mansur, illustrating his extreme caution. The author presents multiple narrations of Abu Hanifa's persecution and death, concluding that the majority held he never accepted judgeship and died by poison. This historical evidence supports the ruling that accepting judgeship is a serious matter and is avoided by the righteous, although it is permissible for the capable under safe conditions. The commentary ends by noting that the commentators did not specify the 'master of judges' (al-mawla li al-qudat) but it is understood to be the caliph or sultan.

Key Terms
التقليد (al-taqleed): Acceptance of the position of judge or appointment by the sultan
الحيف (al-hayf): Injustice and oppression in judgment
كراهة التحريم (karahah al-tahrim): Disapproval that is tantamount to prohibition; it means the act is prohibited but not as severely as haram
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): Personal obligation incumbent upon every qualified individual

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, when does accepting judgeship become makruh tahrimi?
A) When the person is qualified and there are others available
B) When the person fears he will commit injustice or is unable to fulfill the duties
C) When the person knows he will judge justly
D) When the sultan forces the person

Key Takeaway
Accepting judgeship in the Hanafi school carries five possible rulings depending on the candidate's circumstances, with fear of injustice triggering makruh tahrimi and exclusive need triggering fard 'ayn.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
6 min
The Five Rulings on Entering the Judiciary
Presents the five Shar'i categories for accepting the position of qadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five Shar'i rulings for accepting the position of qadi and identify which ruling applies based on the individual's circumstances and self-assessment.

Core Idea
The ruling on becoming a judge depends on your qualification, need, and fear of injustice — it can range from fard ayn to haram.

The judiciary is a weighty responsibility. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that there is no single ruling for accepting the position of qadi. Instead, it can be any of the five Shar'i categories depending on the person's situation: whether they are uniquely qualified, whether others can serve, whether they fear inability or injustice, or whether they feel safe. Understanding this spectrum prevents both reckless eagerness and blanket avoidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act under consideration is accepting the appointment (taqlid) as a qadi (judge).
Taqlid here means appointment, not the usul term.
2
List the five situations
The passage enumerates five distinct scenarios: unique qualification, presence of other qualified persons, fear of inability/injustice, certainty of injustice, and safety with ability.
These correspond to the five ahkam.
3
Assign the ruling to each
Map each situation: no other qualified person → fard ayn; others exist → fard kifayah; fear of inability → makruh/concession; certainty of injustice → haram; safety with ability → mubah (concession).
The majority view is that entering is a concession, not a determination.
4
Understand rukhsa vs azima
The passage highlights a scholarly disagreement: is entering the judiciary a concession (rukhsa) or a determination (azima)? The later consensus is that it is a concession, meaning leaving it is generally better.
This affects the moral weight but not the legal categories.
5
Apply the framework
A person must self-assess: Is he truly qualified? Is he needed? Can he be just? The answer determines the ruling.
Self-delusion is warned against: one often thinks himself just but is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القضاء
التقليد لأن كبار الصحابة والتابعين تقلدوه ولم يتعرض المصنف لكون الدخول فيه عند الأمن رخصة فالأولى تركه أو عزيمة فالأولى الدخول فيه للاختلاف قال في البزازية : وعامة المشايخ على أن التقلد. رخصة والترك عزيمة، وقد دخل في القضاء قوم صالحون وتحامى منه قوم صالحون وترك الدخول أصلح ديناً ودنيا. وفي فتح القدير وإن أمن أبيح رخصة والترك هو العزيمة لأنه وإن أمن فالغالب خطأ ظن من ظن من نفسه الاعتدال فيظهر منه خلافه ا هـ . فالحاصل أنه فرض عين إن تعين وفرض كفاية للمتأهل عند وجود غيره لكن رخصة ومكروه عند خوف العجز أو الحيف وينبغي أن يكون حراماً عند غالب ظنه أنه يجور في الحكم، ومباح وكما قدمناه ففيه الأحكام الخمسة .
The Book of Judiciary. Appointment because great Companions and Followers accepted it. The author did not address whether entering it when safe is a concession (so leaving is preferable) or a determination (so entering is preferable) due to disagreement. He said in al-Bazzaziyya: The general body of scholars is that appointment is a concession and leaving is determination. Righteous people have entered the judiciary and righteous people have avoided it, and leaving it is more beneficial for religion and worldly affairs. In Fath al-Qadir: If one is safe, it is permissible as a concession, and leaving is the determination because even if one is safe, mostly the one who thinks himself balanced is mistaken, and the opposite appears from him. The conclusion: it is fard ayn if it becomes specific to one person, and fard kifayah for the qualified person when others exist, but it is a concession and disliked when one fears inability or tyranny, and it should be haram when one predominantly thinks he will be unjust in judgment, and permissible as we have mentioned. So it encompasses the five rulings.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage from the sharh lays out the complete spectrum of legal rulings (ahkam khamsa) for accepting the position of a qadi. It begins by noting that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not specify whether entering the judiciary during times of safety is a concession (rukhsa, so leaving is superior) or a determination (azima, so entering is superior). The commentator then cites two sources: al-Bazzaziyya stating that the majority consider appointment a concession and leaving the determination, and Fath al-Qadir affirming that even if one believes himself safe, he is likely mistaken about his own integrity. The key synthesis is: 1) fard ayn if one is uniquely qualified and no one else can serve, 2) fard kifayah for the qualified person when others exist, 3) a concession (rukhsa) and makruh if one fears inability or injustice, 4) haram if one is predominantly certain that he will rule unjustly, and 5) mubah otherwise. This shows that the ruling is not monolithic but depends entirely on the individual's circumstances and self-assessment.

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlīd): Appointment as a judge/judicial office
رخصة (rukhṣa): A concession granted by Shari'ah, where performing an act is permissible but leaving it is superior
عزيمة (ʿazīma): The original, stricter ruling without concession
فرض عين (farḍ ʿayn): An individual obligation incumbent on every qualified person
فرض كفاية (farḍ kifāya): A communal obligation; if some fulfill it, others are absolved
مكروه (makrūh): Disliked; omitting it is preferable but not sinful

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does entering the judiciary become haram?
A) When one is not qualified
B) When one predominantly thinks he will be unjust in judgment
C) When one fears inability
D) When no one else is available

Key Takeaway
The ruling on entering the judiciary is not fixed; it depends on the individual's qualification, need, and self-assessment of his ability to rule justly.

The Absolute Prohibition for the Unqualified Judge
States the prohibition and illustrates with Imam Abu Hanifa's refusal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for an unqualified person regarding judgeship and explain the legal reasoning (talil) derived from the example of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
For the unqualified, judgeship is haram; even the qualified may refuse if they fear inability.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on who may accept the role of a judge (qadi). It clarifies the absolute prohibition for the unqualified and the nuanced position for the qualified, drawing on the powerful example of Imam Abu Hanifa's refusal even under torture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for the unqualified
From the opening sentence, determine the hukm for ghayr al-ahl accepting judgeship. Note the word 'absolutely prohibited'.
The ruling is haram, not merely makruh.
2
Understand the exception for the qualified
The author states that for one who is capable (qadir), judgeship is not disliked. This shows a distinction.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists: some say it is makruh for the capable.
3
Analyze the analogy from marriage
The author draws an analogy: just as a man who fears injustice must refuse a marriage request even if it becomes fard, similarly a person who fears injustice in judgement must refuse even if appointed.
This is a qiyas based on the same illa: fear of injustice.
4
Interpret the story of Imam Abu Hanifa
The passage narrates that Imam Abu Hanifa refused judgeship three times, was flogged and imprisoned, and died refusing. This shows that even under duress, acceptance is not permissible when one is unqualified or fears inability.
His response to Abu Yusuf indicates he knew his own inability.
5
Derive the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
From the text and the Imam's practice, the mufta bihi is: judgeship is haram for the unqualified; for the qualified, it is not disliked if they feel capable. Acceptance is only allowed if forced, but even then the Imam refused, showing preference for avoidance.
This is based on al-Bazzaziyya and later fatwa works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما غير الأهل فيحرم عليه الدخول فيه قطعاً، ولم أر حكم ما إذا خاف الجور مع التعين، ومقتضى كلامهم في النكاح أن لا يجوز له القبول تقديماً للمحرم على المبيح وإن كان فرضاً، وقد روي أن أبا حنيفة دعي للقضاء ثلاثة مرات فأبى حتى حبس وجلد كل مرة ثلاثين سوطاً حتى قال له أبو يوسف : لو تقلدت لمنفعة الناس؟ فنظر إليه شبه المغضب فقال : لو أمرت أن أقطع البحر سباحة لكنت أقدر عليه فكأني بك قاضياً ونكس رأسه ولم ينظر إليه بعد. وهذا يدل على كراهة الدخول فيه وهو قول البعض وقدمنا أنه لا يكره للقادر عليه. وظاهر كلام الإمام أنه عرف من نفسه عدم القدرة ولذا لم يقبل، وبه صرح في أنه لا يجوز القبول إلا لمن أجبر عليه ولذا ضرب الإمام أياماً وقيد بضعاً وخمسين وامتنع في الأصح من القبول ومات على الإباء؛ كذا في البزازية .
As for the unqualified, entering it is absolutely prohibited. I have not seen the ruling for when he fears injustice despite being uniquely needed. The implication of their words in the chapter on marriage is that he may not accept, giving precedence to the prohibited over the permissible even if it is obligatory. It has been narrated that Abu Hanifa was called to the judiciary three times and refused until he was imprisoned and flogged each time thirty lashes, until Abu Yusuf said to him: 'If you accepted for the benefit of the people?' He looked at him with anger and said: 'If I were ordered to cross the sea by swimming, I would be able to do it. It is as if I see you as a judge.' He lowered his head and did not look at him afterwards. This indicates the dislike of entering it, and that is the view of some. We have already stated that it is not disliked for one who is capable. The apparent meaning of the Imam's words is that he knew from himself a lack of ability, and therefore did not accept. He explicitly stated that acceptance is not permissible except for one who is forced. For this reason, the Imam was beaten for days and shackled for fifty-something, and he refrained from acceptance according to the most correct view, and died in refusal. So in al-Bazzaziyya.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for someone who is not qualified (ghayr ahl) to be a judge: it is absolutely haram. The author then notes a lacuna: he has not encountered a ruling for someone who fears he will be unjust but is uniquely required. He analogizes from nikah: if a woman asks for marriage and the man fears he cannot fulfill rights, he must refuse even if it is fard to marry if needed. Then the passage recounts the famous episode of Imam Abu Hanifa being forced to accept judgeship by the caliph. He refused and was tortured. His response to Abu Yusuf indicates that he considered himself incapable and that acceptance is not permissible even if forced. The passage concludes that the Imam died in refusal. This serves as a practical illustration: the unqualified must refuse, and even a qualified person may refuse if he fears inability.

Key Terms
غير الأهل (ghayr al-ahl): One who is not qualified or fit for the judiciary

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Imam Abu Hanifa do when called to the judiciary three times?
A) He accepted after being forced
B) He refused and was flogged and imprisoned
C) He accepted for the benefit of the people
D) He accepted but then resigned

Key Takeaway
For the unqualified, accepting judgeship is absolutely haram; even under compulsion, refusal is obligatory as demonstrated by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Conditions for Valid Appointment of a Judge by the Ruler
Details conditions for valid judge appointment by sultan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid appointment of a judge by the sultan and identify which conditions, if missing, render the appointment invalid.

Core Idea
A judge's appointment is valid only if the appointer is of age, designates the judge specifically, and uses a proper method.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the formal requirements for appointing a judge. While the sultan has broad authority, several conditions must be met for the appointment to be legally sound. Understanding these conditions helps distinguish valid from invalid judicial appointments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the appointing authority's scope
Determine whether the sultan or amir was given full authority over the region, including the power to appoint and dismiss judges. If only fiscal authority was given, they cannot appoint judges.
The passage distinguishes between a governor with full authority and one with limited mandate.
2
Check the appointer's eligibility
The appointer must have reached puberty. If the sultan is a minor, the appointment must be done through a governor acting as deputy, and the minor’s appointment becomes real only upon reaching puberty.
If a minor sultan reaches puberty, a new appointment is needed for the judges.
3
Ensure specific designation of the judge
The appointment must name a specific person. Vague phrases like 'I appointed a scholar' or 'one of these two' are invalid.
The passage emphasizes that general terms do not create a valid appointment.
4
Verify the method of appointment
Acceptable methods include direct verbal communication (mushafaha), sending a trustworthy messenger, or sending a letter. However, some scholars considered appointments by letter invalid if the appointer does not directly address the appointee.
The validity of letter-based appointments is debated; direct speech is the clearest.
5
Understand the role of acceptance
The appointee's acceptance is not a condition for validity, but he must not have rejected the appointment. If he rejects and then accepts, it is only valid if the rejection had not yet reached the appointer at the time of acceptance.
This rule mirrors agency (wakala) in Hanafi law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السلطان ناحية وجعل له خراجها وأطلق له التصرف في الرعية وما تقتضيه الإمارة له أن يقلد ويعزل بخلاف ما إذا فوض إليه الأموال فقط. وعنه أيضاً إذا كان القضاء من الأصل ومات القاضي ليس للأمير أن ينصب قاضياً وإن ولى عشرها وخراجها وإن حكم الأمير لم يجز حكمه فإذا جاء هذا المولى بكتاب الخليفة إليه من الأصل لا يكون امضاء لقضائه؛ كذا في البزازية. وللسلطان أن يفوض التولية للقضاء إلى غيره ولو كان المفوض إليه عبداً بطريق النيابة بخلاف ما إذا حكم العبد بنفسه لم يصح. ويشترط للسلطان المولى للقضاة البلوغ لما في البزازية : مات السلطان واتفقت الرعية على سلطنة ابن صغير له ينبغي أن يفوض أمور التقليد إلى والي ويعد هذا الوالي نفسه تبعاً لابن السلطان لشرفه والسلطان في الرسم هو الابن وفي الحقيقة هو الوالي لعدم صحة الإذن والجمعة لا ولاية له ا هـ. وفيها أيضاً: السلطان أو الوالي إذا بلغ يحتاج إلى تقليد جديد وكذا النصراني إذا استؤمر وفي العبد روايتان. ولو اجتمع أهل بلدة على تولية واحد القضاء لم يصح بخلاف ما إذا ولو لسلطاناً بعد موت سلطانهم فإنه يجوز. منها أيضاً ولا بد في صحة التولية من تعيين القاضي، فلو قال السلطان وليت عالماً أو أحد هذين أو فلاناً وفلاناً لم يصح أخذاً مما في البزازية : لو قال السلطان للوالي قلد من ، ولو قال قلد أحداً لم يصح كقوله لوكيله وكل من يصح، يصح وكل أحد لا شئت والتولية للقاضي إما بالمشافهة للقاضي بقوله وليتك قضاء بلدة كذا أو جعلتك قاضي القضاة ونحو ذلك، أو بإرسال ثقة إليه بذلك أو بكتاب. وفي البزازية : كان الفقيه أبو جعفر يقول : كان الفقيه أبو بكر الاسكاف يقول : تولية القضاء في ديارنا غير صحيح لأن المولى لا يواجههم بالتقليد وإنما يكتب المنشور ويكتب في كل فصل عادة من تقدم إن شاء الله تعالى فيبطل المقدم ولو محاه بعده لا ينقلب صحيحاً كما لو كتب أنت طالق إن شاء الله تعالى ثم محى المبطل لا يقع الطلاق ا.هـ. ولا يشترط لصحة التولية قبوله لها وإنما يشترط عدم رده بشرط بلوغه الرد كالوكالة لما في البزازية : السلطان إذا قلده القضاء فرده مشافهة ثم قبل لا يصح، وإن بعث إليه منشوراً أو أرسل إليه فرده ثم قبل إن قبل قبل بلوغ الرد إلى السلطان بعد بلوغ الرد إليه، وكذا الوكيل برد الوكالة ثم يقبل، وكذا إذا كتبت المرأة إلى رجل زوجت نفسي منك فبلغ الكتاب إليه فرده ثم قبل والرسالة كالكتابة ا هـ .
The sultan of a region, if he has appointed its land tax and granted him authority over the subjects and what the governorship requires, he has the right to appoint and dismiss, unlike when only funds are entrusted to him. It is also reported: if the judiciary is from the origin and the judge dies, the amir does not have the right to appoint a judge, even if he has control over its tenth and land tax; if the amir judges, his judgment is not valid. If this appointing authority brings a letter from the caliph from the origin, it does not confirm his judgment. So in al-Bazzaziyya. The sultan may delegate the appointment of judges to another, even if the delegate is a slave, by way of deputyship, unlike if the slave judges himself, it is not valid. It is a condition for the sultan who appoints judges to have reached puberty. In al-Bazzaziyya: if the sultan dies and the subjects agree on the sultanate of his young son, it is appropriate to delegate the matters of appointment to a governor, and this governor considers himself a subordinate to the sultan's son for his honor; the sultan in form is the son, but in reality the governor, because the son's permission is not valid, and Friday prayer he has no authority. Also: the sultan or governor, if he reaches puberty, needs a new appointment; similarly for a Christian if he is appointed; and for a slave there are two narrations. If the people of a town agree to appoint one person as judge, it is not valid, unlike if they appoint a sultan after the death of their sultan, it is permissible. Also: the appointment requires specific designation of the judge. If the sultan says 'I appointed a scholar' or 'one of these two' or 'so-and-so and so-and-so', it is not valid, based on what is in al-Bazzaziyya: If the sultan says to the governor 'Appoint who you want', it is valid; if he says 'Appoint someone', it is not valid, like his saying to his agent 'Appoint who is correct, appoint anyone you wish'. The appointment of a judge is either by directly speaking to the judge saying 'I appoint you to the judgeship of such town' or 'I made you chief judge' and similar, or by sending a trustworthy person with that, or by a letter. In al-Bazzaziyya: Abu Ja'far said: Abu Bakr al-Isakaf used to say: Appointment of judges in our lands is invalid because the appointing authority does not face them with the appointment, rather he writes a document and writes in each section habitually 'from the one who preceded, God willing', so the preceding one is annulled; if he erases it afterwards, it does not become valid, just as if he writes 'You are divorced, God willing' then erases the annulling phrase, the divorce does not occur. The acceptance by the appointee is not a condition for the validity of the appointment; rather, what is required is that he does not reject it, provided the rejection reaches him, like agency. In al-Bazzaziyya: If the sultan appoints him as judge and he rejects it verbally, then accepts, it is not valid. If he sends a document or a messenger and he rejects it, then accepts before the rejection reaches the sultan, it is valid after the rejection reaches him. Similarly, the agent retracts the agency and then accepts; similarly if a woman writes to a man 'I have married myself to you', and the letter reaches him and he rejects it, then accepts, and the message is like writing.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for a valid appointment of a judge by the ruling authority (sultan or amir). It covers: (1) The authority of a sultan or governor who has been given full control over a region can appoint and dismiss judges, unlike one with limited mandate. (2) If the original judge dies, the local amir cannot appoint a replacement unless the caliph's letter confirms it. (3) The sultan may delegate the appointment to another, even a slave, as a deputy. (4) The appointing authority must be of age. If the sultan is a minor, his father or a governor does the appointment. (5) If a minor ruler reaches puberty, a new appointment is needed. (6) Appointment requires specific designation of the judge; general phrases like 'a scholar' are invalid. (7) The method can be verbal, via messenger, or by letter. (8) The validity of the appointment does not require the judge's immediate acceptance, but he must not reject it before the appointment is finalized (similar to agency). If he rejects and then accepts before the rejection reaches the sultan, it is valid; after it reaches, it is not. (9) The passage also cites a view that local appointments via letter are invalid due to the absence of direct address.

Key Terms
تولية القضاء (tawliyat al-qaḍā): The act of appointing a judge
مشافهة (mushāfaha): Direct verbal communication, face-to-face
تقليد (taqlīd): Appointment to a judicial position
منشور (manshūr): Official document or decree of appointment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the sultan says 'I appointed a scholar' without naming anyone, the appointment is:
A) Valid
B) Invalid
C) Valid if the scholar is identified later
D) Valid only if it is a verbal appointment

Key Takeaway
A judge's appointment requires the appointer to have full authority, be of age, name the judge specifically, use a clear method, and ensure the judge does not effectively reject the appointment.

Powers of a Judge Upon Appointment
Enumerates the powers of a judge after valid appointment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four judicial powers acquired by a qadi upon valid appointment and explain the conditions for exercising each.

Core Idea
A judge's authority to judge, imprison, and punish derives from his appointment, not from the parties.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies exactly what powers a qadi gains when appointed. The author collected these from scattered Hanafi sources. Understanding these powers is crucial for any aspiring judge to know the limits of his authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first power: judgment based on evidence
The qadi may issue a judgment when the plaintiff produces valid evidence (bayyina), or the defendant confesses (iqrar), or the defendant refuses to take an oath (nukul) after the plaintiff has no evidence. This is after fulfilling all legal conditions.
Bayyina normally means two male witnesses. Iqrar is a single confession. Nukul leads to judgment against the defendant.
2
Identify the second power: imprisonment for non-payment
The qadi may imprison a person who refuses to pay a proven debt or right after it has been established.
This is a coercive measure, not a punishment.
3
Identify the third power: discretionary punishment (ta'zir)
The qadi can administer ta'zir for offenses that are rights of Allah (e.g., moral crimes) without any request, and for rights of individuals only upon the victim's request.
Imprisonment can be a form of ta'zir.
4
Note the final remark on fard ayn
The passage ends with a note that the earlier discussion on karaha (dislike) applies when the duty is not exclusive; if it becomes exclusive, it becomes fard ayn. This is a separate point about the judge's own obligation.
This is not a power but a ruling on the judge's duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم أر لأصحابنا مجموعاً ما يستفيده القاضي بالتولية وقد جمعته من مواضعة فيملك الحكم الثابت ببينة أو إقراراً ونكول عن اليمين بعد استيفاء الشرائط الشرعية للحكم، ويملك حبس الممتنع عن أداء الحق، ومن وجب عليه تعزير ورأى حبسه لقولهم إنه مفوض إلى رأيه، ويملك إقامة التعازير ما كان حقاً الله تعالى بلا طلب أحد وما كان حق عبد بطلبه، ويملك
قال : ومحل الكراهة ما إذا يتعين عليه فإذا انحصر صار فرض عين عليه وعليه ضبط نفسه الخ. على
I have not seen for our companions a compilation of what the judge attains by appointment. I have collected it from various places: he possesses the power to issue judgment proven by evidence (bayyina) or confession (iqrar) or refusal to take an oath (nukul) after fulfilling the legal conditions for judgment. He possesses the power to imprison the one who refuses to pay a right. And for one upon whom a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) is obligatory, if he sees imprisonment as appropriate, because they said it is delegated to his opinion. He possesses the power to administer ta'zir punishments for what is a right of Allah without anyone's request, and for what is a right of a servant upon his request. He possesses... He said: The place of dislike (karaha) is when it becomes specific to him; if it is exclusive, it becomes fard ayn upon him, and he must restrain himself, etc. etc.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage outlines the judicial powers that a properly appointed judge acquires. These include: (1) The authority to adjudicate based on evidence (bayyina), confessions (iqrar), or refusal to take an oath (nukul) after verifying legal conditions. (2) The power to imprison a person who refuses to fulfill a financial obligation after it has been proven. (3) The authority to impose discretionary punishments (ta'zir) for offenses, both those that are rights of Allah (e.g., moral crimes) and rights of individuals, but the latter requires the individual's request. Imprisonment is one form of ta'zir. The passage ends with a remark that the earlier discussion about karaha (dislike) applies when the duty is not exclusive; when it becomes exclusive, it becomes fard ayn. This is a reminder of the earlier five-fold ruling.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyina): Legal evidence, usually two male witnesses or one male and two females
إقرار (iqrār): Confession or admission of a right against oneself
نكول (nukūl): Refusal to take an oath by the defendant after the plaintiff has no evidence
تعزير (taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment for offenses not covered by fixed penalties (hudud) or prescribed retribution (qisas)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a power that the judge attains upon appointment according to the passage?
A) The power to legislate new laws
B) The power to imprison a person who refuses to pay a proven debt
C) The power to judge without any evidence
D) The power to delegate all authority to a deputy

Key Takeaway
Upon valid appointment, a qadi gains authority to judge based on evidence/confession/oath refusal, imprison for non-payment, and impose ta'zir, with a key distinction between rights of Allah and individuals.

Appointment of Judges: Conditions, Methods, and Legal Effects
Rulings on the authority to appoint judges, conditions, and methods of appointment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a valid judicial appointment (tawliyah al-qada) and distinguish between valid and invalid methods of appointment.

Core Idea
A judge's appointment is valid only if the appointer has authority, the appointee is specifically named, and the appointment is communicated clearly — acceptance is not required.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the legal framework for appointing judges in the Hanafi school. It covers who has the power to appoint, what makes an appointment valid, and how rejection affects the process. The rulings are derived from later fatwa works like al-Bazzaziyya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the appointer's authority
Distinguish between delegation of full governance (wilayah 'ammah) and only fiscal authority. Only the former empowers the appointee to appoint judges.
The sultan may delegate appointment to another, even a slave, but only by way of deputyship.
2
Determine the requirement of specification (ta'yin)
The judge must be specifically named. Vague designations like 'a scholar' or 'one of these two' invalidate the appointment.
Analogy: like agency, vague authorization is invalid.
3
Analyze methods of appointment
Appointment is valid via direct oral communication, sending a trustworthy messenger, or a written letter. All are considered clear communication.
Oral is preferred (mushafahah) but not required.
4
Examine the role of rejection
Acceptance by the judge is not required. The appointment is valid unless the judge explicitly rejects it, and the rejection must reach the appointer to take effect.
This follows the analogy of agency (wakalah).
5
Consider special cases
A minor sultan cannot directly appoint; a regent must do so. A slave as appointer has two narrations. Communal appointment by townspeople is invalid unless appointing a sultan after a sultan's death.
The problematic custom of conditional appointment (with 'if Allah wills') is also discussed; erasing the condition does not cure the defect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القضاء
السلطان ناحية وجعل له خراجها وأطلق له التصرف في الرعية وما تقتضيه الإمارة له أن يقلد ويعزل بخلاف ما إذا فوض إليه الأموال فقط. وعنه أيضاً إذا كان القضاء من الأصل ومات القاضي ليس للأمير أن ينصب قاضياً وإن ولى عشرها وخراجها وإن حكم الأمير لم يجز حكمه فإذا جاء هذا المولى بكتاب الخليفة إليه من الأصل لا يكون امضاء لقضائه؛ كذا في البزازية. وللسلطان أن يفوض التولية للقضاء إلى غيره ولو كان المفوض إليه عبداً بطريق النيابة بخلاف ما إذا حكم العبد بنفسه لم يصح. ويشترط للسلطان المولى للقضاة البلوغ لما في البزازية : مات السلطان واتفقت الرعية على سلطنة ابن صغير له ينبغي أن يفوض أمور التقليد إلى والي ويعد هذا الوالي نفسه تبعاً لابن السلطان لشرفه والسلطان في الرسم هو الابن وفي الحقيقة هو الوالي لعدم صحة الإذن والجمعة لا ولاية له ا هـ. وفيها أيضاً: السلطان أو الوالي إذا بلغ يحتاج إلى تقليد جديد وكذا النصراني إذا استؤمر وفي العبد روايتان. ولو اجتمع أهل بلدة على تولية واحد القضاء لم يصح بخلاف ما إذا ولو لسلطاناً بعد موت سلطانهم فإنه يجوز. منها أيضاً ولا بد في صحة التولية من تعيين القاضي، فلو قال السلطان وليت عالماً أو أحد هذين أو فلاناً وفلاناً لم يصح أخذاً مما في البزازية : لو قال السلطان للوالي قلد من ، ولو قال قلد أحداً لم يصح كقوله لوكيله وكل من يصح، يصح وكل أحد لا شئت والتولية للقاضي إما بالمشافهة للقاضي بقوله وليتك قضاء بلدة كذا أو جعلتك قاضي القضاة ونحو ذلك، أو بإرسال ثقة إليه بذلك أو بكتاب. وفي البزازية : كان الفقيه أبو جعفر يقول : كان الفقيه أبو بكر الاسكاف يقول : تولية القضاء في ديارنا غير صحيح لأن المولى لا يواجههم بالتقليد وإنما يكتب المنشور ويكتب في كل فصل عادة من تقدم إن شاء الله تعالى فيبطل المقدم ولو محاه بعده لا ينقلب صحيحاً كما لو كتب أنت طالق إن شاء الله تعالى ثم محى المبطل لا يقع الطلاق ا.هـ. ولا يشترط لصحة التولية قبوله لها وإنما يشترط عدم رده بشرط بلوغه الرد كالوكالة لما في البزازية : السلطان إذا قلده القضاء فرده مشافهة ثم قبل لا يصح، وإن بعث إليه منشوراً أو أرسل إليه فرده ثم قبل إن قبل قبل بلوغ الرد إلى السلطان بعد بلوغ الرد إليه، وكذا الوكيل برد الوكالة ثم يقبل، وكذا إذا كتبت المرأة [؟] شئت [؟] اهـ. يصح القبول لا إلى رجل زوجت نفسي منك فبلغ الكتاب إليه فرده ثم قبل والرسالة كالكتابة ا هـ
Book of judiciary. The sultan [appoints] a governor and gives him its land tax and allows him to dispose over the subjects and what the emirate requires: he may appoint and dismiss, contrary to if he only delegated to him the funds. And also from him: if the judiciary is from the origin and the judge dies, the emir may not appoint a judge even if he has authority over a tenth of it and its land tax, and if the emir judges, his judgment is not valid. So if this client comes with a book from the caliph to him from the origin, it is not confirmation of his judgment; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. And the sultan may delegate the appointment to the judiciary to someone else, even if the delegate is a slave by way of deputyship, contrary to if the slave judges by himself, it is not valid. And it is required for the sultan who appoints judges to have reached puberty, because in al-Bazzaziyya: if the sultan dies and the subjects agree upon the sultanate of his young son, it is appropriate to delegate the matters of appointment to a governor, and this governor considers himself a follower of the son of the sultan due to his honor, and the sultan in name is the son, but in reality the governor, because the permission is not valid and he has no authority for Friday. And in it also: if the sultan or governor reaches puberty, he needs new appointment; likewise a Christian if he is given authority; and concerning a slave there are two narrations. And if the people of a town gather to appoint one judge, it is not valid, contrary to if they appointed a sultan after the death of their sultan, then it is permissible. And from it: for the validity of appointment it is necessary to specify the judge. If the sultan said 'I appointed a scholar' or 'one of these two' or 'so-and-so and so-and-so', it is not valid, based on what is in al-Bazzaziyya: if the sultan said to the governor 'appoint whoever', and if he said 'appoint one', it is not valid, like his saying to his agent 'appoint whoever is valid, appoint whoever you wish'. And the appointment of a judge is either by direct oral communication to the judge by saying 'I appoint you as judge of such town' or 'I make you judge of judges' and the like, or by sending a trustworthy person to him with that, or by a letter. And in al-Bazzaziyya: al-Faqih Abu Ja'far used to say: al-Faqih Abu Bakr al-Askaf used to say: the appointment of judiciary in our lands is not valid because the appointer does not meet them with appointment; rather he writes the munshur and writes in each section customarily 'from whoever precedes, if Allah wills', so the predecessor becomes invalid, and if he erases it afterwards it does not become valid, like if he wrote 'you are divorced if Allah wills' then erased the 'invalidator', the divorce does not occur. And acceptance by the appointee is not required for the validity of appointment; rather the condition is that he does not reject it, provided his rejection reaches [the appointer], like agency. Because in al-Bazzaziyya: if the sultan appoints him as judge and he rejects it orally, then accepts, it is not valid. And if he sends to him a letter or sends a messenger, and he rejects it, then accepts before the rejection reaches the sultan? No, after the rejection reaches him [it is not valid]. Likewise the agent who rejects agency then accepts. Likewise if a woman wrote to a man 'I married myself to you', and the letter reached him and he rejected it, then accepted, and the message is like the writing.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on the appointment (tawliyah) of judges from the Hanafi perspective. It begins by distinguishing the scope of authority: if a sultan delegates full governance, the appointee may appoint judges; if only funds, he may not. A key principle: appointment of a judge requires clear specification (ta'yin). Vague designations like 'a scholar' or 'one of these two' are invalid. The method can be oral, by messenger, or by written letter. Importantly, acceptance by the judge is not a condition for validity; rather, the appointment is effective unless the judge explicitly rejects it. Rejection must reach the appointer. The passage also discusses the requirement that the sultan himself be an adult, citing a case from al-Bazzaziyya about a minor sultan. Additionally, communal appointment by the people of a town is invalid unless they appoint a sultan after the death of their sultan. The text includes a problematic scenario from the practice of their lands where appointment is done via a written munshur with a condition 'if Allah wills', which, when erased, does not become valid—analogous to a suspended divorce.

Key Terms
تولية (tawliyah): The act of appointing someone to a position, specifically judgeship (qada).
قضاء (qada'): The office of judge; judicial authority.
مشافهة (mushafahah): Oral communication directly between the appointer and the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following makes the appointment of a judge invalid?
A) The sultan says 'I appoint a scholar' without naming anyone.
B) The sultan says 'I appoint you as judge of this town' directly to the person.
C) The sultan writes a letter of appointment and sends it via a trustworthy messenger.
D) The judge does not reject the appointment.

Key Takeaway
A valid judicial appointment in Hanafi law requires a qualified appointer, explicit specification of the judge, clear communication, and no effective rejection by the appointee.
