Powers of the Judge by Appointment
Enumeration of judge's powers with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the powers a judge acquires upon appointment and identify which powers require explicit authorization in the letter of appointment.

Core Idea
A judge's appointment grants several powers, but some require explicit mention in the letter.

The role of a judge extends beyond adjudicating disputes; he also manages affairs of minors, waqf, and punishments. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq compiles the various powers a judge gains by virtue of his appointment, drawing from multiple Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
List the powers
Skim the passage and list all powers mentioned, such as adjudication, imprisonment, ta'zir, hudud, marriage of orphans, delegation, guardianship of property, supervision of waqf, and appointment of executors.
There are 9 distinct powers.
2
Separate conditional from unconditional
Identify which powers are automatic (e.g., adjudication) and which require explicit authorization (e.g., marriage of orphans) or have territorial limits (hudud).
The condition is often stated explicitly in the passage.
3
Analyze the basis of each power
Note that the author collected these from various places; some powers are derived from general principles, others from specific texts like Tahdhib al-Qalanisi.
4
Examine key conditions in detail
For conditional powers, understand the exact requirement: e.g., marriage of orphans needs written mention in the appointment letter; delegation requires explicit permission; hudud only for major cities.
Pay special attention to the phrase 'on condition that it is written in his letter of appointment'.
5
Consider limits and nuances
Note that the judge's authority over waqf cannot be restricted by the founder, and he can intervene in guardianship only if the guardian is neglectful or wasteful.
These nuances prevent overreach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم أر لأصحابنا مجموعاً ما يستفيده القاضي بالتولية وقد جمعته من مواضعة فيملك الحكم الثابت ببينة أو إقراراً ونكول عن اليمين بعد استيفاء الشرائط الشرعية للحكم، ويملك حبس الممتنع عن أداء الحق، ومن وجب عليه تعزير ورأى حبسه لقولهم إنه مفوض إلى رأيه، ويملك إقامة التعازير ما كان حقاً الله تعالى بلا طلب أحد وما كان حق عبد بطلبه، ويملك قال : ومحل الكراهة ما إذا يتعين عليه فإذا انحصر صار فرض عين عليه وعليه ضبط نفسه الخ. على ويملك إقامة الحدود كما صرحوا به في بابها. وفي تهذيب القلانسي أنها إلى الإمام وأمراء الأمصار دون أمراء السواد وعمال الخراج في الرساتيق ا.هـ. ويملك تزويج اليتامى والأيتام حيث لا ولي لهم لكن بشرط أن يكتب في منشوره ذلك، وظاهر كلامهم في باب الأولياء أنه لا يكفي في هذه توليته له قاضي القضاء ويملك الاستخلاف بالإذن الصريح أو بقوله جعلتك قاضي القضاة وإلا فلا يملك ويملك ولاية أموال غير المكلفين ممن لا ولي له وأما ولي فلا إلا أن يتصرف غير صالح فله نقضه أو كان مبذراً مسرفاً فله منعه كما في بيوع الخانية. ويملك ولاية الوقوف ولو شرط الواقف أن لا ولاية له في وقفه فشرطه باطل كما قدمناه في الوقف. ويبحث عن ولاتها فيعزل الخائن عنها ولو كان ابن الواقف. ويحاسبهم ويحلف من يتهمه منهم كما قدمناه في الوقف وله نصب الأوصياء إن لم يكن للميت وصي.
I have not seen for our companions a collected [work] of what the judge gains by appointment, and I have collected it from places: he possesses judgment established by evidence or confession or refusal to take an oath after fulfilling the legal conditions for judgment; he possesses imprisonment of one who refuses to pay a right; and [for] one upon whom ta'zir is obligatory and he sees his imprisonment because they said it is delegated to his opinion; he possesses execution of ta'zir for what is a right of Allah without anyone requesting and what is a right of a slave with his request; and he possesses... He said: The place of dislike is when it is incumbent upon him, and when it is exclusive it becomes fard 'ayn and upon him to restrain himself, etc. and he possesses execution of hudud as they stated in their chapter. And in Tahdhib al-Qalanisi: they are to the Imam and governors of large cities, not to governors of rural areas and tax collectors in districts. He possesses marriage of orphans and orphan girls where they have no guardian, but on condition that it is written in his letter of appointment; and apparently from their statements in the chapter on guardians that the appointment of a judge of judges is not sufficient for this. He possesses delegation (istikhlaf) with explicit permission or by his saying 'I make you judge of judges', otherwise he does not possess it. He possesses guardianship of the wealth of non-legally responsible persons who have no guardian; as for one who has a guardian, no, unless he acts improperly, then he may annul it, or if he is wasteful and extravagant, he may prevent him, as in Buyu' al-Khaniyya. He possesses guardianship of endowments (waqf), even if the founder stipulated that he has no authority over it, his condition is void as we have mentioned in the chapter on waqf. He investigates their custodians, removes the treacherous even if he is the son of the founder. He audits them and swears those he suspects as we mentioned in waqf. He has the power to appoint guardians (awsiya') if the deceased has no executor.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage systematically enumerates the powers a judge acquires by virtue of his appointment. The author notes that he has collected these from various sources. The powers include: (1) adjudicating based on evidence, confession, or refusal of oath; (2) imprisoning a person who refuses to pay a debt; (3) imposing discretionary punishment (ta'zir) and imprisonment if he deems it appropriate—this is delegated to his discretion; (4) executing hudud (fixed punishments) but only for major cities, not rural areas; (5) marrying orphans who have no guardian, provided this authority is explicitly mentioned in his letter of appointment; (6) delegating to a deputy (istikhlaf) only with explicit permission; (7) guardianship over the wealth of minors and insane persons who have no guardian; if there is a guardian, the judge only intervenes if the guardian is neglectful or wasteful; (8) supervision of endowments (waqf), including the power to dismiss corrupt custodians even if they are the founder's children; (9) appointing guardians (awsiya') when the deceased left none. The passage emphasizes that the judge's authority over waqf cannot be restricted by the founder's conditions. A marginal note explains that if performing such duties becomes exclusive to him, it becomes fard 'ayn (individual obligation).

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offenses that are not hadd or qisas, left to the judge's opinion.
حدود (hudud): Fixed corporal punishments prescribed by the Qur'an and Sunnah.
ولاية (wilayah): Guardianship or authority, here over wealth of minors, waqf, etc.
استخلاف (istikhlaf): Delegation of judicial authority to a deputy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can a judge marry off an orphan according to this passage?
A) He always has this power by default.
B) Only if the orphan's guardian is absent.
C) Only if it is written in his appointment letter.
D) Only with the consent of the orphan's relatives.

Key Takeaway
A judge's powers are extensive but not unlimited; some require explicit terms in the appointment letter.

Seven Cases for Judge-Appointed Guardians
Detailed listing of seven (plus one) instances where a judge may appoint a guardian

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven cases where a Hanafi judge may appoint a guardian and explain the condition of disconnected absence.

Core Idea
A judge may appoint a guardian in seven specific cases—not for every absentee—to protect vulnerable interests.

The judge's authority to appoint guardians is not unlimited. Hanafi fiqh enumerates precise situations where this power is exercised, balancing the need to protect minors, estates, and creditors against the rights of absent parties. This lesson walks through those cases and clarifies the critical distinction between a missing person (mafqud) and an absentee (gha'ib).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the context: qada and guardianship
Understand that the judge's power to appoint a guardian is part of his general authority in the judiciary. The passage builds on the earlier book of qada.
The text is from al-Bazzaziyya, a later Hanafi fatwa collection.
2
Identify the first seven cases from Imam al-Halwani
Read each case carefully: (1) debt in estate with heir unwilling or minor; (2) wasteful father of minor; (3) defect discovered after purchase from deceased; (4) debt with absent heir (disconnected); (5) father of minor absent (disconnected); (6) missing person (mafqud); (7) by implication, not for non-disconnected absentee.
Case 7 is inferred from the prohibition of appointing for a gha'ib.
3
Understand al-Khassaf's restriction on disconnected absence
Al-Khassaf specifies that for cases 4 and 5, the absence must be 'disconnected' (inqita')—no news and no travel possible. If the heir is reachable, the judge does not appoint.
This is the key condition that prevents abuse.
4
Learn the eighth case: deaf, blind, mute defendant
From al-Qunyah, if the defendant cannot communicate, the judge appoints a guardian to represent him in the lawsuit, provided he has no other guardian.
This is a procedural necessity.
5
Reconcile the apparent contradiction about appointing for the absent
Some later texts allow appointment for an absentee if necessary. Sheikh Khayr al-Din reconciles: the prohibition applies when the absence is not disconnected and there is no pressing need.
The mufta bihi follows the seven cases with the disconnected condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البزازية من التاسع في نصب الوصي من كتاب القضاء قال الإمام الحلواني : للقاضي أن ينصب الوصي في مواضع إذا كان في التركة دين مهراً كان الدين أو غيره، بشرط امتناع الوارث الكبير من البيع للقضاء أو وصية أو صغير فينصبه القاضي لقضاء الدين أو لتنفيذ الوصية أو لحفظ مال الصغير، وكذا لو كان أبو الصغير مبذراً متلفاً لمال الصغير ينصب وصياً لحفظ ماله ولو اشترى الوارث من مورثه شيئاً ثم اطلع بعد موته على عيب نصب القاضي وصياً حتى يرده الأب عليه وقيد الخصاف نصب الوصي فيما إذا كان على الميت دين وله وارث كبير غائب بانقطاعه عن بلد المتوفى لا يأتي ولا تذهب القافلة، فإن لم يكن منقطعاً لا ينصب، وكذا ينصب وصياً على الصغير عند غيبة أبيه واحتيج إلى إثبات حق الصغير إن كانت غيبة الأب منقطعة وإلا فلا. وينصب وصياً عن المفقود لحفظ حقوقه ولا ينصب عن الغائب ا هـ . فهذه سبعة مواضع يملك فيها نصب الوصي. ثم رأيت ثامناً قال في القنية : إذا كان المدعى عليه أصم أعمى أخرس فالقاضي ينصب عنه وصياً ويأمر المدعي بالخصومة معه إن لم يكن له أب أو جد أو وصيهما ا هـ. قال في البزازية بعدها : وإنما يلي أن قوله «وإن كان فرضاً يدفع التوقف وما استدل به تأمل قوله ولا ينصب على الغائب) في جامع الفصولين عن فتاوى رشيد الدين للقاضي : نصب الوصي لو كان وارثه غائباً ويكتب في نسخه الوصاية أنه جعله وصياً ووراثه غائب مدة السفر .اهـ. ووفق الشيخ خير الدين في حاشيته على الفصولين بإمكان حمل الأول على ما إذا كان معروفاً ولم تكن غيبته منقطعة وعلى ما لم تدع إليه الضرورة قال : وسيأتي ما يؤيده وتقدم ما يؤيده أيضاً .اهـ. ويأتي قريباً أن له إقراض مال الغائب قوله : (ثم رأيت ثامناً الخ) قال الرملي وفي واقعات الناطفي : رجل مات وأوصى إلى رجل فادعى إنسان ديناً على الميت والوصي غائب نصب القاضي خصماً عن الميت حتى يخاصم الغريم ليصل إلى أدب القاضي المنسوب إلى صاحب المحيط أن القاضي ينصب وصياً يدعى عليه وإن حقه. وفي شرح
And in al-Bazzaziyya, from the ninth [section] on the appointment of a guardian from the Book of Judiciary: Imam al-Halwani said: The judge may appoint a guardian in places: if there is debt in the estate, whether it be mahr or other debt, on condition that the adult heir refrains from selling for the debt or the will, or [the heir is] a minor, so the judge appoints him to pay the debt or execute the will or preserve the property of the minor. Likewise if the father of a minor is wasteful, destroying the property of the minor, he appoints a guardian to preserve his property. And if the heir bought something from the deceased then after his death discovered a defect, the judge appoints a guardian until he returns it upon the father. And al-Khassaf restricted the appointment of a guardian to when the deceased has a debt and has an adult heir who is absent with complete disconnection from the deceased's town, not coming and no caravan going; if not disconnected, he does not appoint. Likewise he appoints a guardian over a minor during the absence of his father and there is need to establish a right of the minor, if the father's absence is disconnected; otherwise no. And he appoints a guardian for the missing (mafqud) to preserve his rights, but does not appoint for the absent (gha'ib). This completes seven places where he gets to appoint a guardian. Then I saw an eighth: he said in al-Qunyah: If the defendant is deaf, blind, and mute, the judge appoints a guardian for him and orders the plaintiff to contend with him, if he has no father, grandfather, or their guardian. He said in al-Bazzaziyya after it: But it is fitting that his statement "and if it were fard it would remove the hesitation and what he argued with, reflect on his statement 'does not appoint for the absent'" in Jami' al-Fusulayn from Fatawa Rashid al-Din for the judge: appointment of a guardian if his heir is absent; and he writes in his copy of guardianship that he made him a guardian and his heir absent for the duration of travel. Sheikh Khayr al-Din in his hashiyah on al-Fusulayn reconciled: it is possible to carry the first on the case where he is known and his absence is not disconnected, and where necessity does not call for it. He said: evidence supporting this will come and has come before. Soon it will come that he may lend the property of the absent. His statement: 'Then I saw an eighth etc.' said al-Ramli: And in Waqi'at al-Natafi: A man died and appointed an executor to a man, then a person claimed a debt against the deceased while the executor is absent; the judge appoints an opponent for the deceased so that he contends with the creditor to reach... the adab of the judge attributed to the author of al-Muhit: that the judge appoints a guardian who is sued concerning his right. And in Sharh...
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage elaborates on one of the judge's powers—appointing guardians (awsiya')—by specifying the cases where this is permissible. The author quotes Imam al-Halwani from al-Bazzaziyya listing seven situations: (1) debt in the estate and the adult heir is unwilling to sell, or the heir is a minor; (2) the father of a minor is wasteful; (3) the heir bought something from the deceased with a defect discovered after death; (4) the deceased has debt and an adult heir who is completely absent (disconnected); (5) the father of a minor is absent with disconnection; (6) the missing person (mafqud) needs someone to preserve his rights—here the judge appoints a guardian; (7) [implied by contrast with 'does not appoint for the absent']. Note that 'absent' (gha'ib) means someone whose location is known but not reachable, whereas 'missing' (mafqud) means location unknown. Then an eighth case is added from al-Qunyah: when the defendant is deaf, blind, and mute, the judge appoints a guardian to represent him. The passage also includes reconciliations from later scholars like al-Ramli and Sheikh Khayr al-Din regarding apparent contradictions about appointing for the absent. The final sentence mentions that the judge may lend the property of the absent person. The text is dense and reflects later Hanafi fatwa literature (mutakhkhirin).

Key Terms
نصب الوصي (nasb al-wasi): The act of appointing a guardian (wasi) by the judge to manage affairs of minors, the missing, or estates with debt.
غائب (gha'ib): An absentee whose location is known but communication is cut off (non-disconnected absence).
مفقود (mafqud): A missing person whose whereabouts are unknown and no news is available.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases does the judge NOT have the power to appoint a guardian according to the passage?
A) The deceased has a debt and the adult heir refuses to pay.
B) The father of a minor is wasteful with the minor's money.
C) There is an adult heir who is absent but his absence is not disconnected (e.g., he can be reached).
D) The defendant is deaf, blind, and mute with no guardian.

Key Takeaway
A judge may appoint a guardian in seven specific cases, and for an absentee only when the absence is disconnected.

Eight Cases for Judge-Appointed Guardianship (Nasb al-Wasi)
Enumeration of cases with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight cases where a Hanafi judge may appoint a guardian and identify the conditions that must be satisfied for such an appointment.

Core Idea
A judge may appoint a guardian only in specific cases listed by the fuqaha, with strict conditions on the judge and the appointee.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates the specific situations in which a Hanafi judge is empowered to appoint a guardian (wasi) for those who lack one, such as minors, missing persons, or estates with debts. The author lists seven cases from Imam al-Halwani, then adds an eighth from al-Quniya, and further notes conditions from al-Bazzaziyya. Understanding these cases is essential for students of qada (judicial rulings) and for anyone who may need to petition a judge for guardianship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base authority
Who is credited with the seven cases? Look for the name in the passage. The source attributes the seven cases to Imam al-Halwani.
This helps you track the chain of transmission of the ruling.
2
List the seven cases from al-Halwani
Read through the passage and extract each of the seven situations where the judge appoints a guardian. Write them down in your own words.
The cases involve debts, minors, wasteful fathers, etc.
3
Note the conditions
What extra requirements are mentioned? For example, the judge must be authorized to delegate (ma'dhun bi al-istikhlaf) and the guardian must be just, trustworthy, competent, and not a stranger.
These are shurut (conditions) for the validity of the appointment.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf
What restriction does al-Khassaf add? He requires that the absent heir be completely cut off (munqati') – i.e., no communication or caravans. Compare this with al-Halwani's general statement.
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi difference.
5
Identify the added eighth case
From al-Quniya: the judge appoints a guardian for a defendant who is deaf, blind, and dumb, if he has no father, grandfather, or their executor.
This expands the original seven cases.
6
Recognize additional notes
Al-Ramli mentions a case from Waqi'at al-Natifi where the executor is absent. Also note the condition that the guardian must be known (not a stranger) and that the judge's authority to delegate is required.
These details come from later Hanafi works (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

وله نصب الأوصياء إن لم يكن للميت وصي. وفي البزازية من التاسع في نصب الوصي من كتاب القضاء قال الإمام الحلواني : للقاضي أن ينصب الوصي في مواضع إذا كان في التركة دين مهراً كان الدين أو غيره، بشرط امتناع الوارث الكبير من البيع للقضاء أو وصية أو صغير فينصبه القاضي لقضاء الدين أو لتنفيذ الوصية أو لحفظ مال الصغير، وكذا لو كان أبو الصغير مبذراً متلفاً لمال الصغير ينصب وصياً لحفظ ماله ولو اشترى الوارث من مورثه شيئاً ثم اطلع بعد موته على عيب نصب القاضي وصياً حتى يرده الأب عليه وقيد الخصاف نصب الوصي فيما إذا كان على الميت دين وله وارث كبير غائب بانقطاعه عن بلد المتوفى لا يأتي ولا تذهب القافلة، فإن لم يكن منقطعاً لا ينصب، وكذا ينصب وصياً على الصغير عند غيبة أبيه واحتيج إلى إثبات حق الصغير إن كانت غيبة الأب منقطعة وإلا فلا. وينصب وصياً عن المفقود لحفظ حقوقه ولا ينصب عن الغائب ا هـ . فهذه سبعة مواضع يملك فيها نصب الوصي. ثم رأيت ثامناً قال في القنية : إذا كان المدعى عليه أصم أعمى أخرس فالقاضي ينصب عنه وصياً ويأمر المدعي بالخصومة معه إن لم يكن له أب أو جد أو وصيهما ا هـ. قال في البزازية بعدها : وإنما يلي النصب إذا كان مأذوناً بالاستخلاف وينصب عدلاً أميناً كافياً لا غريباً لا يعرف، ويثبت ذلك بإخبار عدل . قوله (ثم رأيت ثامناً الخ) قال الرملي وفي واقعات الناطفي : رجل مات وأوصى إلى رجل فادعى إنسان ديناً على الميت والوصي غائب نصب القاضي خصماً عن الميت حتى يخاصم الغريم ليصل إلى أدب القاضي المنسوب إلى صاحب المحيط أن القاضي ينصب وصياً يدعى عليه وإن حقه[؟]. وفي شرح النصب إذا كان مأذوناً بالاستخلاف وينصب عدلاً أميناً كافياً لا غريباً لا يعرف، ويثبت ذلك بإخبار عدل .
He has the authority to appoint guardians if the deceased has no executor. In al-Bazaziyya, from the ninth chapter on appointment of guardian from the Book of Judgement, Imam al-Halwani said: The judge may appoint a guardian in places: if the estate has a debt, whether the debt is a dower or otherwise, on condition that the major heir refrains from selling for payment of debt or for execution of will or if there is a minor, then the judge appoints a guardian for payment of debt, execution of will, or preservation of the minor's property. Similarly, if the father of a minor is squandering and wasting the minor's property, he appoints a guardian to preserve his property. And if the heir buys something from his predecessor and then after his death discovers a defect, the judge appoints a guardian so that the father returns it to him. Al-Khassaf restricted appointment of guardian to the case where the deceased has a debt and has a major absent heir whose absence is total from the deceased's country, he does not come and the caravan does not go; if not totally absent, he does not appoint. Similarly, he appoints a guardian for a minor upon the absence of his father and need to establish the minor's right if the father's absence is total, otherwise not. And he appoints a guardian for the missing person to preserve his rights, but does not appoint for the absent person. End. So these are seven places where he is empowered to appoint a guardian. Then I saw an eighth: in al-Quniya: if the defendant is deaf, blind, dumb, the judge appoints a guardian for him and orders the plaintiff to litigate with him if he has no father, grandfather, or their executor. End. He said in al-Bazaziyya after it: He only undertakes appointment if he is authorized to delegate and appoints a just, trustworthy, competent person, not a stranger who is not known, and it is established by the report of a reliable person. He said (then I saw an eighth etc.): al-Ramli said, and in Waqi'at al-Natifi: A man died and bequeathed to a man, and a person claimed a debt on the deceased and the executor was absent; the judge appointed a representative against the deceased so that he litigate with the creditor until he reaches the permission of the judge attributed to the author of al-Muhit that the judge appoints a guardian to be sued against and his right[?]. And in Sharh al-Nasb: if he is authorized to delegate and appoints a just, trustworthy, competent person, not a stranger who is not known, and it is established by the report of a reliable person.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage enumerates the specific situations in which a Hanafi judge may appoint a guardian (wasi) for those who lack one. The author lists seven cases derived from Imam al-Halwani's work, then adds an eighth from al-Quniya. The seven cases include: 1) when the estate has a debt and the major heir refuses to sell; 2) when there is a minor heir; 3) when the father of a minor is wasteful; 4) when the heir buys from the deceased and finds a defect; 5) when there is a major absent heir who is completely cut off; 6) when the father of a minor is absent with total disconnection; 7) when a person is missing (mafqud). The eighth case is when the defendant is deaf, blind, and dumb. A condition is added from al-Bazzaziyya: the judge himself must be authorized to delegate (ma'dhun bi al-istikhlaf) and the appointed guardian must be just, trustworthy, competent, and known. The commentary from al-Ramli adds a further case from al-Natifi where the executor is absent. The passage is from the commentary al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Key Terms
نصب الوصي (nasb al-wasi): The judge's act of appointing a guardian for someone who lacks one, such as a minor, missing person, or estate with debts.
الغائب (al-ghā'ib): A person who is absent from the location but whose whereabouts are known; distinguished from al-mafqud (missing).
المفقود (al-mafqūd): A person who is missing and whose whereabouts are unknown; the judge may appoint a guardian to preserve his rights.
منقطع (munqati'): Totally absent, with no contact or possibility of return, as when no caravans come from his location.
مبذر (mubadhdhir): A wasteful person who squanders property; in the context, a father who wastes his minor child's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the deceased has no debts and the heir is present
B) When the minor's father is wasteful with the minor's property
C) When the defendant is a healthy adult with no disabilities
D) When the absent heir is present in the same city

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi judge's authority to appoint a guardian is limited to eight specific cases, each with its own conditions, and the appointment requires the judge's delegation and a qualified guardian.

Condition of Jurisdiction for Guardian Appointment
Dispute over the condition of jurisdiction for guardian appointment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on whether a judge's appointment of a guardian requires the orphan to be within the judge's jurisdiction and explain the positions of al-Qadi, al-Halwani, and al-Sughdi.

Core Idea
Among Hanafis, the condition of jurisdiction for guardian appointment is disputed: some require it, others do not.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a disagreement among Hanafi scholars on whether a judge's appointment of a guardian (wasi) over an orphan requires that the orphan or the estate be within the judge's territorial jurisdiction. The base text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq stipulates the condition, but later authorities like al-Halwani reject it, leading to a practical difference in the scope of the guardian's authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq
The matn states the condition: the orphan must be in the judge's jurisdiction. This is the view chosen by al-Qadi.
2
Recognize the ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars
Multiple positions are cited: al-Zahiriyya requiring the boy's presence, al-Halwani rejecting any condition, and al-Sughdi limiting to the portion of the estate within jurisdiction.
3
Analyze al-Halwani's position
Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani holds that no condition of jurisdiction is necessary; the appointment is valid even if neither orphan nor estate is in the judge's jurisdiction.
4
Analyze al-Sughdi's position
Rukn al-Islam al-Sughdi restricts guardianship to only that part of the estate located within the judge's jurisdiction.
5
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under al-Halwani, a guardian appointed by a judge can manage all property anywhere; under al-Sughdi, only property within the judge's territory is covered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط في نصب الوصي على اليتيم كونه في ولاية القاضي لا التركة، وفي الوقف كون المدعى عليه في ولايته ؛ هكذا اختاره القاضي وفيه اختلاف. قوله : (ويشترط في نصب الوصي اليتيم الخ وفي الظهيرية أن الصحيح اشتراط حضور الصبي عند القاضي في نصب الوصي للزوم الإشارة إليه. وفي مبسوط شمس الأئمة الحلواني أنه لا يشترط في صحة نصب الوصي كون اليتيم أو التركة في ولايته وفي فتاوى القاضي : إذا نصب وصياً في تركه أيتام وهم في ولايته والتركة ليست في ولايته أو كانت التركة في ولايته والأيتام لم يكونوا في ولايته أو كان بعض التركة في ولايته والبعض لم يكن في ولايته قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : يصح النصب على كل حال ويكون الوصي وصياً في جميع التركة أينما كانت التركة. وكان ركن الإسلام على السغدي يقول: ما كان من التركة في ولايته يصير وصياً وما لا فلا أدب الأوصياء من فصل النصب وتمامه فيه قوله : (دل هذا على أنه يملك بعث مال إلى الغائب إليه الخ هذا مصرح به الخانية ونصها كما في الحامدية :
It is stipulated in the appointment of a guardian over an orphan that [the orphan] be in the judge's jurisdiction, not the estate, and in the endowment that the defendant be in his jurisdiction; thus al-Qadi chose it, and there is disagreement. His statement: (It is stipulated in the appointment of a guardian over the orphan etc.) In al-Zahiriyya that the correct view is the stipulation of the presence of the boy before the judge in the appointment of a guardian due to the necessity of pointing to him. And in the Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani that it is not a condition for the validity of appointment of a guardian that the orphan or the estate be in his jurisdiction. And in Fatawa al-Qadi: If he appoints a guardian in an estate of orphans while they are in his jurisdiction and the estate is not in his jurisdiction, or the estate is in his jurisdiction and the orphans are not, or some of the estate is in his jurisdiction and some not, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: The appointment is valid in all cases and the guardian becomes guardian over all the estate wherever the estate is. And Rukn al-Islam 'Ali al-Sughdi says: What is in his jurisdiction from the estate, he becomes guardian over it, and what is not, he does not. Discipline of guardians from the chapter on appointment and its completion. His statement: (This indicates that he may send property to the absent person etc.) This is explicitly stated in al-Khaniyya and its text as in al-Hamidiyya:
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage discusses a dispute among Hanafi scholars regarding the condition for the validity of a judge's appointment of a guardian (wasi). The original text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq stipulates that the orphan must be within the judge's jurisdiction, not the estate; similarly for endowment, the defendant must be in his jurisdiction. This is the choice of al-Qadi (likely al-Qaduri). However, there is ikhtilaf. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq brings the view of al-Zahiriyya that the correct opinion is that the boy must be present before the judge (to point to him). Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani in his Mabsut holds that no condition of jurisdiction is required at all for validity; the appointment is valid even if neither the orphan nor the estate is in the judge's jurisdiction. In one fatwa, if some of the estate is in jurisdiction and some not, al-Halwani validates the appointment over all, while Rukn al-Islam 'Ali al-Sughdi restricts the guardian's authority to only that part within the judge's jurisdiction. This dispute shows the range of opinion within the Hanafi school on the extent of the judge's wilaya.

Key Terms
ولاية القاضي (wilāyat al-qāḍī): The territorial or personal jurisdiction of the judge over the orphan or property.
نصب الوصي (nasb al-waṣiyy): The appointment of a guardian by the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, both must be in his jurisdiction
B) No, it is not a condition
C) Only the orphan must be present
D) Only the estate must be in his jurisdiction

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains a significant dispute on whether a judge's appointment of a guardian requires jurisdiction over the orphan or property; al-Halwani's view validates the appointment in all cases, while others restrict it.

Judge's Powers Over Absent Persons' Property
List of judge's powers over property of absent persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least five specific powers of a Hanafi judge regarding absent persons and identify the one explicit restriction mentioned in the text.

Core Idea
The judge can sell, lend, appoint, collect, and maintain—but never marry the umm walad of the absent.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq enumerates the extensive authority of the Hanafi judge over the property and affairs of persons who are absent (gha'ib), missing (mafqud), or deceased without known heirs. Understanding these powers is crucial for judicial practice and for protecting rights in the absence of the party concerned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
The judge's authority stems from the need to prevent loss (mafsada) of property and rights. Scan the text for phrases like 'if he fears destruction' or 'for preservation'.
This is the underlying rationale.
2
Categorise the Powers
Group the listed powers into: (a) sale of property, (b) lending and collection, (c) appointment of agents, (d) family maintenance, (e) handling deposits and missing persons.
This helps memorise the extensive list.
3
Identify the Restriction
Locate the statement beginning with 'wa laysa lahu'. The judge may NOT marry the umm walad of the absent person. Note other implied restrictions (e.g., cannot marry slaves of absent/insane).
The restriction is explicit and important.
4
Trace the Source Authority
Note that the text cites al-Bazzaziyya and Jami' al-Fusulayn—these are later Hanafi fiqh works, not Zahir al-Riwayah. Understand the authority weight.
Fatawa mutakhkhirin.
5
Apply to a Hypothetical
Given a scenario: an absent person's movable property is perishable, and his location is unknown. What can the judge do?
Refer to the text: sell the movable property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويملك البيع على المديون لإيفاء دينه على القول المفتى به كما صرحوا به في الحجر وله ولاية إقراض اللقطة الملتقط، وولاية إقراض مال الغائب وله بيع منقوله إذا خاف عليه التلف إذا لم يعلم مكان الغائب، فإذا علم مكانه بعث إليه لأنه يمكنه حفظ العين والمالية دل هذا على أنه يملك بعث ما الغائب إليه إذا خاف التلف وله نصب وكيل في جمع غلات المفقود. طلب الوارث أو لا. وله إيفاء ديون الغائب بماله بالحصص وبيع ماله لإيفاء دينه إذا كان دينه ثابتاً عنده. وله الإرسال خلف من نسب إلى طلاق زوجته الثلاث إذا أخبره عدلان وإن لم تطلبه المرأة، الكل من البزازية من نوع في ولاية القاضي قال : وليس له أن يزوج أم ولد الغائب وله الإذن بالإنفاق على مال الغائب وزوجته وأولاده وأصله من ماله كما قدمناه في النفقات. وله فرض النفقة على الزوج إذا لم يكن صاحب مائدة وطعام كثير. وفي جامع الفصولين : للقاضي إيداع مال الغائب وله الإذن في بيع شيء باعه مالكه لرجل وغاب المشتري ليأخذ ثمنه من ثمنه لو من جنسه ولو كانت دابة فله الإذن بإجارتها وعلفها من أجرتها. وله الإذن ببيع الجارية المغصوبة لو كان مالكها غائباً ولو من الغاصب فيحل له وطؤها، وإن حضر مالكها كان له علي ذي اليد ثمنها ولا يملك تزويج أمة الغائب والمجنون وقنهما، وله أن يكاتبهما ويبيعهما، وله أن يقبض دين غائب من محبوسه وله أن يضعه عند عدل، وله إطلاق محبوسة بكفيل بنفسه، وله الإذن ببيع وديعة خيف فسادها وربها غائب كصوف، وله بيع دار الميت إذا لم يعلم له وارث وإذا علم جاز أيضاً حفظاً، وله بيع الآبق وله إجارة بيع بيت المفقود لو لم يكن الوارث غائباً في رواية ؛ كذا في الفصول العامدية
He has the authority to sell on behalf of the debtor to pay off his debt according to the relied-upon opinion, as they stated in the chapter on interdiction. And he has the authority to lend the found object (luqta) found, and the authority to lend the property of the absent person. And he has the authority to sell his movable property if he fears its destruction when he does not know the location of the absent person; if he knows his location, he sends to him because he can preserve the item and its value. This indicates that he has the authority to send property to the absent person if he fears destruction. And he has the authority to appoint an agent to collect the produce of the missing person, whether the heir requests or not. And he has the authority to pay off the debts of the absent person from his property in proportion and to sell his property to pay his debt if the debt is established with him. And he has the authority to send for someone who is suspected of divorcing his wife three times if two reliable persons inform him, even if the woman does not request it. All from al-Bazzaziyya, from the type on the judge's authority. He said: He does not have the authority to marry the umm walad of the absent person, but he has the authority to permit expenditure from the property of the absent person for his wife and children, and its origin from his property as we earlier in the chapter on maintenance. And he has the authority to impose maintenance on the husband if he is not a host with abundant food. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: The judge may deposit the property of the absent person, and he may permit the sale of something its owner sold to a man and the buyer went absent, to take its price from its price if of the same type, and if it is an animal, he may permit its hire and its fodder from its hire. And he may permit the sale of a slave girl who was usurped if her owner is absent, even from the usurper; then intercourse with her becomes lawful, and if her owner appears, he has the right to her price from the possessor. And he does not have the authority to marry the slave girl of the absent person or the insane person, nor their male slave; but he may make a contract of kitaba with them and sell them. And he may collect a debt of an absent person from his imprisoned [debtor] and may place it with a trustworthy person. And he may release a female prisoner with a surety for herself. And he may permit the sale of a deposit whose corruption is feared while its owner is absent, like wool. And he may sell the house of the deceased if no heir is known, and if known, it is also permissible for preservation. And he may sell the runaway slave. And he may lease or sell the house of the missing person if the heir is not absent in one narration; thus in al-Fusul al-'Amidiyya.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage lists numerous powers of the judge (qadi) concerning the property and affairs of absent persons (gha'ib), missing persons (mafqud), and deceased persons without heirs. The judge can sell debtor's property to pay debts, lend found property, lend property of absent persons, sell movable property of an absent person if feared loss, send property to the absent person if feared loss, appoint an agent to collect produce of the missing, pay debts of absent persons, sell property to pay established debts, act on reports of triple divorce, permit expenditure on the absent person's family, impose maintenance, deposit property, sell items sold to an absent buyer, hire out animals, sell a usurped slave girl (making intercourse lawful for the buyer), conclude kitaba, collect debts, release prisoners, sell deposits that may spoil, sell houses of the deceased with no heir, sell runaway slaves, and lease or sell the missing person's house if the heir is present. However, he cannot marry the umm walad of an absent person or marry slaves of absent or insane persons. These powers are drawn from al-Bazzaziyya and Jami' al-Fusulayn, reflecting the extensive authority of the Hanafi judge in preserving rights and managing affairs.

Key Terms
ولاية القاضي (wilāyat al-qāḍī): The judge's authority to manage the affairs and property of absent persons, missing persons, and others in need.
الغائب (al-ghā'ib): A person who is absent but whose location is known, distinguished from al-mafqud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi judge has extensive discretionary powers to preserve property and rights of absent persons, but with one explicit restriction: he cannot marry the umm walad of an absent person.

Conditions for Appointing a Guardian Over an Orphan
Condition for appointing a guardian over an orphan and the disagreement among Hanafi authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for appointing a guardian over an orphan in Hanafi fiqh and explain the disagreement among Hanafi authorities regarding jurisdiction.

Core Idea
The judge's appointment of a guardian for an orphan requires the orphan's presence in his jurisdiction, not the estate's location.

This lesson examines the key condition for appointing a guardian (wasi) over an orphan as presented in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The passage first states the condition succinctly, then provides a detailed discussion of the differing opinions, particularly from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and Rukn al-Islam al-Sughdi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition
Locate the condition stated in the matn: the orphan must be within the judge's jurisdiction, not the estate. Note the parallel condition for waqf: the defendant must be in his jurisdiction.
The condition is introduced with the verb 'yushtarat'.
2
Understand the Rationale
The judge's authority (wilaya) over the person of the orphan is necessary for guardianship because the guardian must act under the judge's supervision. Jurisdiction over the estate alone is insufficient without access to the orphan.
This is the chosen view of the Qadi (al-Qadi al-Marwazi?).
3
Trace the Disagreement
Al-Zahiriyyah requires the child's physical presence before the judge for appointment. Al-Halwani holds that jurisdiction over either the orphan or the estate suffices, and the appointment is valid even if neither is in his jurisdiction. Al-Sughdi restricts guardianship only to what is in the judge's jurisdiction.
The passage cites Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and Rukn al-Islam al-Sughdi.
4
Determine the Relied-Upon View
The passage leans toward al-Halwani's view that the appointment is valid in all circumstances, making the guardian effective over all the estate wherever it is.
This is the position that gives maximum flexibility to protect orphans.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب القضاء النصب إذا كان مأذوناً بالاستخلاف وينصب عدلاً أميناً كافياً لا غريباً لا يعرف، ويثبت ذلك بإخبار عدل . ويشترط في نصب الوصي على اليتيم كونه في ولاية القاضي لا التركة، وفي الوقف كون المدعى عليه في ولايته ؛ هكذا اختاره القاضي وفيه اختلاف ويملك البيع على المديون لإيفاء دينه على القول المفتى به كما صرحوا به في الحجر وله ولاية إقراض اللقطة الملتقط، وولاية إقراض مال الغائب وله بيع منقوله إذا خاف عليه التلف إذا لم يعلم مكان الغائب، فإذا علم مكانه بعث إليه لأنه يمكنه حفظ العين والمالية دل هذا على أنه يملك بعث ما الغائب إليه إذا خاف التلف وله نصب وكيل في جمع غلات المفقود. طلب الوارث أو لا. وله إيفاء ديون الغائب بماله بالحصص وبيع ماله لإيفاء دينه إذا كان دينه ثابتاً عنده. وله الإرسال خلف من نسب إلى طلاق زوجته الثلاث إذا أخبره عدلان وإن لم تطلبه المرأة، الكل من البزازية من نوع في ولاية القاضي قال : وليس له أن يزوج أم ولد الغائب وله الإذن بالإنفاق على مال الغائب وزوجته وأولاده وأصله من ماله كما قدمناه في النفقات. وله فرض النفقة على الزوج إذا لم يكن صاحب مائدة وطعام كثير. وفي جامع الفصولين : للقاضي إيداع مال الغائب وله الإذن في بيع شيء باعه مالكه لرجل وغاب المشتري ليأخذ ثمنه من ثمنه لو من جنسه ولو كانت دابة فله الإذن بإجارتها وعلفها من أجرتها. وله الإذن ببيع الجارية المغصوبة لو كان مالكها غائباً ولو من الغاصب فيحل له وطؤها، وإن حضر مالكها كان له على ذي اليد ثمنها ولا يملك تزويج أمة الغائب والمجنون وقنهما، وله أن يكاتبهما ويبيعهما، وله أن يقبض دين غائب من محبوسه وله أن يضعه عند عدل، وله إطلاق محبوسة بكفيل بنفسه، وله الإذن ببيع وديعة خيف فسادها وربها غائب كصوف، وله بيع دار الميت إذا لم يعلم له وارث وإذا علم جاز أيضاً حفظاً، وله بيع الآبق وله إجارة بيع بيت المفقود لو على لم يكن الوارث غائباً في رواية ؛ كذا في الفصول العامدية قوله : (ويشترط في نصب الوصي اليتيم الخ وفي الظهيرية أن الصحيح اشتراط حضور الصبي عند القاضي في نصب الوصي للزوم الإشارة إليه. وفي مبسوط شمس الأئمة الحلواني أنه لا يشترط في صحة نصب الوصي كون اليتيم أو التركة في ولايته وفي فتاوى القاضي : إذا نصب وصياً في تركه أيتام وهم في ولايته والتركة ليست في ولايته أو كانت التركة في ولايته والأيتام لم يكونوا في ولايته أو كان بعض التركة في ولايته والبعض لم يكن في ولايته قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : يصح النصب على كل حال ويكون الوصي وصياً في جميع التركة أينما كانت التركة. وكان ركن الإسلام على السغدي يقول: ما كان من التركة في ولايته يصير وصياً وما لا فلا أدب الأوصياء من فصل النصب وتمامه فيه قوله : (دل هذا على أنه يملك بعث مال إلى الغائب إليه الخ هذا مصرح به الخانية ونصها كما في الحامدية : . خيف خرابه لو لم يسكن وله قبض المغصوب الغائب من غاصبه، وله أخذ وديعة المفقود وإيداعها عند من يثق به. ا هـ ما في جامع الفصولين ملخصاً. وأما إقامة الجمع والأعياد فيملكها القاضي إن كانت في منشوره وإلا فلا وقول محمد للقاضي أن يجمع حمله المشايخ على هذا؛ كذا في البزازية من أول القضاء وله النظر في الطريق فيمنع متعدياً فيها ببناء وإشراع جناح لا يجوز، وله نصب القسام كما ذكروه في كتاب القسمة. وله نصب أئمة المساجد، ولم أر حكم نصبه للمحتسبين وينبغي أن يكون له ذلك إن لم ينصب الإمام أحداً. وأما نصب العاشر والجابي للزكوات فإلى الإمام كأخذ الجزية والخراج وما يتعلق بأموال بيت المال.
Book of Judging: Appointment if the judge is authorized to delegate and appoints a just, trustworthy, capable person, not a stranger who is unknown; and that is established by the report of a just person. And it is a condition in appointing a guardian over an orphan that the orphan be within the judge's jurisdiction, not the estate; and in the case of a waqf, that the defendant be within his jurisdiction. Thus the judge chose it, and there is difference of opinion. And he has the authority to sell the debtor's property to fulfill his debt according to the relied-upon opinion as they stated in the chapter on interdiction. And he has the authority to lend out the found property entrusted to him, and to lend out the property of an absent person. And he has the authority to sell his movable property if he fears its loss when he does not know the location of the absent person; if he knows his location, he sends it to him because he can preserve the physical object and its value. This indicates that he has the authority to send the property of the absent person to him if he fears destruction. And he has the authority to appoint an agent to collect the produce of the missing person, whether the heir requests it or not. And he has the authority to pay off the debts of the absent person from his property proportionally, and to sell his property to pay his debt if the debt is established with him. And he has the authority to send for one who is accused of divorcing his wife three times if two just persons inform him, even if the woman does not request it. All from al-Bazzaziyyah of the type 'On the Authority of the Judge'. He said: He does not have the authority to marry off the umm walad of an absent person; and he has the authority to permit spending from the property of the absent person on his wife and children, its basis being from his property as we mentioned in the chapter on maintenance. And he has the authority to impose maintenance on the husband if he is not a host with abundant food. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: The judge may deposit the property of an absent person, and may permit the sale of something sold by its owner to a man and the buyer is absent, to take its price from its price if of the same type; and if it is an animal, he may permit its hire and feeding from its hire. And he may permit the sale of a stolen slave-girl if her owner is absent, and even from the thief, so intercourse with her becomes lawful; and if her owner appears, he has the right to her price against the possessor. And he does not have the authority to marry off the slave-girl of an absent person or an insane person, nor their male slave; but he may make a kitaba contract for them and sell them. And he may collect a debt owed to an absent person from his imprisoned debtor and place it with a trustworthy person. And he may release an imprisoned person with a surety for his person. And he may permit the sale of a trust if its corruption is feared and its owner is absent, like wool. And he may sell the house of a deceased if no heir is known; and if known, it is also permissible for preservation. And he may sell a runaway slave. And he may lease and sell the house of a missing person if the heir is not absent, according to one narration. So in al-Fusul al-'Amidiyyah. He said: 'And it is a condition in appointing a guardian over the orphan, etc.' And in al-Zahiriyyah, the correct view is that the presence of the child before the judge is required in appointing a guardian due to the need to point to him. And in the Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, it is not a condition for the validity of appointing a guardian that the orphan or the estate be within his jurisdiction. And in the Fatawa of al-Qadi: If he appoints a guardian over the estate of orphans who are within his jurisdiction but the estate is not, or the estate is within his jurisdiction and the orphans are not, or part of the estate is within his jurisdiction and part is not, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: The appointment is valid in all cases, and the guardian is a guardian over all the estate wherever it is. And Rukn al-Islam al-Sughdi used to say: What is within his jurisdiction of the estate, he becomes a guardian over it; what is not, he does not. The discipline of guardians is from the section on appointment, and its completion is in it. He said: 'This indicates that he has the authority to send property to the absent person, etc.' This is stated explicitly in al-Khaniyyah, and its text as in al-Hamidiyyah: He feared its ruin if not inhabited. And he has the authority to take back a stolen item from its thief on behalf of the absent owner, and to take the trust of a missing person and deposit it with someone he trusts. End of the summary from Jami' al-Fusulayn. As for establishing the Friday and Eid prayers, the judge has authority if they are within his charter; otherwise not. The statement of Muhammad that the judge may gather for Friday is interpreted by the scholars accordingly; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah from the beginning of 'The Book of Judging'. And he has authority over the road, preventing aggressors from building or projecting a balcony that is not permissible. And he has authority to appoint a land surveyor as mentioned in the Book of Division. And he has authority to appoint imams of mosques; I have not seen a ruling on his appointment of muhtasibs, and it should be that he has that if the imam has not appointed anyone. As for the appointment of the tax collector and the collector of zakat, it is up to the imam, like taking the jizya and kharaj and what pertains to the public treasury.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage, from the book of al-Qada (Judging) in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, lists numerous powers of the judge (qadi). It opens by stating that if the judge is authorized to delegate, he may appoint a deputy who is just, trustworthy, and competent—not a stranger. The appointment is established by the testimony of a just person. The passage then details conditions for appointing a guardian over an orphan: the orphan must be within the judge's jurisdiction (not the estate), and in waqf cases, the defendant must be in his jurisdiction. There is some disagreement on this, but the chosen view is as stated. The judge also has authority to sell a debtor's property to pay debts, according to the mufta bihi view, as clarified in the chapter on interdiction. He can lend out found property (luqata) entrusted to him, and lend out the property of an absent person. If an absent person's movable property is at risk of destruction and his location is unknown, the judge may sell it; if known, he sends it to him. This indicates the judge may send property to an absent person if he fears loss. He can appoint an agent to collect the produce of a missing person, whether the heir asks or not. He can pay debts of an absent person proportionally and sell his property for debt if the debt is proven. If two just persons report that someone has divorced his wife three times, the judge may send for that person, even without the woman's request. These rulings are from al-Bazzaziyyah. The judge cannot marry off an absent person's umm walad (concubine who bore a child). He can authorize spending from the absent person's property for his wife and children, as previously mentioned. He can impose maintenance on a husband who is not a host with abundant food. According to Jami' al-Fusulayn, the judge may deposit an absent person's property, authorize the sale of something sold by its owner to an absent buyer to take its price, and if it's an animal, hire it and feed it from its hire. He may sell a stolen slave-girl if the owner is absent, even to the thief, making intercourse permissible; if the owner appears, he has the right to her price from the possessor. He cannot marry off the slave-girl or male slave of an absent or insane person. He can make a kitaba contract for them and sell them. He can collect a debt from an imprisoned debtor and place it with a trustworthy person. He can release an imprisoned person with a surety for his person. He can permit sale of a trust if it might spoil, like wool. He can sell a deceased's house if no heir is known, and even if known, for preservation. He can sell a runaway slave. He can lease and sell the house of a missing person if the heir is not absent (one narration). The passage then discusses a condition in appointing a guardian: according to al-Zahiriyyah, the child's presence is required; but Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani's Mabsut says it is not a condition that the orphan or estate be in his jurisdiction. In Fatawa al-Qadi, the appointment is valid in all situations. The passage concludes with more powers: the judge may take back stolen property from the thief, take a missing person's trust and deposit it with a trustworthy person. Regarding Friday and Eid prayers, the judge has authority if in his charter; otherwise not. Imam Muhammad's statement about the judge leading Friday prayers is interpreted accordingly. The judge oversees roads, appoints land surveyors, mosque imams, and possibly muhtasibs if the imam hasn't appointed one. Tax and zakat collectors are appointed by the imam, along with matters of jizya, kharaj, and the public treasury.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-wasiy): A guardian appointed over an orphan or a will; the judge can appoint one for orphans within his jurisdiction.
ولاية (wilaya): Jurisdiction or authority of a judge over persons and property within his territorial district.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the initial matn in the passage, what is the condition for a judge to appoint a guardian over an orphan?
A) The estate must be in the judge's jurisdiction.
B) The orphan must be in the judge's jurisdiction.
C) Both the orphan and the estate must be in the judge's jurisdiction.
D) The guardian must be appointed by the imam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi judge's appointment of a guardian over an orphan requires the orphan's presence in his jurisdiction, not the estate.

Qada — Judiciary
beginner
12 min
Judge's Powers Over the Property of Absent Persons
Enumeration of judge's powers over absent persons' property and affairs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least five specific powers a judge has over the property of an absent person and explain the condition that restricts these powers.

Core Idea
The judge acts as a guardian for absent persons, with powers limited by necessity and the ability to preserve the property.

This lesson covers the extensive list of powers the judge has over the property and affairs of absent persons (gha'ib) as detailed in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. These powers include selling, lending, spending, collecting debts, and more. The overarching theme is that the judge acts to preserve the interests of the absent person when no other means exist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Category
The passage enumerates powers under the heading of the judge's authority over absent persons, including gha'ib (absent), mafqud (missing), and others.
The powers are scattered from 'wamalik al-bay' to 'wa lahu ijara bay' al-mafqud'.
2
Categorize the Powers
Group the powers into: powers over property (sell, lend, spend), powers over debts (collect, pay), powers over contracts (hire, permit sale), and powers over persons (send for, release).
This helps in memorization.
3
Note the Conditions
Many powers are conditional: e.g., selling depends on fear of loss and unknown location; lending is for preservation; spending is for maintenance of dependents.
The condition 'if he fears its destruction' appears often.
4
Recognize Limits
The judge cannot marry off the umm walad or slave of an absent person, showing limits to his authority.
Also, he can only send property if he knows the location, otherwise sell.

كتاب القضاء النصب إذا كان مأذوناً بالاستخلاف وينصب عدلاً أميناً كافياً لا غريباً لا يعرف، ويثبت ذلك بإخبار عدل . ويشترط في نصب الوصي على اليتيم كونه في ولاية القاضي لا التركة، وفي الوقف كون المدعى عند عدل، وله إطلاق محبوسة بكفيل بنفسه، وله الإذن ببيع وديعة خيف فسادها وربها غائب كصوف، وله بيع دار الميت إذا لم يعلم له وارث وإذا علم جاز أيضاً حفظاً، وله بيع الآبق وله إجارة بيع بيت المفقود لو على And in the Fatawa of al-Qadi: If he appoints a guardian over the estate of orphans who are within his jurisdiction but the estate is not, or the estate is within his jurisdiction and the orphans are not, or part of the estate is within his jurisdiction and part is not, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: The appointment is valid in all cases, and the guardian is a guardian over all the estate wherever it is. And Rukn al-Islam al-Sughdi used to say: What is within his jurisdiction of the estate, he becomes a guardian over it; what is not, he does not. The discipline of guardians is from the section on appointment, and its completion is in it. He said: 'This indicates that he has the authority to send property to the absent person, etc.' This is stated explicitly in al-Khaniyyah, and its text as in al-Hamidiyyah: He feared its ruin if not inhabited. And he has the authority to take back a stolen item from its thief on behalf of the absent owner, and to take the trust of a missing person and deposit it with someone he trusts. End of the summary from Jami' al-Fusulayn. As for establishing the Friday and Eid prayers, the judge has authority if they are within his charter; otherwise not. The statement of Muhammad that the judge may gather for Friday is interpreted by the scholars accordingly; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah from the beginning of 'The Book of Judging'. And he has authority over the road, preventing aggressors from building or projecting a balcony that is not permissible. And he has authority to appoint a land surveyor as mentioned in the Book of Division. And he has authority to appoint imams of mosques; I have not seen a ruling on his appointment of muhtasibs, and it should be that he has that if the imam has not appointed anyone. As for the appointment of the tax collector and the collector of zakat, it is up to the imam, like taking the jizya and kharaj and what pertains to the public treasury.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage, from the book of al-Qada (Judging) in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, lists numerous powers of the judge (qadi). It opens by stating that if the judge is authorized to delegate, he may appoint a deputy who is just, trustworthy, and competent—not a stranger. The appointment is established by the testimony of a just person. The passage then details conditions for appointing a guardian over an orphan: the orphan must be within the judge's jurisdiction (not the estate), and in waqf cases, the defendant must be in his jurisdiction. There is some disagreement on this, but the chosen view is as stated. The judge also has authority to sell a debtor's property to pay debts, according to the mufta bihi view, as clarified in the chapter on interdiction. He can lend out found property (luqata) entrusted to him, and lend out the property of an absent person. If an absent person's movable property is at risk of destruction and his location is unknown, the judge may sell it; if known, he sends it to him. This indicates the judge may send property to an absent person if he fears loss. He can appoint an agent to collect the produce of a missing person, whether the heir asks or not. He can pay debts of an absent person proportionally and sell his property for debt if the debt is proven. If two just persons report that someone has divorced his wife three times, the judge may send for that person, even without the woman's request. These rulings are from al-Bazzaziyyah. The judge cannot marry off an absent person's umm walad (concubine who bore a child). He can authorize spending from the absent person's property for his wife and children, as previously mentioned. He can impose maintenance on a husband who is not a host with abundant food. According to Jami' al-Fusulayn, the judge may deposit an absent person's property, authorize the sale of something sold by its owner to an absent buyer to take its price, and if it's an animal, hire it and feed it from its hire. He may sell a stolen slave-girl if the owner is absent, even to the thief, making intercourse permissible; if the owner appears, he has the right to her price from the possessor. He cannot marry off the slave-girl or male slave of an absent or insane person. He can make a kitaba contract for them and sell them. He can collect a debt from an imprisoned debtor and place it with a trustworthy person. He can release an imprisoned person with a surety for his person. He can permit sale of a trust if it might spoil, like wool. He can sell a deceased's house if no heir is known, and even if known, for preservation. He can sell a runaway slave. He can lease and sell the house of a missing person if the heir is not absent (one narration). The passage then discusses a condition in appointing a guardian: according to al-Zahiriyyah, the child's presence is required; but Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani's Mabsut says it is not a condition that the orphan or estate be in his jurisdiction. In Fatawa al-Qadi, the appointment is valid in all situations. The passage concludes with more powers: the judge may take back stolen property from the thief, take a missing person's trust and deposit it with a trustworthy person. Regarding Friday and Eid prayers, the judge has authority if in his charter; otherwise not. Imam Muhammad's statement about the judge leading Friday prayers is interpreted accordingly. The judge oversees roads, appoints land surveyors, mosque imams, and possibly muhtasibs if the imam hasn't appointed one. Tax and zakat collectors are appointed by the imam, along with matters of jizya, kharaj, and the public treasury.

Key Terms
الغائب (al-gha'ib): A person who is away from his residence and whose location is unknown or inaccessible.
اللقطة (al-luqata): Lost property found by someone; the judge has authority to lend it out or sell it if it is at risk of spoilage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can the judge sell an absent person's movable property?
A) Whenever the judge deems it beneficial
B) Only if the absent person is in debt
C) If he fears the property will be destroyed and the absent person's location is unknown
D) Only with the permission of the absent person's relative

Key Takeaway
The judge may sell, lend, or otherwise deal with an absent person's property only when necessary to prevent loss or fulfill debts.

Qada — Judiciary

Administrative Powers of the Judge: Friday, Eid, Roads, and Appointments
Limits and conditions of the judge's administrative and appointment powers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the judge's administrative powers regarding Friday and Eid prayers, road maintenance, and appointment of imams, surveyors, and tax collectors.

Core Idea
The judge's administrative authority is limited to matters within his charter and does not extend to certain fiscal appointments.

This lesson covers the remaining powers of the judge from the passage, focusing on public worship (Friday and Eid prayers), road regulation, and the appointment of imams, qassam (surveyors), muhtasibs, and tax collectors. It clarifies that the judge's authority is circumscribed by his charter (manshur) and that some appointments belong to the imam (ruler).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Domain
The passage moves from property matters to public affairs: establishing Friday and Eid prayers, road supervision, and appointments.
These are administrative rather than judicial or guardianship powers.
2
Note the Condition for Prayers
The judge can lead Friday and Eid prayers only if his charter (manshur) includes that authority; otherwise, he cannot.
This is based on a statement of Imam Muhammad.
3
Road and Appointments
The judge prevents aggression on roads (e.g., building encroachments). He appoints qassam (land surveyors) and imams for mosques. The text questions whether he can appoint muhtasibs but suggests yes if the imam hasn't.
The judge's power over muhtasibs is inferred.
4
Identify Limitations
Tax collectors (ashir) and zakat collectors are appointed by the imam, not the judge, as these involve state finances.
This includes jizya, kharaj, and bayt al-mal matters.

الفصولين : للقاضي إيداع مال الغائب وله الإذن في بيع شيء باعه مالكه لرجل وغاب المشتري ليأخذ ثمنه من ثمنه لو من جنسه ولو كانت دابة فله الإذن بإجارتها وعلفها من أجرتها. وله الإذن ببيع الجارية المغصوبة لو كان مالكها غائباً ولو من الغاصب فيحل له وطؤها، وإن حضر مالكها كان له على ذي اليد ثمنها ولا يملك تزويج أمة الغائب والمجنون وقنهما، وله أن يكاتبهما ويبيعهما، وله أن يقبض دين غائب من محبوسه وله أن يضعه عند عدل، وله إطلاق محبوسة بكفيل بنفسه، وله الإذن ببيع وديعة خيف فسادها وربها غائب كصوف، وله بيع دار الميت إذا لم يعلم له وارث وإذا علم جاز أيضاً حفظاً، وله بيع الآبق وله إجارة بيع بيت المفقود لو على لم يكن الوارث غائباً في رواية ؛ كذا في الفصول العامدية قوله : (ويشترط في نصب الوصي اليتيم الخ وفي الظهيرية أن الصحيح اشتراط حضور الصبي عند القاضي في نصب الوصي للزوم الإشارة إليه. وفي مبسوط شمس الأئمة الحلواني أنه لا يشترط في صحة نصب الوصي كون اليتيم أو التركة في ولايته وفي فتاوى القاضي : إذا نصب وصياً في تركه أيتام وهم في ولايته والتركة ليست في ولايته أو كانت التركة في ولايته والأيتام لم يكونوا في ولايته أو كان بعض التركة في ولايته والبعض لم يكن في ولايته قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : يصح النصب على كل حال ويكون الوصي وصياً في جميع التركة أينما كانت التركة. وكان ركن الإسلام على السغدي يقول: ما كان للقاضي أن يجمع حمله المشايخ على هذا؛ كذا في البزازية من أول القضاء وله النظر في الطريق فيمنع متعدياً فيها ببناء وإشراع جناح لا يجوز، وله نصب القسام كما ذكروه في كتاب القسمة. وله نصب أئمة المساجد، ولم Book of Judging: Appointment if the judge is authorized to delegate and appoints a just, trustworthy, capable person, not a stranger who is unknown; and that is established by the report of a just person. And it is a condition in appointing a guardian over an orphan that the orphan be within the judge's jurisdiction, not the estate; and in the case of a waqf, that the defendant be within his jurisdiction. Thus the judge chose it, and there is difference of opinion. And he has the authority to sell the debtor's property to fulfill his debt according to the relied-upon opinion as they stated in the chapter on interdiction. And he has the authority to lend out the found property entrusted to him, and to lend out the property of an absent person. And he has the authority to sell his movable property if he fears its loss when he does not know the location of the absent person; if he knows his location, he sends it to him because he can preserve the physical object and its value. This indicates that he has the authority to send the property of the absent person to him if he fears destruction. And he has the authority to appoint an agent to collect the produce of the missing person, whether the heir requests it or not. And he has the authority to pay off the debts of the absent person from his property proportionally, and to sell his property to pay his debt if the debt is established with him. And he has the authority to send for one who is accused of divorcing his wife three times if two just persons inform him, even if the woman does not request it. All from al-Bazzaziyyah of the type 'On the Authority of the Judge'. He said: He does not have the authority to marry off the umm walad of an absent person; and he has the authority to permit spending from the property of the absent person on his wife and children, its basis being from his property as we mentioned in the chapter on maintenance. And he has the authority to impose maintenance on the husband if he is not a host with abundant food. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: The judge may deposit the property of an absent person, and may permit the sale of something sold by its owner to a man and the buyer is absent, to take its price from its price if of the same type; and if it is an animal, he may permit its hire and feeding from its hire. He said: 'And it is a condition in appointing a guardian over the orphan, etc.' And in al-Zahiriyyah, the correct view is that the presence of the child before the judge is required in appointing a guardian due to the need to point to him. The discipline of guardians is from the section on appointment, and its completion is in it. Key Terms
المنشور (al-manshur): The official charter or appointment letter given to a judge that specifies his powers and jurisdiction.
المحتسب (al-muhtasib): A market inspector or public morals official; the judge may appoint him if the imam hasn't.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A judge's administrative powers are bounded by his charter; fiscal appointments are the imam's prerogative.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Seeking Judgeship: Prohibition and Its Exception
Explains prohibition of seeking judgeship and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on seeking the position of judge, identify the proof from hadith, and apply the exception of ta'ayyun (unique qualification) that makes seeking obligatory.

Core Idea
Seeking judgeship is prohibited unless you are uniquely needed — then it becomes obligatory.

The position of judge (qadi) carries great responsibility. The Prophet warned against actively seeking it, but what if no one else is qualified? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling: the general prohibition, the proof from hadith, the distinction between inner desire and verbal request, and the crucial exception when one is specifically designated (ta'ayyun). Understanding this distinction is essential for both scholars and those involved in judicial appointments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds seeking judgeship (talab al-qada) to be prohibited (haram) in normal circumstances. This includes both internal desire and verbal solicitation.
The matn states 'ولا يسأل القضاء' – he should not ask for judgeship.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that some Shafi'is consider it recommended (mustahabb) for a qualified person who can uphold justice. Understand the basis of their view.
The opposing view is mentioned: 'واستحب بعض الشافعية طلبه'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response relies on the hadith 'Whoever seeks judgeship will be left to himself' and the reasoning that seeking involves reliance on self and leads to degradation of knowledge.
The commentator gives two reasons: reliance on self vs. reliance on Allah, and humiliation of knowledge.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi would not actively seek appointment, while a Shafi'i might. However, the Hanafi school allows accepting if offered without solicitation.
The passage does not explicitly allow accepting, but it is implied from the hadith about being forced/compelled.
5
Identify the exception (ta'ayyun)
When one is uniquely qualified (ta'ayyun) – no one else is fit for the role – seeking becomes obligatory (wajib) to protect Muslims' rights and prevent injustice.
The passage says: 'أما إن تعين ... وجب عليه الطلب'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يسأل القضاء لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام) من طلب القضاء وكل إلى ومن أجبر عليه نزل عليه ملك يسدده (۱) أي يلهمه رشده؛ ذكره الصدر الشهيد. ولأن من طلبه اعتمد على نفسه فيحرم ومن أجبر عليه توكل على ربه فيلهم. وعلله في السراج الوهاج بأخرى بأن في طلب القضاء إذلالاً وإهانة بالعلم لأن كل معرض مهان ا هـ . وهو يفيد منع العالم من السؤال مطلقاً لا لحاجة، وقد جمع القدوري بين النهي عن طلبه والنهي عن سؤاله ففهم الشارحون المغايرة بينهما ؛ فقيل الطلب بالقلب والسؤال باللسان؛ كذا في المستصفى. وفي الينابيع الطلب أن يقول للإمام ولني والسؤال أن يقول للناس لو ولاني الإمام قضاء بلدة كذا لأجبته إلى ذلك وهو يطمع أن يبلغ ذلك إلى الإمام ا هـ. والمراد كراهة السؤال أي تحريماً أي لا يحل كما في فتح القدير، وليس النهي عن السؤال على أطلاقه بل مقيد بأن لا يتعين للقضاء أما إن تعين بأن لم يكن أحد غيره يصلح للقضاء وجب عليه الطلب صيانة لحقوق المسلمين ودفعاً لظلم الظالمين واستحب بعض الشافعية طلبه لحامل (۱) رواه ابن ماجه في كتاب الأحكام باب ١.
He said: 'And he should not seek the position of judge because of his saying, peace be upon him: Whoever seeks the position of judge will be left to himself, and whoever is forced upon it, an angel descends upon him and guides him.' That is, it inspires him with his guidance; mentioned by al-Sadr al-Shahid. And because whoever seeks it relies on himself, so it is prohibited; and whoever is forced upon it relies on his Lord, so he is inspired. And he gave another reason in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: that in seeking the position of judge there is degradation and humiliation of knowledge because everything exposed is humiliated. End. And it indicates the absolute prohibition of a scholar asking, except out of need. And al-Quduri combined the prohibition of seeking it and the prohibition of asking about it, so the commentators understood the difference between them: it is said that seeking is with the heart and asking is with the tongue; thus in al-Mustasfa. And in al-Yanabi', seeking is to say to the imam 'Appoint me,' and asking is to say to the people, 'If the imam appoints me to the judgeship of such town, I would accept it,' hoping that this reaches the imam. End. And the intended meaning is the prohibition of asking, i.e., as a prohibition of unlawfulness; it is not permissible as in Fath al-Qadir. And the prohibition of asking is not absolute but restricted to when he is not specifically designated for judgeship; if he is designated – i.e., there is no one else fit for judgeship – then seeking becomes obligatory to protect the rights of Muslims and prevent the oppression of wrongdoers. And some Shafi'is considered it recommended for one who carries... Reported by Ibn Majah in the Book of Judgments, Chapter 1.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement 'ولا يسأل القضاء' (He should not seek the position of judge). It opens with the Prophet's hadith: 'Whoever seeks judgeship will be left to himself, and whoever is forced upon it, an angel descends upon him to guide him.' The hadith shows that seeking the post is blameworthy because it involves reliance on oneself, whereas being compelled leads to divine help. Al-Sadr al-Shahid and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj provide further reasoning: seeking judgeship degrades knowledge because exposing oneself to the public leads to humiliation. Al-Quduri distinguished between 'seeking' (طلب) internally and 'asking' (سؤال) verbally. Seeking is an inner desire; asking is verbal solicitation. Both are prohibited, but the prohibition is not absolute. It applies only when one is not uniquely qualified. If there is no one else fit for the role, then seeking becomes obligatory to protect Muslims' rights and prevent injustice. The passage notes that some Shafi'is consider seeking recommended for a qualified person. The Hanafi position is that it is prohibited (haram) in normal circumstances, but obligatory if one is specifically needed. The commentator also clarifies that the prohibition is on asking, not on accepting if offered. The hadith is referenced from Ibn Majah.

Key Terms
طلب القضاء (talab al-qada): Actively seeking the position of a judge, either by inner desire or verbal request.
السؤال (al-su'al): Verbal request for the position of judge, e.g., saying 'If the imam appoints me, I would accept.'
التعين (al-ta'ayyun): When a person is specifically designated or uniquely qualified for judgeship with no alternative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, when does seeking the position of judge become obligatory?
A) When one is knowledgeable in fiqh
B) When one is uniquely qualified and no one else is fit for the role
C) When the salary is high
D) When one is invited by the ruler

Key Takeaway
Seeking judgeship is generally prohibited, but becomes obligatory when one is uniquely qualified to protect rights and prevent injustice.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
