Additional Powers of the Judge: Protecting Property and Appointing Preachers
Continues listing judge's powers and comments on appointment of Friday preachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state two additional discretionary powers of the judge and explain the limitation on his authority to appoint a Friday preacher.

Core Idea
A judge's authority to appoint a Friday preacher is limited to authorizing replacements; initial appointment belongs to the sultan.

In this passage, Al-Bahr al-Raiq continues listing the judge's powers with two specific rulings from Al-Khaniyyah: the judge may send the property of an absent person if it is at risk, and he may take an orphan's property from a wasteful father for safekeeping. The commentator then expands on the matn's statement about Friday and Eid prayers, clarifying that the judge's authority to establish them depends on his charter, and he may only authorize a preacher replacement, not make an initial appointment. An anecdote from the Umayyad Mosque illustrates the practical tension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings from Al-Khaniyyah
Find the two specific actions a judge may take regarding property: sending absent person's property to another absent person, and taking orphan's property from a wasteful father.
These are additional powers beyond the standard jurisdiction.
2
Analyze the conditions for each ruling
For sending property, the condition is fear of destruction (khawf al-halakah). For taking orphan's property, the condition is that the father is a wasteful spender (musrif mubadhdhir).
These conditions justify the judge's intervention for protection.
3
Examine the matn statement on Friday/Eid prayers
The base matn says the judge establishes Friday and Eid prayers if they are in his charter (manshur). The commentator explains that this means he authorizes the preacher, not that he leads the prayer himself.
The judge's role is supervisory, not direct.
4
Review the commentator's expansion and anecdote
The commentator adds that in practice, the judge authorizes a replacement preacher when the incumbent dies and writes to the sultan for confirmation. He then recounts an incident in the Umayyad Mosque where a judge's action caused public doubt about the validity of the Friday prayer.
The anecdote highlights the importance of proper authorization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللقاضي أن يبعث مال الغائب إلى الغائب إذا خاف الهلاك، وله أن يأخذ مال اليتيم من والده إذا كان الوالد مسرفاً مبذراً ويضعه على يد عدل إلى أن يبلغ اليتيم؛ خانية في فصل من يقضي في المجتهدات قوله : (وأما إقامة الجمع والأعياد فيملكها القاضي إن كانت في منشورة) قلت : وفي زماننا يؤذن القاضي بنصب الخطيب إذا مات خطيب الجامع ويكتب إلى السلطنة العلية ليقرره فيها، وليس مأذوناً في نصب الخطيب ابتداء هكذا أخبرني ترجمان القاضي الحادثه اقتضت ذلك، ومقتضى هذا أنه ليس له إقامتها بنفسه ولكن كنت مرة في جامع بني أمية وقد مات الخطيب وكان نائباً عن رجل فخرج الأصيل ليخطب وكان حديث السن والقاضي حاضر في الجامع فغضب من ذلك وأنزله من المنبر وأخرج نائب القاضي فخطب بالناس وصلى وضج الناس وصاروا يتحدثون بأن هذه الجمعة لم تصح حيث لم يأذن الخطيب لنائب القاضي فلا أدري هل ذلك جهل من ذلك القاضي أو كان
And the judge has the authority to send the property of an absent person to another absent person if he fears destruction; and he has the authority to take the property of an orphan from his father if the father is a wasteful spender and place it with a trustworthy person until the orphan reaches maturity. (From al-Khaniyyah in the section on 'He Who Judges in Ijtihad Matters'). He said: 'As for establishing the Friday and Eid prayers, the judge has authority if they are in his charter.' I say: In our time, the judge authorizes the appointment of a preacher when the preacher of the congregational mosque dies, and writes to the supreme sultanate to confirm him in it; he is not authorized to appoint a preacher initially. Thus the translator of the judge informed me, the incident necessitated that. The implication of this is that he does not have the authority to establish them himself. But once I was in the Umayyad Mosque when the preacher died, and the deputy for a man came out to preach, and he was young in age, and the judge was present in the mosque. He became angry at that, removed him from the pulpit, brought out the judge's deputy, who then preached to the people and led the prayer. The people became agitated and began saying that this Friday prayer was invalid because the preacher did not authorize the judge's deputy. I do not know whether that was ignorance on the part of that judge or whether it was...
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the judge's powers with two additional rulings from al-Khaniyyah. First, the judge may send the property of an absent person to another absent person if he fears its destruction (e.g., if it is perishable). Second, he may take property from the orphan's father if the father is a wasteful spender (mubadhdhir) and place it with a trustworthy person until the orphan matures. This is to protect the orphan's inheritance. The passage then comments on the matn statement regarding Friday and Eid prayers: the judge has authority to establish them only if it is in his charter (manshur). The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, adds a practical observation: in his time, the judge does not appoint a preacher initially; rather, when a preacher dies, the judge authorizes a replacement and writes to the sultan for confirmation. This implied that the judge himself does not lead the prayers. He recounts an incident in the Umayyad Mosque where a young deputy attempted to preach, and the judge, angered, removed him and had his own deputy lead the prayer, causing public outcry about the validity of the Friday prayer. The commentator expresses uncertainty about whether the judge acted out of ignorance or had some other basis.

Key Terms
المنشور (al-manshur): The official charter or authorization given to a judge by the ruler, specifying his jurisdiction and powers.
الخطيب (al-khatib): The preacher who delivers the Friday sermon; the judge may authorize his appointment if the position becomes vacant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what action may the judge take if an orphan's father is a wasteful spender?
A) Appoint a guardian over the father
B) Take the orphan's property from the father and place it with a trustworthy person
C) Sell the father's property
D) Imprison the father

Key Takeaway
The judge's power to appoint a Friday preacher is limited to authorizing replacements; initial appointments require sultanic confirmation, and leading the prayer may also be restricted.
